Psalms
תהילים
THE JPS TANAKH: Gender-Sensitive Edition
https://jps.org/books/the-jps-tanakh-gender-sensitive-edition/

Psalms



Chapter 1

<span class="poetry indentAll">Happy is the one who has not followed the counsel of the wicked,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">or taken the path of sinners,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">or joined the company of the insolent;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">rather, this one delights in G<small>OD</small>’s teaching,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and studies<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>studies </b>Or “recites”; lit. “utters.”</i> that teaching day and night.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Such a one is like a tree planted beside streams of water,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">which yields its fruit in season,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">whose foliage never fades,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and whatever it produces thrives.<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>it produces thrives </b>Or “he does prospers.”</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Not so the wicked;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">rather, they are like chaff that wind blows away.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Therefore the wicked will not survive judgment,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">nor will sinners, in the assembly of the righteous.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For G<small>OD</small> cherishes the way of the righteous,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">but the way of the wicked is doomed.</span>

Chapter 2

<span class="poetry indentAll">Why do nations assemble,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and peoples plot<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>plot </b>Lit. “utter.”</i> vain things;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">kings of the earth take their stand,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and regents intrigue together</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">against the one anointed by G<small>OD</small>?<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>against the one anointed by G<small>OD</small> </b>Lit. “against G<small>OD</small> and against His anointed one.”</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">“Let us break the cords of their yoke,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">shake off their ropes from us!”</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">The One who is enthroned in heaven laughs;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my Sovereign mocks at them.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Then [God] speaks to them in anger,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">terrifying them with divine rage,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">“But I have installed My king</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">on Zion, My holy mountain!”</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Let me tell of the decree:</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble"> 
G<small>OD</small>
 said to me,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">“You are My son,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I have fathered you this day.<sup class="footnote-marker">c</sup><i class="footnote"><b>You are My son, / I have fathered you this day </b>I.e., G<small>OD</small> agrees to provide the king with what fathers in the ancient Near East normally provide sons: ongoing protection and aid, in return for accountability. Compare <a class="refLink" data-ref="II Samuel 7:14" href="II_Samuel.7.14">2 Sam. 7.14</a> and <a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 89:27" href="Psalms.89.27">Ps. 89.27ff</a>.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Ask it of Me,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and I will make the nations your domain;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">your estate, the limits of the earth.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You can smash them with an iron mace,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">shatter them like potter’s ware.”</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">So now, O kings, be prudent;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">accept discipline, you rulers of the earth!</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Serve G<small>OD</small> in awe;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">tremble with fright,<sup class="footnote-marker">d</sup><i class="footnote"><b>tremble with fright </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain; in contrast to others “rejoice with trembling.”</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">pay homage in good faith,<sup class="footnote-marker">e</sup><i class="footnote"><b>pay homage in good faith </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">lest [God] be angered, and your way be doomed</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">in the mere flash of divine anger.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Happy are all who take refuge in [God].</span>

Chapter 3

A psalm of David when he fled from his son Absalom.
<span class="poetry indentAll">O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, my foes are so many!</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Many are those who attack me;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">many say of me,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">“There is no deliverance for him through God.” <i>   Selah.</i><sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>Selah </b>A liturgical direction of uncertain meaning.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">But You, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, are a shield about me,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my glory, who holds my head high.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I cry aloud to G<small>OD</small>,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who answers me from the holy mountain. <i>   Selah.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I lie down and sleep and wake again,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for G<small>OD</small> sustains me.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I have no fear of the myriad forces</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">arrayed against me on every side.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Rise, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One!</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Deliver me, O my God!</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">For You slap all my enemies in the face;<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>face </b>Lit. “cheek.”</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You break the teeth of the wicked.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Deliverance is G<small>OD</small>’s;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Your blessing be upon Your people! <i>   Selah.</i> </span>

Chapter 4

For the leader; with instrumental music.<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>For the leader; with instrumental music </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> A psalm of David.
<span class="poetry indentAll">Answer me when I call,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">O God, my vindicator!</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">You freed me from distress;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">have mercy on me and hear my prayer.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You who side against me,<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>who side against me </b>Or “high and mighty ones,” or “people”; force of Heb. uncertain.</i> how long will my glory be mocked,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">will you love illusions,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">have recourse to frauds? <i>   Selah.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Know that G<small>OD</small> keeps the faithful close;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble"> 
G<small>OD</small>
 hears when I call out.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">So tremble, and sin no more;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">ponder it on your bed, and sigh.<sup class="footnote-marker">c</sup><i class="footnote"><b>sigh </b>In contrast to others “be still.”</i> <i>   Selah.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Offer sacrifices in righteousness</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and trust in G<small>OD</small>.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Many say, “O for good days!”</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Bestow Your favor on us,<sup class="footnote-marker">d</sup><i class="footnote"><b>Bestow Your favor on us </b>Lit. “Lift up the light of Your countenance upon us”; cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Numbers 6:25-26" href="Numbers.6.25-26">Num. 6.25–26</a>.</i> O E<small>TERNAL</small> One.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You put joy into my heart</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">when their grain and wine show increase.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Safe and sound, I lie down and sleep,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for You alone, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, keep me secure.<sup class="footnote-marker">e</sup><i class="footnote"><b>for You alone, O <small>ETERNAL ONE</small>, keep me secure </b>Or “for You, O <small>ETERNAL ONE</small>, keep me alone and secure.”</i> </span>

Chapter 5

For the leader; on <i>neḥiloth</i>.<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>For the leader; on <i>neḥiloth</i> </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> A psalm of David.
<span class="poetry indentAll">Give ear to my speech, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">consider my utterance.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Heed the sound of my cry,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my Sovereign and God,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for I pray to You.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Hear my voice, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, at daybreak;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">at daybreak I plead before You, and wait.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For You are not a God who desires wickedness;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">evil cannot abide with You;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the wanton cannot endure in Your sight.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">You detest all evildoers;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You doom those who speak lies;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">deceitful murderers G<small>OD</small> abhors.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">But I, through Your abundant love, enter Your house;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I bow down in awe at Your holy temple.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, lead me along Your righteous [path]<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>lead me along Your righteous [path] </b>Or “as You are righteous, lead me.”</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">because of my watchful foes;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">make Your way straight before me.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For there is no sincerity on their lips;<sup class="footnote-marker">c</sup><i class="footnote"><b>lips </b>Lit. “mouth.”</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">their heart is [filled with] malice;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">their throat is an open grave;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">their tongue slippery.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Condemn them, O God;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">let them fall by their own devices;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">cast them out for their many crimes,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for they defy You.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">But let all who take refuge in You rejoice,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">ever jubilant as You shelter them;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and let those who love Your name exult in You.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For You surely bless the righteous, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">encompassing them with favor like a shield.</span>

Chapter 6

For the leader; with instrumental music on the <i>sheminith</i>.<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>For the leader; with instrumental music on the <i>sheminith</i> </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> A psalm of David.
<span class="poetry indentAll">O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, do not punish me in anger,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">do not chastise me in fury.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Have mercy on me, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, for I languish;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">heal me, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, for my bones shake with terror.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">My whole being is stricken with terror,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">while You, E<small>TERNAL</small> One—O, how long!</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, turn! Rescue me!</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Deliver me as befits Your faithfulness.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For there is no praise of You among the dead;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">in Sheol, who can acclaim You?</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I am weary with groaning;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">every night I drench my bed,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I melt my couch in tears.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">My eyes are wasted by vexation,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">worn out because of all my foes.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Away from me, all you evildoers,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for G<small>OD</small> heeds the sound of my weeping.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">
G<small>OD</small>
 heeds my plea,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble"> 
G<small>OD</small>
 accepts my prayer.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">All my enemies will be frustrated and stricken with terror;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they will turn back in an instant, frustrated.</span>

Chapter 7

<i>Shiggaion</i> of David,<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b><i>Shiggaion</i> of David </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> which he sang to G<small>OD</small>, concerning Cush, a Benjaminite.
<span class="poetry indentAll">O my E<small>TERNAL</small> God, in You I seek refuge;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">deliver me from all my pursuers and save me,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">lest, like a lion, they tear me apart,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">rending in pieces, and no one save me.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">O my E<small>TERNAL</small> God, if I have done such things,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">if my hands bear the guilt of wrongdoing,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">if I have dealt evil to my ally—</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I who rescued my foe without reward<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>I who rescued my foe without reward </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain; in contrast to others “or stripped my foe clean.”</i>—</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">then let the enemy pursue and overtake me;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">let my life be trampled to the ground,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and my body dwell in the dust. <i>   Selah.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Rise, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, in Your anger;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">assert Yourself against the fury of my foes;<sup class="footnote-marker">c</sup><i class="footnote"><b>against the fury of my foes </b>Or “in Your fury against my foes.”</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">bestir Yourself in my behalf;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You have ordained judgment.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll"><sup class="footnote-marker">d</sup><i class="footnote">Meaning of verse uncertain.</i> Let the assembly of peoples gather about You,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">with You enthroned above, on high.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">
G<small>OD</small>
 judges the peoples;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">vindicate me, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for the righteousness and blamelessness that are mine.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Let the evil of the wicked come to an end,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">but establish the righteous;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the One who probes the mind and conscience<sup class="footnote-marker">e</sup><i class="footnote"><b>conscience </b>Lit. “kidneys.”</i> is God the Righteous.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I look to God to shield me;<sup class="footnote-marker">f</sup><i class="footnote"><b>I look to God to shield me </b>Cf. Ibn Ezra and Kimhi; lit. “My Shield is upon God.”</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the deliverer of the upright.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">God vindicates the righteous;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">God pronounces doom<sup class="footnote-marker">g</sup><i class="footnote"><b>pronounces doom </b>In contrast to others “has indignation.”</i> each day.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">If someone [wicked] does not turn back, but whets his sword,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">bends his bow and aims it,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">then against himself he readies deadly weapons,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and makes his arrows sharp.<sup class="footnote-marker">h</sup><i class="footnote">Meaning of these verses uncertain. Or, with God as the main subject: “If one does not turn back, [God] whets a sword, / bends a bow and aims it— / <sup>14</sup>preparing deadly weapons for him, / and making the arrows sharp.”</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">See, he hatches evil, conceives mischief,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and gives birth to fraud.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">He has dug a pit and deepened it,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and will fall into the trap he made.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">His mischief will recoil upon his own head;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">his lawlessness will come down upon his skull.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I will praise G<small>OD</small> for being righteous,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and sing a hymn to the name of G<small>OD</small> Most High.</span>

Chapter 8

For the leader; on the <i>gittith</i>.<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>For the leader; on the <i>gittith</i> </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> A psalm of David.
<span class="poetry indentAll">O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, our Sovereign,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">how majestic is Your name throughout the earth—</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You who have covered the heavens with Your splendor!<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>You who have covered the heavens with Your splendor </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain; or “You whose splendor is celebrated all over the heavens!”</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll"><sup class="footnote-marker">c</sup><i class="footnote">Meaning of verse uncertain.</i> From the mouths of infants and sucklings</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You have founded strength on account of Your foes,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">to put an end to enemy and avenger.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">When I behold Your heavens, the work of Your fingers,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the moon and stars that You set in place,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">what are human beings that You have been mindful of them,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">mortals that You have taken note of them,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">that You have made them little less than divine,<sup class="footnote-marker">d</sup><i class="footnote"><b>divine </b>Or “the angels.”</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and adorned them with glory and majesty?</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You have made them master over Your handiwork,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">laying the world at their feet—</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">sheep and oxen, all of them,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and wild beasts, too;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the birds of the heavens, the fish of the sea,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">whatever travels the paths of the seas.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, our Sovereign, how majestic is Your name throughout the earth!</span>

Chapter 9

For the leader; <i>ʻalmuth labben</i>.<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>For the leader; <i>ʻalmuth labben</i> </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain; some mss. and ancient versions, <i>ʻal muth labben</i>, as though “over the death of the son.”</i> A psalm of David.
<span class="poetry indentAll">I will praise You, E<small>TERNAL</small> One, with all my heart;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I will tell all Your wonders.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I will rejoice and exult in You,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">singing a hymn to Your name, O Most High.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">When my enemies retreat,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they stumble to their doom at Your presence.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For You uphold my right and claim,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">enthroned as righteous judge.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You blast the nations;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You destroy the wicked;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You blot out their name forever.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll"><sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote">Meaning of verse uncertain.</i> The enemy is no more—</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">ruins everlasting;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You have torn down their cities;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">their very names are lost.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">But G<small>OD</small>, whose throne is set up for judgment, abides forever;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">it is [God] who judges the world with righteousness,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">rules the peoples with equity.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">
G<small>OD</small>
 is a haven for the oppressed,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">a haven in times of trouble.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Those who know Your name trust You,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for You do not abandon those who turn to You, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Sing a hymn to the E<small>TERNAL</small>, who reigns in Zion;<sup class="footnote-marker">c</sup><i class="footnote"><b>who reigns in Zion </b>Or “O You who dwell in Zion.”</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">declare God’s deeds among the peoples.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For [God] does not ignore the cry of the afflicted;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the One who requites bloodshed is mindful of them.<sup class="footnote-marker">d</sup><i class="footnote">Clauses transposed for clarity.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Have mercy on me, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">see my affliction at the hands of my foes,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You who lift me from the gates of death,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">so that in the gates of Fair Zion<sup class="footnote-marker">e</sup><i class="footnote"><b>Fair Zion </b>Lit. “the Daughter of Zion.”</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I might tell all Your praise,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I might exult in Your deliverance.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">The nations sink in the pit they have made;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">their own foot is caught in the net they have hidden.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">
G<small>OD</small>
 is known,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">having worked judgment;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the wicked are snared by their own devices. <i>Higgaion</i>.<sup class="footnote-marker">f</sup><i class="footnote"><b><i>Higgaion</i> </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> <i>   Selah.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Let the wicked be<sup class="footnote-marker">g</sup><i class="footnote"><b>be </b>In contrast to others “return to.”</i> in Sheol,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">all the nations who ignore God!</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Not always shall the needy be ignored,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">nor the hope of the afflicted forever lost.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Rise, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One!</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Let not mortals have power;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">let the nations be judged in Your presence.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Strike fear into them,<sup class="footnote-marker">h</sup><i class="footnote"><b>Strike fear into them </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> O E<small>TERNAL</small> One;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">let the nations know they are only mortals. <i>   Selah.</i> </span>

Chapter 10

<span class="poetry indentAll">Why, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, do You stand aloof,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">heedless in times of trouble?</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">The wicked in their arrogance hound the lowly—</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">may they be caught in the schemes they devise!<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>may they be caught in the schemes they devise </b>Or “they (i.e., the lowly) are caught by the schemes they devised.”</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">The wicked crow about their unbridled lusts;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the grasping revile and scorn G<small>OD</small>.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">The wicked, arrogant as they are,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">in all their scheming [think],<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>The wicked crow … their scheming [think] </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">“God does not care<sup class="footnote-marker">c</sup><i class="footnote"><b>God does not care </b>Lit. “There is no God.”</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and does not call to account.”<sup class="footnote-marker">d</sup><i class="footnote">Clauses transposed for clarity.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Their ways prosper at all times;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Your judgments are far beyond them;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they snort at all their foes.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Such people think, “I shall not be shaken,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">through all time never be in trouble.”</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Their mouth is full of oaths, deceit, and fraud;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">mischief and evil are under their tongue.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They lurk in outlying places;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">from a covert they slay the innocent;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">their eyes spy out the hapless.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They wait in a covert like a lion in a lair;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">wait to seize the lowly;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they seize the lowly as they pull their net shut;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they stoop, they crouch,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and the hapless fall prey to their might.<sup class="footnote-marker">e</sup><i class="footnote"><b>and the hapless fall prey to their might </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They think, “God is not mindful,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the divine face is hidden and never looks.”</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Rise, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One!</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Strike at them,<sup class="footnote-marker">f</sup><i class="footnote"><b>Strike at them </b>Lit. “Lift Your hand.”</i> O God!</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Do not forget the lowly.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Why should the wicked scorn God,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">thinking You do not call to account?</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You do look!</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">You take note of mischief and vexation!</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">To requite is in Your power.<sup class="footnote-marker">g</sup><i class="footnote"><b>To requite is in Your power </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">To You the hapless can entrust themselves;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You have ever been the orphans’ help.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">O break the power of the wicked and evildoers,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">so that when You look for<sup class="footnote-marker">h</sup><i class="footnote"><b>look for </b>A play on <i>darash</i>, which in vv. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 10:4" href="Psalms.10.4">4</a> and <a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 10:13" href="Psalms.10.13">13</a> means “to call to account.”</i> their wickedness</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You will find it no more.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">
G<small>OD</small>
 is sovereign for ever and ever;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the nations will perish from this<sup class="footnote-marker">i</sup><i class="footnote"><b>this </b>Heb. “His.”</i> land.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You will listen to the entreaty of the lowly, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You will make their hearts firm;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You will incline Your ear</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">to champion the orphan and the downtrodden,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">that mere earthly mortals tyrannize no more.<sup class="footnote-marker">j</sup><i class="footnote"><b>that mere earthly mortals tyrannize no more </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span>

Chapter 11

For the leader. Of David.<br><span class="poetry indentAll">In G<small>OD</small> I take refuge;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">how can you say to me,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">“Take to the hills like a bird!<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>the hills like a bird </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain; lit. “your hill, bird!”</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For see, the wicked bend the bow,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they set their arrow on the string</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">to shoot from the shadows at the upright.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">When the foundations are destroyed,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">what can the righteous do?”<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>When the foundations are destroyed, / what can the righteous do? </b>Or “For the foundations are destroyed; what has the Righteous One done?” Or “If the foundations are destroyed, what have the righteous accomplished?”</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">
G<small>OD</small>
 is in the divine palace;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble"> 
G<small>OD</small>—whose throne is in heaven,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">whose eyes behold, whose gaze searches humankind.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">
G<small>OD</small>
 seeks out someone righteous,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">but loathes the wicked one who loves injustice.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">[God] will rain down upon the wicked blazing coals and sulfur;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">a scorching wind shall be their lot.<sup class="footnote-marker">c</sup><i class="footnote"><b>their lot </b>Lit. “the portion of their cup.”</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For G<small>OD</small> is righteous,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and loves righteous deeds;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the upright shall behold God’s face.</span>

Chapter 12

For the leader; on the <i>sheminith</i>. A psalm of David.
<span class="poetry indentAll">Help, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One!</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">For the faithful are no more;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the loyal have vanished from among mortals.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">People speak lies to one another;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">their speech is smooth;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they talk with duplicity.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">May G<small>OD</small> cut off all flattering lips,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">every tongue that speaks arrogance.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They say, “By our tongues we shall prevail;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">with lips such as ours, who can be our master?”</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">“Because of the groans of the plundered poor and needy,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I will now act,” says G<small>OD</small>.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">“I will give help,” [God] affirms to them.<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>“I will give help,” [God] affirms to them </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">
G<small>OD</small>’s words are pure words,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">silver purged in an earthen crucible,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">refined sevenfold.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, will keep them,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">guarding each from this age<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>from this age </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> evermore.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">On every side the wicked roam</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">when baseness is exalted among mortals.<sup class="footnote-marker">c</sup><i class="footnote"><b>when baseness is exalted among mortals </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span>

Chapter 13

For the leader. A psalm of David.
<span class="poetry indentAll">How long, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One; will You ignore me forever?</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">How long will You hide Your face from me?</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">How long will I have cares on my mind,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">grief in my heart all day?</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">How long will my enemy have the upper hand?</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Look at me, answer me, O my E<small>TERNAL</small> God!</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Restore the luster to my eyes,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">lest I sleep the sleep of death;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">lest my enemy say, “I have overcome him,”</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my foes exult when I totter.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">But I trust in Your faithfulness,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my heart will exult in Your deliverance.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">I will sing to G<small>OD</small>,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who has been good to me.</span>

Chapter 14

<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote">Cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 53:1" href="Psalms.53.1">Psalm 53</a>.</i> For the leader. Of David.<br><span class="poetry indentAll">The scoundrel thinks,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">“God does not care.”<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>God does not care </b>Lit. “There is no God”; cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 10:4" href="Psalms.10.4">10.4</a>.</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Human<sup class="footnote-marker">c</sup><i class="footnote"><b>Human </b>Heb. “Their.”</i> deeds are corrupt and loathsome;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">no one does good.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">
G<small>OD</small>
 looks down from heaven on humankind</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">to find someone with understanding,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">someone mindful of God.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">All have turned bad,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">altogether foul;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">there is no one who does good,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">not even one.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Are they so witless, all those evildoers,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who devour my people as they devour food,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and do not invoke G<small>OD</small>?</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">There they will be seized with fright,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for God is present in the circle of the righteous.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You may set at naught the counsel of the lowly,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">but G<small>OD</small> is their refuge.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">O that the deliverance of Israel might come from Zion!</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">When G<small>OD</small> restores the fortunes of this covenanted people,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Jacob will exult, Israel will rejoice.</span>

Chapter 15

A psalm of David.<br><span class="poetry indentAll"> 
G<small>OD</small>, who may sojourn in Your tent,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who may dwell on Your holy mountain?</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Anyone who lives without blame,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who does what is right,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and in their heart acknowledges the truth;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">whose tongue is not given to evil;<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>whose tongue is not given to evil </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain; or “who has no slander upon the tongue.”</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who has never done harm to a compatriot,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">or borne reproach for [acts toward] a neighbor;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for whom someone contemptible is abhorrent,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">but who honors those who fear G<small>OD</small>;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who keeps an oath even when it hurts;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who has never lent money at interest,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">or accepted a bribe against the innocent.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">One who acts thus shall never be shaken.</span>

Chapter 16

A <i>michtam</i><sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b><i>michtam</i> </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> of David.<br><span class="poetry indentAll">Protect me, O God, for I seek refuge in You.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I say to G<small>OD</small>,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">“You are my Sovereign, my benefactor;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">there is none above You.”<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>my benefactor; / there is none above You </b>In contrast to others “I have no good but in You.”</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">As to the holy and mighty ones that are in the land,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my whole desire concerning them is that</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">those who espouse another [god]</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">may have many sorrows!<sup class="footnote-marker">c</sup><i class="footnote"><b>As to the holy and mighty ones … sorrows </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain; “holy and mighty ones” taken as epithets for divine beings; cf. <i>qedoshim</i> in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 89:6" href="Psalms.89.6">Ps. 89.6</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 89:8" href="Psalms.89.8">8</a>, and <i>ʼaddirim</i> in <a class="refLink" data-ref="I Samuel 4:8" href="I_Samuel.4.8">1 Sam. 4.8</a>.</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">I will have no part of their bloody libations;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">their names will not pass my lips.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">
G<small>OD</small>
 is my allotted share and portion;<sup class="footnote-marker">d</sup><i class="footnote"><b>portion </b>Lit. “cup.”</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You control my fate.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Delightful country has fallen to my lot;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">lovely indeed is my estate.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I bless G<small>OD</small> who has guided me;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my conscience<sup class="footnote-marker">e</sup><i class="footnote"><b>conscience </b>Lit. “kidneys.”</i> admonishes me at night.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I am ever mindful of G<small>OD</small>’s presence—</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who is at my right hand; I shall never be shaken.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">So my heart rejoices,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my whole being exults,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and my body rests secure.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For You will not abandon me to Sheol,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">or let Your faithful one see the Pit.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You will teach me the path of life.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">In Your presence is perfect joy;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">delights are ever in Your right hand.</span>

Chapter 17

A prayer of David.<br><span class="poetry indentAll">Hear, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, what is just;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">heed my cry, give ear to my prayer,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">uttered without guile.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">My vindication will come from You;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Your eyes will behold what is right.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You have visited me at night, probed my mind,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You have tested me and found nothing amiss;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I determined that my mouth should not transgress.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">As for mortals’ dealings,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">in accord with the command of Your lips,<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>I determined … lips </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I have kept in view the fate<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>fate </b>Cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Proverbs 1:19" href="Proverbs.1.19">Prov. 1.19</a>; lit. “paths.”</i> of the lawless.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">My feet have held to Your paths;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my legs have not given way.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I call on You;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You will answer me, God;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">turn Your ear to me,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">hear what I say.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Display Your faithfulness in wondrous deeds,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You who deliver with Your right hand</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">those who seek refuge from assailants.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Guard me like the apple of Your eye;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">hide me in the shadow of Your wings</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">from the wicked who despoil me,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my mortal enemies who<sup class="footnote-marker">c</sup><i class="footnote"><b>my mortal enemies who </b>Or “from my enemies who avidly.”</i> encircle me.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Their hearts are closed to pity;<sup class="footnote-marker">d</sup><i class="footnote"><b>Their hearts are closed to pity </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they mouth arrogance;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">now they hem in our feet on every side;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they set their eyes roaming over the land.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They are<sup class="footnote-marker">e</sup><i class="footnote"><b>They are </b>Heb. “He is.”</i> like a lion eager for prey,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">a king of beasts lying in wait.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Rise, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One! Go forth to meet my enemies.<sup class="footnote-marker">f</sup><i class="footnote"><b>my enemies </b>Heb. “him.”</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Bring them down;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">rescue me from the wicked with Your sword,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">from mortals, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, with Your hand,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">from mortals whose share in life is fleeting.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">But as to Your treasured ones,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">fill their bellies.<sup class="footnote-marker">g</sup><i class="footnote"><b>from mortals, O <small>ETERNAL ONE</small>, … fill their bellies </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Their children too shall be satisfied,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and have something to leave over for their young.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Then I, justified, will behold Your face;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">awake, I am filled with the vision of You.</span>

Chapter 18

<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote">This poem occurs again at <a class="refLink" data-ref="II Samuel 22" href="II_Samuel.22">2 Sam. 22</a>, with a number of variations, some of which are cited in the following notes.</i> For the leader. Of David, the servant of G<small>OD</small>, who addressed the words of this song to G<small>OD</small> after G<small>OD</small> had saved him from the hands of all his enemies and from the clutches of Saul.
<span class="poetry indentAll">He said:</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I adore you, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, my strength,<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>I adore you, O <small>ETERNAL ONE</small>, my strength </b>Not in <a class="refLink" data-ref="II Samuel 22:2" href="II_Samuel.22.2">2 Sam. 22.2</a>.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, my crag, my fortress, my deliverer,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my God, my rock in which I take shelter,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my shield, my mighty champion,<sup class="footnote-marker">c</sup><i class="footnote"><b>mighty champion </b>Lit. “horn of rescue.”</i> my haven.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">All praise! I called on G<small>OD</small><sup class="footnote-marker">d</sup><i class="footnote"><b>All praise! I called on G<small>OD</small> </b>Construction of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and was delivered from my enemies.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Ropes<sup class="footnote-marker">e</sup><i class="footnote"><b>Ropes </b>Cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="II Samuel 22:5" href="II_Samuel.22.5">2 Sam. 22.5</a> “breakers.”</i> of Death encompassed me;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">torrents of Belial<sup class="footnote-marker">f</sup><i class="footnote"><b>Belial </b>I.e., the netherworld, like “Death” and “Sheol.”</i> terrified me;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">ropes of Sheol encircled me;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">snares of Death confronted me.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">In my anguish I called on the E<small>TERNAL</small>,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">cried out to my God,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who from a heavenly abode<sup class="footnote-marker">g</sup><i class="footnote"><b>a heavenly abode </b>Lit. “His temple”; cf. v. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 18:10" href="Psalms.18.10">10</a>.</i> heard my voice,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">whose ears received my cry.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Then the earth rocked and quaked;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the foundations of the mountains shook—</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">rocked by divine indignation;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">smoke went up from God’s nostrils,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">devouring fire from God’s mouth—</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">live coals blazing forth.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">[God] bent the sky and came down,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">thick cloud beneath divine feet.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">[God] mounted a cherub and flew,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">gliding on the wings of the wind.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">[God] made darkness a screen—</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">pavilions of dark thunderheads,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">dense clouds of the sky all around.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">In the divine brilliance,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">hail and fiery coals pierced those clouds.<sup class="footnote-marker">h</sup><i class="footnote"><b>pierced those clouds </b>Cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="II Samuel 22:13" href="II_Samuel.22.13">2 Sam. 22.13</a> “blazed.”</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Then G<small>OD</small> thundered from heaven,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the Most High gave forth voice—</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">hail and fiery coals<sup class="footnote-marker">i</sup><i class="footnote"><b>hail and fiery coals </b>Not in <a class="refLink" data-ref="II Samuel 22:14" href="II_Samuel.22.14">2 Sam. 22.14</a>.</i>—</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">letting shafts fly, and scattering them;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">discharging lightning, and routing them.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">The ocean bed was exposed;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the foundations of the world were laid bare</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">by Your mighty roaring, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">at the blast of Your breath.<sup class="footnote-marker">j</sup><i class="footnote"><b>Your breath </b>Lit. “the breath of Your nostrils.”</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Reaching down from on high, [God] took me,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">drawing me out of the mighty waters—</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">rescuing me from my fierce enemy,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">from foes too strong for me.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They confronted me on the day of my calamity,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">but G<small>OD</small> was my support—</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">bringing me out to freedom,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">pleased with me enough to rescue me.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">
G<small>OD</small>
 rewarded me according to my merit—</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">requiting the cleanness of my hands—</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for I have kept to the ways of G<small>OD</small> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and have not been guilty before my God;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for I am mindful of all God’s rules</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and have not disregarded God’s laws.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I have been blameless toward [God],</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and have guarded myself against sinning;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and G<small>OD</small> has requited my merit,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">according to the evident cleanness of my hands.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">With the loyal, You deal loyally;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">with the blameless,<sup class="footnote-marker">k</sup><i class="footnote"><b>the blameless </b>Heb. “blameless man.”</i> blamelessly.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">With the pure, You act purely,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and with the perverse, You are wily.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">It is You who deliver lowly folk,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">but haughty eyes You humble.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">It is You who light my lamp;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my E<small>TERNAL</small> God lights up my darkness.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">With You, I can rush a barrier;<sup class="footnote-marker">l</sup><i class="footnote"><b>barrier </b>Cf. note to <a class="refLink" data-ref="II Samuel 22:30" href="II_Samuel.22.30">2 Sam. 22.30</a>; or “troop.”</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">with my God, I can scale a wall.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">The way of God is perfect;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the word of the E<small>TERNAL</small> is pure.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">[God] shields all who seek refuge.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Truly, who is a god except the E<small>TERNAL</small>,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who is a rock but our God?—</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the God who girded me with might,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who made my way secure;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who made my legs like a deer’s,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and set me firmly on the<sup class="footnote-marker">m</sup><i class="footnote"><b>the </b>Taking <i>bamothai</i> as a poetic form of <i>bamoth</i>; cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Habakkuk 3:19" href="Habakkuk.3.19">Hab. 3.19</a>; in contrast to others “my.”</i> heights;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who trained my hands for battle—</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my arms can bend a bow of bronze!</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You have granted me the shield of Your protection;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Your right hand has sustained me,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Your care<sup class="footnote-marker">n</sup><i class="footnote"><b>care </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain; in contrast to others “condescension.”</i> has made me great.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You have let me stride on freely;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my feet have not slipped.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I pursued my enemies and overtook them;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I did not turn back till I destroyed them.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I struck them down,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and they could rise no more;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they lay at my feet.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You have girded me with strength for battle,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">brought low my adversaries before me,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">made my enemies turn tail before me;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I wiped out my foes.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They cried out, but there was none to deliver;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">to G<small>OD</small>, who did not answer them.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I ground them fine as windswept dust;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I trod them flat like dirt of the streets.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You have rescued me from the strife of people;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You have set me at the head of nations;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">peoples I knew not must serve me.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">At the mere report of me they are submissive;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">foreign peoples cower before me.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Foreign peoples lose courage,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and come trembling out of their strongholds.<sup class="footnote-marker">o</sup><i class="footnote"><b>and come trembling out of their strongholds </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">
G<small>OD</small>
 lives! Blessed is my rock!</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Exalted be God, my deliverer,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the God who has vindicated me</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and made peoples subject to me,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who rescued me from my enemies,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who raised me clear of my adversaries,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">saved me from the lawless opposition!</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For this I sing Your praise among the nations, E<small>TERNAL</small> One,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and hymn Your name:</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">According great victories<sup class="footnote-marker">p</sup><i class="footnote"><b>According great victories </b>Cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="II Samuel 22:51" href="II_Samuel.22.51">2 Sam. 22.51</a>, “Tower of victory.”</i> to Your<sup class="footnote-marker">q</sup><i class="footnote"><b>Your </b>Heb. 3rd person.</i> king,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">keeping faith with Your<sup class="footnote-marker">r</sup><i class="footnote"><b>Your </b>See preceding note.</i> anointed,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">with David and his offspring evermore.</span>

Chapter 19

For the leader. A psalm of David.
<span class="poetry indentAll">The heavens declare the glory of God,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the sky proclaims God’s handiwork.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Day to day makes utterance,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">night to night speaks out.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">There is no utterance,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">there are no words,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">whose sound goes unheard.<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>whose sound goes unheard </b>With Septuagint, Symmachus, and Vulgate; or “their sound is not heard.”</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Their<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>Their </b>Namely, of the heavens.</i> voice<sup class="footnote-marker">c</sup><i class="footnote"><b>voice </b>Cf. Septuagint, Symmachus, and Vulgate; Arabic <i>qawwah</i>, “to shout.”</i> carries throughout the earth,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">their words to the end of the world.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">[God] placed in them a tent for the sun,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who is like a groom coming forth from the chamber,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">like a hero, eager to run his course.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">His rising-place is at one end of heaven,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and his circuit reaches the other;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">nothing escapes his heat.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">The teaching of G<small>OD</small> is perfect,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">renewing life;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the decrees of G<small>OD</small> are enduring,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">making the simple wise,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">The precepts of G<small>OD</small> are just,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">rejoicing the heart;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the instruction of G<small>OD</small> is lucid,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">making the eyes light up.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">The fear of G<small>OD</small> is pure,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">abiding forever;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the judgments of G<small>OD</small> are true,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">righteous altogether,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">more desirable than gold,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">than much fine gold;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">sweeter than honey,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">than drippings of the comb.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Your servant pays them heed;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">in obeying them there is much reward.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Who can be aware of errors?</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Clear me of unperceived guilt,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and from willful sins<sup class="footnote-marker">d</sup><i class="footnote"><b>willful sins </b>Or “the arrogant”; cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 119:51" href="Psalms.119.51">119.51</a>.</i> keep Your servant;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">let them not dominate me;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">then shall I be blameless</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and clear of grave offense.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">May the words of my mouth</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and the prayer of my heart<sup class="footnote-marker">e</sup><i class="footnote"><b>heart </b>For <i>leb</i> as a source of speech, see note to <a class="refLink" data-ref="Ecclesiastes 5:1" href="Ecclesiastes.5.1">Eccl. 5.1</a>.</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">be acceptable to You,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, my rock and my redeemer.</span>

Chapter 20

For the leader. A psalm of David.
<span class="poetry indentAll">May G<small>OD</small> answer you in time of trouble,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the name of Jacob’s God keep you safe—</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">sending you help from the sanctuary,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and sustaining you from Zion.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">May [God] receive the tokens<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>receive the tokens </b>Cf. <i>ʼazkarah</i>, “token portion” of grain offering; <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 2:2" href="Leviticus.2.2">Lev. 2.2</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 2:9" href="Leviticus.2.9">9</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 2:16" href="Leviticus.2.16">16</a>, etc.</i> of all your grain offerings,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and approve<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>approve </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> your burnt offerings. <i>   Selah.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">May your desire be granted,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">your every plan fulfilled.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">May we shout for joy in your victory,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">arrayed by standards in the name of our God.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">May G<small>OD</small> fulfill your every wish.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Now I know that G<small>OD</small> will give victory to our anointed one,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">will answer him from the heavenly sanctuary</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">with the mighty victories of God’s right arm.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They [call] on chariots, they [call] on horses,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">but we call on the name of the E<small>TERNAL</small> our God.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They collapse and lie fallen,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">but we rally and gather strength.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, grant victory to the king;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">may [God] answer us when we call.<sup class="footnote-marker">c</sup><i class="footnote"><b>O <small>ETERNAL ONE</small>, grant victory to the king; / may [God] answer us when we call </b>Or “O <small>ETERNAL ONE</small>, grant victory! / May the King answer us when we call,” depicting G<small>OD</small> as the figure who leads the (divine) army into battle.</i> </span>

Chapter 21

For the leader. A psalm of David.
<span class="poetry indentAll">O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, the king rejoices in Your strength;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">how greatly he exults in Your victory!</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You have granted him the desire of his heart,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">have not denied the request of his lips. <i>   Selah.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You have proffered him blessings of good things,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">have set upon his head a crown of fine gold.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">He asked You for life; You granted it;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">a long life, everlasting.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Great is his glory through Your victory;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You have endowed him with splendor and majesty.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You have made him blessed forever,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">gladdened him with the joy of Your presence.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For the king trusts in G<small>OD</small>;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">through the faithfulness of the Most High</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">he will not be shaken.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Your hand is equal to all Your enemies;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Your right hand overpowers Your foes.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You set them ablaze like a furnace</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">when You show Your presence.<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>when You show Your presence </b>Or “at the time of Your anger.”</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">
G<small>OD</small>
 in anger destroys them;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">fire consumes them.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You wipe their offspring from the earth,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">their issue from among humankind.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For they schemed against You;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they laid plans,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">but could not succeed.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For You make them turn back<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>For You make them turn back </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">by Your bows aimed at their face.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Be exalted, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, through Your strength;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">we will sing and chant the praises of Your mighty deeds.</span>

Chapter 22

For the leader; on <i>ayyeleth ha-shaḥar</i>.<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b><i>ayyeleth ha-shaḥar</i> </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> A psalm of David.
<span class="poetry indentAll">My God, my God,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">why have You abandoned me;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">why so far from delivering me</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and from my anguished roaring?</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">My God,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I cry by day—You answer not;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">by night, and have no respite.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">But You are the Holy One,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">enthroned,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the Praise of Israel.<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>But You are the Holy One, / enthroned, / the Praise of Israel </b>Or “But You are holy, enthroned upon the praises of Israel.”</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">In You our ancestors trusted;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they trusted, and You rescued them.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">To You they cried out</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and they escaped;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">in You they trusted</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and were not disappointed.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">But I am a worm, less than human;<sup class="footnote-marker">c</sup><i class="footnote"><b>less than human </b>Or “inconsequential.”</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">scorned by everyone, despised by people.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">All who see me mock me;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they curl their lips,<sup class="footnote-marker">d</sup><i class="footnote"><b>they curl their lips </b>Lit. “they open wide with a lip.”</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they shake their heads.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">“Let him commit himself to G<small>OD</small>;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">let [God] rescue him,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">let [God] save him,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for [God] is pleased with him.”</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You drew me<sup class="footnote-marker">e</sup><i class="footnote"><b>drew me </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> from the womb,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">made me secure at my mother’s breast.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I became Your charge at birth;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">from my mother’s womb You have been my God.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Do not be far from me,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for trouble is near,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and there is none to help.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Many bulls surround me,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">mighty ones of Bashan encircle me.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They open their mouths at me</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">like tearing, roaring lions.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">My life ebbs away:<sup class="footnote-marker">f</sup><i class="footnote"><b>My life ebbs away </b>Lit. “I am poured out like water.”</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">all my bones are disjointed;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my heart is like wax,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">melting within me;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my vigor dries up like a shard;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my tongue cleaves to my palate;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You commit me to the dust of death.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Dogs surround me;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">a pack of evil ones closes in on me,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">like lions [they maul] my hands and feet.<sup class="footnote-marker">g</sup><i class="footnote"><b>like lions [they maul] my hands and feet </b>With Rashi; cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Isaiah 38:13" href="Isaiah.38.13">Isa. 38.13</a>.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I take the count of all my bones</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">while they look on and gloat.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They divide my clothes among themselves,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">casting lots for my garments.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">But You, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, be not far off;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my strength, hasten to my aid.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Save my life from the sword,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my precious life<sup class="footnote-marker">h</sup><i class="footnote"><b>precious life </b>Lit. “only one.”</i> from the clutches of a dog.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Deliver me from a lion’s mouth;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">from the horns of wild oxen rescue<sup class="footnote-marker">i</sup><i class="footnote"><b>rescue </b>Lit. “answer.”</i> me.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Then will I proclaim Your fame to my kin,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">praise You in the congregation.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You who fear G<small>OD</small>, give praise!</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">All you offspring of Jacob, show honor!</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Be in dread, all you offspring of Israel!</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For [God] did not scorn, and did not spurn,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the plea<sup class="footnote-marker">j</sup><i class="footnote"><b>plea </b>Or “plight.”</i> of anyone lowly;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">[God] did not turn away<sup class="footnote-marker">k</sup><i class="footnote"><b>turn away </b>Lit. “hide His face.”</i> from them;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">when they cried out, [God] listened.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Because of You I offer praise<sup class="footnote-marker">l</sup><i class="footnote"><b>Because of You I offer praise </b>Lit. “From You is my praise.”</i> in the great congregation;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I pay my vows in the presence of God’s worshipers.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Let the lowly eat and be satisfied;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">let all who seek G<small>OD</small> give praise.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Always be of good cheer!</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Let all the ends of the earth pay heed and turn to G<small>OD</small>,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and the peoples of all nations prostrate themselves before You;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for sovereignty is G<small>OD</small>’s,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who rules the nations.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll"><sup class="footnote-marker">m</sup><i class="footnote">Meaning of verse uncertain; in contrast to others “All the fat ones of the earth shall eat and worship; / All they that go down to the dust shall kneel before Him, / Even he that cannot keep his soul alive.”</i> All those in full vigor shall eat and prostrate themselves;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">all those at death’s door, whose spirits flag,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">shall bend the knee in submission.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Offspring shall serve [God];</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the Sovereign’s fame shall be proclaimed to the generation </span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">to come;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they shall tell of the beneficence to people yet to be born,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for [God] has acted.</span>

Chapter 23

A psalm of David.<br><span class="poetry indentAll"> 
G<small>OD</small>
 is my shepherd;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I lack nothing.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">[God] makes me lie down in green pastures,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and leads me to water in places of repose—<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>water in places of repose </b>In contrast to others “still waters.”</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">renewing my life,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">guiding me in the right paths</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">as befits the divine name.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Though I walk through a valley of deepest darkness,<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>a valley of deepest darkness </b>In contrast to others “the valley of the shadow of death.”</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I fear no harm, for You are with me;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Your rod and Your staff—they comfort me.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You spread a table for me in full view of my enemies;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You anoint my head with oil;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my drink is abundant.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Only goodness and steadfast love shall pursue me</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">all the days of my life,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and I shall dwell in G<small>OD</small>’s house</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for many long years.</span>

Chapter 24

Of David. A psalm.<br><span class="poetry indentAll">The earth is G<small>OD</small>’s and all that it holds,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the world and its inhabitants.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For [God] founded it upon the ocean,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">set it on the nether-streams.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Who may ascend G<small>OD</small>’s mountain?</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Who may stand in that holy place?—</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Anyone who has clean hands and a pure heart,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who has not taken a false oath by My<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>My </b>Ancient versions and some mss. read in the 3rd person.</i> life</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">or sworn deceitfully.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They shall carry away a blessing from G<small>OD</small>,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">a just reward from God, their deliverer.</span>
