Chapter 35

Of David.<br><span class="poetry indentAll">O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, strive with my adversaries,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">give battle to my foes,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">take up shield and buckler,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and come to my defense;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">ready the spear and javelin</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">against my pursuers;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">tell me, “I am your deliverance.”</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Let those who seek my life</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">be frustrated and put to shame;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">let those who plan to harm me</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">fall back in disgrace.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Let them be as chaff in the wind,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble"> 
G<small>OD</small>’s angel driving them on.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Let their path be dark and slippery,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">with G<small>OD</small>’s angel in pursuit.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For without cause they hid a net to trap me;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">without cause they dug a pit<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>a pit </b>Transferred from first clause for clarity.</i> for me.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Let disaster overtake them unawares;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">let the net they hid catch them;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">let them fall into it when disaster [strikes].</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Then shall I exult in G<small>OD</small>,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">rejoice in having been delivered.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">All my bones shall say,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">“E<small>TERNAL</small> One, who is like You?</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">You save a pauper from someone stronger,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">a needy pauper from a despoiler.”</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Malicious witnesses appear</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who question me about things I do not know.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They repay me evil for good,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">[seeking] my bereavement.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Yet, when they were ill,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my dress was sackcloth,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I kept a fast—</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">may what I prayed for happen to me!<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>may what I prayed for happen to me </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain; lit. “my prayer returns upon my bosom.”</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I walked about as though it were my friend or my kin;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I was bowed with gloom, like one mourning for a mother.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">But when I stumble, they gleefully gather;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">wretches gather against me,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I know not why;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they tear at me without end.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">With impious, mocking grimace<sup class="footnote-marker">c</sup><i class="footnote"><b>they tear … grimace </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they gnash their teeth at me.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">O my Sovereign, how long will You look on?</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Rescue me from their attacks,<sup class="footnote-marker">d</sup><i class="footnote"><b>from their attacks </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my precious life, from the lions,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">that I may praise You in a great congregation,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">acclaim You in a mighty throng.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Let not my treacherous enemies rejoice over me,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">or those who hate me without reason wink their eyes.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For they do not offer amity,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">but devise fraudulent schemes against harmless folk.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They open wide their mouths at me,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">saying, “Aha, aha, we have seen it!”</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You have seen it, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">do not hold aloof!</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">O my Sovereign, be not far from me!</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Wake, rouse Yourself for my cause,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for my claim, O my God and my Sovereign!</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Take up my cause, O my E<small>TERNAL</small> God, as You are beneficent,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and let them not rejoice over me.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Let them not think,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">“Aha, just what we wished!”</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Let them not say,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">“We have destroyed him!”</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">May those who rejoice at my misfortune</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">be frustrated and utterly disgraced;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">may those who vaunt themselves over me</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">be clad in frustration and shame.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">May those who desire my vindication</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">sing forth joyously;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">may they always say,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">“Extolled be G<small>OD</small> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who desires the well-being of one who renders service,”</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">while my tongue shall recite Your beneficent acts,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Your praises all day long.</span>

Chapter 36

For the leader. Of the servant of G<small>OD</small>, of David.
<span class="poetry indentAll">I know<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>I know </b>Lit. “In my heart is.”</i> what Transgression says to the wicked;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they have no sense of the dread of God,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">because its speech is seductive to them</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">till their iniquity be found out and they be hated.<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote">Meaning of verse uncertain.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Their words are evil and deceitful;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they will not consider doing good.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">In bed they plot mischief;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they are set on a path of no good,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they do not reject evil.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, Your faithfulness reaches to heaven;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Your steadfastness to the sky;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Your beneficence is like the high mountains;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Your justice like the great deep;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">human and animal You deliver, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">How precious is Your faithful care, O God!</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Humankind shelters in the shadow of Your wings.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They feast on the rich fare of Your house;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You let them drink at Your refreshing stream.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">With You is the fountain of life;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">by Your light do we see light.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Bestow Your faithful care on those devoted to You,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and Your beneficence on the upright.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Let not the foot of the arrogant tread on me,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">or the hand of the wicked drive me away.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">There lie the evildoers, fallen,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">thrust down, unable to rise.</span>

Chapter 37

Of David.<br><span class="poetry indentAll"> <b>א</b> Do not be vexed by evildoers;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">do not be incensed by wrongdoers;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for they soon wither like grass,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">like verdure fade away.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll"> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll"><b>ב</b> Trust in G<small>OD</small> and do good,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">abide in the land and remain loyal.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Seek G<small>OD</small>’s favor,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and you will be granted the desires of your heart.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll"> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll"><b>ג</b> Leave all<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>all </b>Lit. “your way.”</i> to G<small>OD</small>;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">be trusting; [God] will do it—</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">causing your vindication to shine forth like the light,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the justice of your case, like the noonday sun.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll"> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll"><b>ד</b> Be patient and wait for G<small>OD</small>,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">do not be vexed by the one who is prospering—</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the opponent who carries out schemes.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll"> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll"><b>ה</b> Give up anger, abandon fury,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">do not be vexed;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">it can only do harm.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For evildoers will be cut off,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">but those who look to G<small>OD</small>—</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they shall inherit the land.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll"> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll"><b>ו</b> A little longer and there will be no wicked;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">you will look at where they were—</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they will be gone.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">But the lowly shall inherit the land,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and delight in abundant well-being.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll"> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll"><b>ז</b> The wicked scheme against the righteous,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and gnash their teeth at them.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">My Sovereign laughs at them,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">knowing that their day will come.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll"> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll"><b>ח</b> The wicked draw their swords, bend their bows,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">to bring down the lowly and needy,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">to slaughter the upright.<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>the upright </b>Lit. “those whose way is upright.”</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Their swords shall pierce their own hearts,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and their bows shall be broken.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll"> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll"><b>ט</b> Better the little that a righteous person has</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">than the great abundance of the wicked.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For the arms of the wicked shall be broken,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">but G<small>OD</small> is the support of the righteous.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll"> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll"><b>י</b> G<small>OD</small> is concerned for the needs<sup class="footnote-marker">c</sup><i class="footnote"><b>needs </b>Lit. “days.”</i> of the blameless;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">their portion lasts forever;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they shall not come to grief in bad times;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">in famine, they shall eat their fill.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll"> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll"><b>כ</b> But the wicked shall perish,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and G<small>OD</small>’s enemies shall be consumed,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">like meadow grass<sup class="footnote-marker">d</sup><i class="footnote"><b>meadow grass </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> consumed in smoke.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll"> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll"><b>ל</b> The wicked borrow and do not repay;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the righteous are generous and keep giving.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Those blessed by [God] shall inherit the land,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">but those who are cursed shall be cut off.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll"> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll"><b>מ</b> People’s steps<sup class="footnote-marker">e</sup><i class="footnote"><b>People’s steps </b>Or “[Even] the steps of virile men.”</i> are made firm by G<small>OD</small>,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">when their way is a delight to [God].</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Though they stumble, they do not fall down,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for G<small>OD</small> gives them support.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll"> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll"><b>נ</b> I have been young and am now old,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">but I have never seen someone righteous abandoned,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">or their children seeking bread.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They are always generous, and lend,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and their children are held blessed.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll"> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll"><b>ס</b> Shun evil and do good,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and you shall abide forever.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For G<small>OD</small> loves what is right,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and does not abandon those who are faithful.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">They are preserved forever,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">while the children of the wicked will be cut off.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">The righteous shall inherit the land,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and abide forever in it.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll"> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll"><b>פ</b> The mouth of the righteous utters wisdom,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and their tongue speaks what is right.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">The teaching of their God is in their heart;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">their feet do not slip.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll"> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll"><b>צ</b> The wicked watch for the righteous,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">seeking to put them to death;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">
G<small>OD</small>
 will not abandon them to their power,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and will not let them be condemned in judgment.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll"> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll"><b>ק</b> Look to G<small>OD</small> and keep to the godly way,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and you will be raised high that you may inherit the land;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">when the wicked are cut off, you shall see it.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll"> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll"><b>ר</b> I saw the wicked, powerful,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">well-rooted like a robust native tree.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Suddenly they vanished and were gone;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I sought them, but they were not to be found.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll"> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll"><b>ש</b> Mark the blameless, note the upright,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for there is a future for the person of integrity.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">But transgressors shall be utterly destroyed,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the future of the wicked shall be cut off.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll"> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll"><b>ת</b> The deliverance of the righteous comes from G<small>OD</small>,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">their stronghold in time of trouble.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">
G<small>OD</small>
 helps them and rescues them,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">rescues them from the wicked and delivers them,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for in [God] they seek refuge.</span>

Chapter 38

A psalm of David. <i>Lehazkir</i>.<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b><i>Lehazkir</i> </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> 
<span class="poetry indentAll">O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, do not punish me in wrath;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">do not chastise me in fury.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For Your arrows have struck me;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Your blows have fallen upon me.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">There is no soundness in my flesh because of Your rage,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">no wholeness in my bones because of my sin.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For my iniquities have overwhelmed me;<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>overwhelmed me </b>Lit. “passed over my head.”</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they are like a heavy burden, more than I can bear.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">My wounds stink and fester</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">because of my folly.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I am all bent and bowed;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I walk about in gloom all day long.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For my sinews are full of fever;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">there is no soundness in my flesh.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I am all benumbed and crushed;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I roar because of the turmoil in my mind.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">O my Sovereign, You are aware of all my entreaties;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my groaning is not hidden from You.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">My mind reels;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my strength fails me;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my eyes too have lost their luster.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">My friends and companions stand back from my affliction;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my kin stand far off.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Those who seek my life lay traps;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">those who wish me harm speak malice;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they utter deceit all the time.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">But I am like the deaf, unhearing,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">like the mute who cannot speak up;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I am like one who does not hear,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">whose mouth has no retort.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">But I wait for You, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You will answer, O my Sovereign, my God.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For I fear they will rejoice over me;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">when my foot gives way they will vaunt themselves against me.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For I am on the verge of collapse;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my pain is always with me.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I acknowledge my iniquity;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I am fearful over my sin;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for my mortal enemies are numerous;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my treacherous foes are many.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Those who repay evil for good</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">harass me for pursuing good.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Do not abandon me, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my God, be not far from me;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">hasten to my aid,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">O my Sovereign, my deliverance.</span>

Chapter 39

For the leader; for <i>Jeduthun</i>. A psalm of David.
<span class="poetry indentAll">I resolved I would watch my step</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">lest I offend by my speech;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I would keep my mouth muzzled</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">while the villain was in my presence.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I was dumb, silent;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I was very<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>very </b>Cf. use of <i>ṭwb</i> in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Hosea 10:1" href="Hosea.10.1">Hos. 10.1</a>; <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jonah 4:4" href="Jonah.4.4">Jonah 4.4</a>.</i> still</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">while my pain was intense.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">My mind was in a rage,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my thoughts were all aflame;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I spoke out:</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Tell me, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, what my term is,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">what is the measure of my days;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I would know how fleeting my life is.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You have made my life just handbreadths long;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">its span is as nothing in Your sight;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">no human endures any longer than a breath.<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>no human endures any longer than a breath </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> <i>   Selah.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Everyone walks about as a mere shadow;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">mere futility is their hustle and bustle,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">amassing and not knowing who will gather in.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">What, then, can I count on, O my Sovereign?</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">In You my hope lies.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Deliver me from all my transgressions;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">make me not the butt of the benighted.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I am dumb, I do not speak up,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for it is Your doing.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Take away Your plague from me;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I perish from Your blows.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You chastise everyone in punishment for sin,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">consuming like a moth what they treasure.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">No human is more than a breath. <i>   Selah.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Hear my prayer, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">give ear to my cry;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">do not disregard my tears;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for like all my forebears</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I am an alien, resident with You.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Look away from me, that I may recover,<sup class="footnote-marker">c</sup><i class="footnote"><b>that I may recover </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">before I pass away and am gone.</span>

Chapter 40

For the leader. A psalm of David.
<span class="poetry indentAll">I put my hope in G<small>OD</small>,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who inclined toward me,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and heeded my cry.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I was lifted out of the miry pit,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the slimy clay,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and my feet were set on a rock,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my legs steadied.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">A new song was placed into my mouth,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">a hymn to our God.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">May many see it and stand in awe,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and trust in G<small>OD</small>.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Happy is the one<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>the one </b>Or “a virile man.”</i> who trusts in G<small>OD</small>,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who turns not to the arrogant or to followers of falsehood.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You, O my E<small>TERNAL</small> God, have done many things;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the wonders You have devised for us</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">cannot be set out before You;<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>You, O my E<small>TERNAL</small> God, have done many things; / the wonders You have devised for us / cannot be set out before You </b>Or “You, O my E<small>TERNAL</small> God, have done many things— / the wonders You have devised for us; / none can equal You.”</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I would rehearse the tale of them,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">but they are more than can be told.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You gave me to understand that<sup class="footnote-marker">c</sup><i class="footnote"><b>You gave me to understand that </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You do not desire sacrifice and grain offering;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You do not ask for burnt offering and purgation offering.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Then I said,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">“See, I will bring a scroll recounting what befell me.”<sup class="footnote-marker">d</sup><i class="footnote"><b>See, I will bring a scroll recounting what befell me </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">To do what pleases You, my God, is my desire;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Your teaching is in my inmost parts.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I proclaimed [Your] righteousness in a great congregation;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">see, I did not withhold my words;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, You must know it.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I did not keep Your beneficence to myself;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I declared Your faithful deliverance;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I did not fail to speak of Your steadfast love in a great congregation.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, You will not withhold from me Your compassion;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Your steadfast love will protect me always.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For misfortunes without number envelop me;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my iniquities have caught up with me;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I cannot see;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they are more than the hairs of my head;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I am at my wits’ end.<sup class="footnote-marker">e</sup><i class="footnote"><b>I am at my wits’ end </b>Or “my courage fails me.”</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll"><sup class="footnote-marker">f</sup><i class="footnote">Cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 70:1" href="Psalms.70.1">Psalm 70</a>.</i> O favor me, E<small>TERNAL</small> One, and save me;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, hasten to my aid.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Let those who seek to destroy my life</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">be frustrated and disgraced;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">let those who wish me harm</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">fall back in shame.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Let those who say “Aha! Aha!” over me</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">be desolate because of their frustration.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">But let all who seek You be glad and rejoice in You;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">let those who are eager for Your deliverance always say,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">“Extolled be G<small>OD</small>!”</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">But I am poor and needy;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">may my Sovereign devise [deliverance] for me.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You are my help and my rescuer;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my God, do not delay.</span>

Chapter 41

For the leader. A psalm of David.
<span class="poetry indentAll">Happy is someone who is thoughtful of the wretched;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">in bad times may G<small>OD</small> keep them<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>them </b>I.e., the thoughtful person.</i> from harm.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">May G<small>OD</small> guard them and preserve them;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and may they be thought happy in the land.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Do not subject them to the will of their enemies.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">
G<small>OD</small>
 will sustain them on their sickbed;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You shall wholly transform their bed of suffering.<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>You shall wholly transform their bed of suffering </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I said, “O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, have mercy on me,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">heal me, for I have sinned against You.”</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">My enemies speak evilly of me,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">“When will he die and his name perish?”</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Each of them who comes to visit speaks falsely,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">storing up evil thoughts—</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">speaking them once outside.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">All my enemies whisper together against me,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">imagining the worst for me.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">“Something baneful has settled in him;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">he’ll not rise from his bed again.”</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">My ally in whom I trusted,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">even someone who shares my bread,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">has been utterly false to me.<sup class="footnote-marker">c</sup><i class="footnote"><b>has been utterly false to me </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">But You, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, have mercy on me;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">let me rise again and repay them.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Then shall I know that You are pleased with me:</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">when my enemy cannot shout in triumph over me.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You will support me because of my integrity,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and let me abide in Your presence forever.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Blessed is the E<small>TERNAL</small>, God of Israel,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">from eternity to eternity.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Amen and Amen.</span>

Chapter 42

For the leader. A <i>maskil</i> of the Korahites.
<span class="poetry indentAll">Like a hind crying for water,<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>water </b>Lit. “watercourses.”</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my soul cries for You, O God;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my soul<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>soul </b>Or “throat.”</i> thirsts for God, the living God;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">O when will I come to appear before God!</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">My tears have been my food day and night;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I am ever taunted with, “Where is your God?”</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">When I think of this, I pour out my soul:</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">how I walked with the crowd, moved with them,<sup class="footnote-marker">c</sup><i class="footnote"><b>walked with the crowd, moved with them </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the festive throng, to the House of God</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">with joyous shouts of praise.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Why so downcast, my soul,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">why disquieted within me?</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Have hope in God;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I will yet give praise</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for God’s saving presence.<sup class="footnote-marker">d</sup><i class="footnote"><b>for God’s saving presence </b>Several ancient versions and Heb. mss. connect the end of this verse with the first word in v. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 42:7" href="Psalms.42.7">7</a>, reading <i>yeshuʻot panai we-ʼElohai</i>, “my ever-present help, my God,” as in v. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 42:12" href="Psalms.42.12">12</a> and <a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 43:5" href="Psalms.43.5">43.5</a>.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">O my God, my soul is downcast;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">therefore I think of You</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">in this land of Jordan and Hermon,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">in Mount Mizar,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">where deep calls to deep</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">in the roar of Your cataracts;<sup class="footnote-marker">e</sup><i class="footnote"><b>Your cataracts </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">all Your breakers and billows have swept over me.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">By day may G<small>OD</small> devote faithful care,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">so that at night a song may be with me:</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">a prayer to the God of my life.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I say to God, my rock,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">“Why have You forgotten me,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">why must I walk in gloom,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">oppressed by my enemy?”</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Crushing my bones,<sup class="footnote-marker">f</sup><i class="footnote"><b>Crushing my bones </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my foes revile me,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">taunting me always with, “Where is your God?”</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Why so downcast, my soul,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">why disquieted within me?</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Have hope in God;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I will yet give praise,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my ever-present help, my God.</span>

Chapter 43

<span class="poetry indentAll"><sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote">A continuation of <a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 42:1" href="Psalms.42.1">Psalm 42</a>.</i> Vindicate me, O God,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">champion my cause</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">against faithless people;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">rescue me from treacherous, dishonest opponents.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For You are my God, my stronghold;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">why have You rejected me?</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Why must I walk in gloom,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">oppressed by the enemy?</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Send forth Your light and Your truth;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they will lead me;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they will bring me to Your holy mountain,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">to Your dwelling-place,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">that I may come to the altar of God,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">God, my delight, my joy;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">that I may praise You with the lyre,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">O God, my God.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Why so downcast, my soul,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">why disquieted within me?</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Have hope in God;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I will yet give praise,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my ever-present help, my God.</span>

Chapter 44

For the leader. Of the Korahites. A <i>maskil</i>.
<span class="poetry indentAll">We have heard, O God,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">our ancestors have told us</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the deeds You performed in their time,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">in days of old.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">With Your hand You planted them,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">displacing nations;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You brought misfortune on peoples,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and drove them out.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">It was not by their sword that they took the land,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">their arm did not give them victory,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">but Your right hand, Your arm, and Your goodwill,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for You favored them.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You are my king,<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>king </b>See note at <a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 24:7" href="Psalms.24.7">24.7</a>.</i> O God;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">decree victories for Jacob!</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Through You we gore our foes;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">by Your name we trample our adversaries;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I do not trust in my bow;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">it is not my sword that gives me victory;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You give us victory over our foes;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You thwart those who hate us.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">In God we glory at all times,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and praise Your name unceasingly. <i>   Selah.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Yet You have rejected and disgraced us;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You do not go with our armies.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You make us retreat before our foe;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">our enemies plunder us at will.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You let them devour us like sheep;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You disperse us among the nations.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You sell Your people for no fortune,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You set no high price on them.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You make us the butt of our neighbors,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the scorn and derision of those around us.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You make us a byword among the nations,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">a laughingstock<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>laughingstock </b>Lit. “wagging of the head.”</i> among the peoples.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I am always aware of my disgrace;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I am wholly covered with shame</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">at the sound of taunting revilers,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">in the presence of the vengeful foe.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">All this has come upon us,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">yet we have not forgotten You,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">or been false to Your covenant.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Our hearts have not gone astray,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">nor have our feet swerved from Your path,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">though You cast us, crushed, to where the sea monster<sup class="footnote-marker">c</sup><i class="footnote"><b>sea monster </b>Heb. <i>tannim</i> = <i>tannin</i>, as in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Ezekiel 29:3" href="Ezekiel.29.3">Ezek. 29.3</a>; <a class="refLink" data-ref="Ezekiel 32:2" href="Ezekiel.32.2">32.2</a>.</i> is,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and covered us over with deepest darkness.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">If we forgot the name of our God</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and spread forth our hands to a foreign god,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">God would surely search it out,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">as the One who knows the secrets of the heart.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">It is for Your sake that we are slain all day long,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">that we are regarded as sheep to be slaughtered.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Rouse Yourself; why do You sleep, O my Sovereign?</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Awaken, do not reject us forever!</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Why do You hide Your face,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">ignoring our affliction and distress?</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">We lie prostrate in the dust;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">our body clings to the ground.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Arise and help us,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">redeem us, as befits Your faithfulness.</span>

Chapter 45

For the leader; on <i>shoshannim</i>.<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b><i>shoshannim</i> </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> Of the Korahites. A <i>maskil</i>. A love song.
<span class="poetry indentAll">My heart is astir with gracious words;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I speak my poem to a king;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my tongue is the pen of an expert scribe.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You are fairer than all mortals;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">your speech is endowed with grace;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">rightly has God given you an eternal blessing.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Gird your sword upon your thigh, O hero,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">in your splendor and glory;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble"><sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote">Meaning of verse uncertain.</i> in your glory, win success;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">ride on in the cause of truth and meekness and right;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and let your right hand lead you to awesome deeds.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Your arrows, sharpened,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">[pierce] the breast of the king’s enemies;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">peoples fall at your feet.<sup class="footnote-marker">c</sup><i class="footnote"><b>[pierce] the breast of the king’s enemies; / peoples fall at your feet </b>Clauses transposed for clarity.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Your divine throne<sup class="footnote-marker">d</sup><i class="footnote"><b>divine throne </b>Cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="I Chronicles 29:23" href="I_Chronicles.29.23">1 Chron. 29.23</a>.</i> is everlasting;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">your royal scepter is a scepter of equity.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You love righteousness and hate wickedness;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">rightly has God, your God, chosen to anoint you</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">with oil of gladness over all your peers.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">All your robes [are fragrant] with</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">myrrh and aloes and cassia;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">from ivoried palaces</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">lutes entertain you.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Royal princesses are your favorites;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the consort stands at your right hand,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">decked in gold of Ophir.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Take heed, lass, and note,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">incline your ear:</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">forget your people and your father’s house,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and let the king be aroused by your beauty;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">since he is your lord, bow to him.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">O Tyrian lass,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the wealthiest people will court your favor with gifts,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">goods of all sorts.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">The royal princess,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">her dress embroidered with golden mountings,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">is led inside to the king;<sup class="footnote-marker">e</sup><i class="footnote"><b>goods of all sorts … to the king </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">maidens in her train, her companions,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">are presented to you.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They are led in with joy and gladness;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they enter the palace of the king.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Your sons will succeed your fathers;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">you will appoint them princes throughout the land.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I commemorate your fame for all generations,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">so peoples will praise you forever and ever.</span>

Chapter 46

For the leader. Of the Korahites; <i>alamoth</i>.<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b><i>alamoth</i> </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> A song.
<span class="poetry indentAll">God is our refuge and stronghold,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">a help in trouble, very near.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Therefore we are not afraid</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">though the earth reels,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">though mountains topple into the sea—</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">its waters rage and foam;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">in its swell mountains quake. <i>   Selah.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">There is a river whose streams gladden God’s city,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the holy dwelling-place of the Most High.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">God is in its midst, it will not be toppled;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">by daybreak God will come to its aid.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Nations rage, kingdoms topple;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">at the sound of God’s thunder the earth dissolves.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">
G<small>OD</small>
 of hosts is with us;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the God of Jacob is our haven. <i>   Selah.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Come and see what G<small>OD</small> has done,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">how devastation has been wrought on the earth.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">[God] puts a stop to wars throughout the earth,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">breaking the bow, snapping the spear,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">consigning wagons to the flames.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">“Desist! Realize that I am God!</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">I dominate the nations;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I dominate the earth.”</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">
G<small>OD</small>
 of hosts is with us;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the God of Jacob is our haven. <i>   Selah.</i> </span>

Chapter 47

For the leader. Of the Korahites. A psalm.
<span class="poetry indentAll">All you peoples, clap your hands,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">raise a joyous shout for God.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For G<small>OD</small> Most High is awesome,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">great ruler over all the earth,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who subjects peoples to us,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">sets nations at our feet.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">[God] chose our heritage for us,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the pride of Jacob the beloved. <i>   Selah.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">God ascends midst acclamation;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble"> the E<small>TERNAL</small>, to the blasts of the horn.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Sing, O sing to God;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">sing, O sing to our sovereign;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for God is ruler over all the earth;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">sing a hymn.<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>hymn </b>Heb. <i>maskil</i>, a musical term of uncertain meaning.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">God reigns over the nations;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">God is seated on the holy throne.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">The great of the peoples are gathered together,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the retinue of Abraham’s God;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for the guardians of the earth belong to God,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who is greatly exalted.</span>

Chapter 48

A song. A psalm of the Korahites.
<span class="poetry indentAll">
G<small>OD</small>
 is great and much acclaimed</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">in the city of our God,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the holy mountain—</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">fair-crested, joy of all the earth,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Mount Zion, summit of Zaphon,<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>Zaphon </b>A term for the divine abode.</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">city of the great ruler.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Through its citadels, God has become known as a haven.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">See, the kings joined forces;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they advanced together.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">At the mere sight of it they were stunned,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they were terrified, they panicked;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they were seized there with a trembling,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">like a woman in the throes of labor,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">as the Tarshish fleet was wrecked</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">in an easterly gale.<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>as the Tarshish fleet … gale </b>See <a class="refLink" data-ref="I Kings 22:49" href="I_Kings.22.49">1 Kings 22.49</a>.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">The likes of what we heard we have now witnessed</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">in the city of G<small>OD</small> of hosts,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">in the city of our God—</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">may God preserve it forever! <i>   Selah.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">In Your temple, God,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">we meditate upon Your faithful care.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">The praise of You, God, like Your name,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">reaches to the ends of the earth;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Your right hand is filled with beneficence.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Let Mount Zion rejoice!</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Let the towns<sup class="footnote-marker">c</sup><i class="footnote"><b>towns </b>Or “women.”</i> of Judah exult,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">because of Your judgments.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Walk around Zion,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">circle it;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">count its towers,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">take note of its ramparts;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">go through<sup class="footnote-marker">d</sup><i class="footnote"><b>go through </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> its citadels,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">that you may recount it to a future age.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For God truly is our God forever,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who will lead us evermore.<sup class="footnote-marker">e</sup><i class="footnote"><b>evermore </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span>

Chapter 49

For the leader. Of the Korahites. A psalm.
<span class="poetry indentAll">Hear this, all you peoples;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">give ear, all inhabitants of the world,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">both low and high,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">rich and poor alike.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">My mouth utters wisdom,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my speech<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>my speech </b>Lit. “utterance of my heart”; on <i>leb</i>, cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 19:15" href="Psalms.19.15">19.15</a>.</i> is full of insight.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I will turn my attention to a theme,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">set forth my lesson to the music of a lyre.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">In time of trouble, why should I fear</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the encompassing evil of those who would supplant me—</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">those who trust in their riches,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who glory in their great wealth?</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Ah, it<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>Ah, it </b>Or “A brother.”</i> cannot redeem anyone,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">or pay one’s ransom to God;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the price of life is too high;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and so one ceases to be, forever.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Shall anyone live eternally,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and never see the grave?</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For one sees that the wise die,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">that the foolish and ignorant both perish,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">leaving their wealth to others.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Their grave<sup class="footnote-marker">c</sup><i class="footnote"><b>Their grave </b>Heb. <i>qirbam</i>, taken with ancient versions and medieval commentators as the equivalent of <i>qibram</i>.</i> is their eternal home,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the dwelling-place for all generations</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">of those once famous on earth.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Mortals do not abide in honor;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they are like the beasts that perish.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Such is the fate of those who are self-confident,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the end of those pleased with their own talk.<sup class="footnote-marker">d</sup><i class="footnote"><b>the end of those pleased with their own talk </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> <i>   Selah.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Sheeplike they head for Sheol,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">with Death as their shepherd.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">The upright shall rule over them at daybreak,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and their form shall waste away in Sheol</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">till its nobility be gone.<sup class="footnote-marker">e</sup><i class="footnote"><b>and their form … gone </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">But God will redeem my life from the clutches of Sheol,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">by taking me. <i>   Selah.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Do not be afraid when someone else becomes rich,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">when their household goods increase;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for when they die they can take none of it along;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">their goods cannot follow them down.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Though they congratulate themselves in their lifetime</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">—“All must admit that you did well by yourself”<sup class="footnote-marker">f</sup><i class="footnote"><b>All must admit that you did well by yourself </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i>—</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">yet they must join the company of their ancestors,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who will never see daylight again.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Mortals do not understand honor;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they are like the beasts that perish.</span>

Chapter 50

A psalm of Asaph.<br><span class="poetry indentAll">God, the E<small>TERNAL</small> God<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>God,…God </b>Heb. <i>ʼEl ʼElohim</i>.</i> spoke</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and summoned the world from east to west.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">From Zion, perfect in beauty,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">God appeared</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">—let our God come and not fail to act!</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">[God] was preceded by devouring fire,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">with a fierce storm all around.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">The heavens above were summoned,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and the earth, for the trial of God’s people.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">“Bring in My devotees,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who made a covenant with Me over sacrifice!”</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Then the heavens proclaimed God’s righteousness,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for this is a God who judges. <i>   Selah.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">“Pay heed, My people, and I will speak,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">O Israel, and I will arraign you.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">I am God, your God.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I censure you not for your sacrifices,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and your burnt offerings, made to Me daily;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I claim no bull from your estate,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">no he-goats from your pens.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For Mine is every animal of the forest,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the beasts on a thousand mountains.<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>a thousand mountains </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I know every bird of the mountains,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the creatures of the field are subject to Me.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Were I hungry, I would not tell you,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for Mine is the world and all it holds.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Do I eat the flesh of bulls,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">or drink the blood of he-goats?</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Sacrifice a thank offering to God,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and pay your vows to the Most High.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Call upon Me in time of trouble;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I will rescue you, and you shall honor Me.”</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">And to the wicked, God said:</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">“Who are you to recite My laws,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and mouth the terms of My covenant,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">seeing that you spurn My discipline,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and brush My words aside?</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You fall in with a thief when you see one,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and throw in your lot with adulterers;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">you devote your mouth to evil,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and yoke your tongue to deceit;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">you are busy maligning your kin,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">defaming the child of your mother.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">If I failed to act when you did these things,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">you would fancy that I was like you;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">so I censure you and confront you with charges.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Mark this, you who are unmindful of God,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">lest I tear you apart and no one save you.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Whoever sacrifices a thank offering honors Me,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and to one who sets out on the proper way<sup class="footnote-marker">c</sup><i class="footnote"><b>and to one who sets out on the proper way </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I will show the salvation of God.”</span>

Chapter 51

For the leader. A psalm of David, 
when Nathan the prophet came to him after he had come to Bathsheba.<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>when Nathan … Bathsheba </b>Cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="II Samuel 12" href="II_Samuel.12">2 Sam. 12</a>.</i> 
<span class="poetry indentAll">Have mercy upon me, O God,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">as befits Your faithfulness;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">in keeping with Your abundant compassion,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">blot out my transgressions.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Wash me thoroughly of my iniquity,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and purify me of my sin;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">for I recognize my transgressions,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and am ever conscious of my sin.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Against You alone have I sinned,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and done what is evil in Your sight;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">so You are just in Your sentence,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and right in Your judgment.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Indeed I was born with iniquity;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">with sin my mother conceived me.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll"><sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote">Meaning of verse uncertain.</i> Indeed You desire truth about that which is hidden;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">teach me wisdom about secret things.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Purge me with hyssop till I am pure;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">wash me till I am whiter than snow.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Let me hear tidings of joy and gladness;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">let the bones You have crushed exult.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Hide Your face from my sins;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">blot out all my iniquities.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Fashion a pure heart for me, O God;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">create in me a steadfast spirit.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Do not cast me out of Your presence,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">or take Your holy spirit away from me.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Let me again rejoice in Your help;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">let a vigorous spirit sustain me.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I will teach transgressors Your ways,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">that sinners may return to You.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Save me from bloodguilt,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">O God, God, my deliverer,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">that I may sing forth Your beneficence.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">O my Sovereign, open my lips,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and let my mouth declare Your praise.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You do not want me to bring sacrifices;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You do not desire burnt offerings;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">True sacrifice to God is a contrite spirit;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">God, You will not despise</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">a contrite and crushed heart.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">May it please You to make Zion prosper;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">rebuild the walls of Jerusalem.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Then You will want sacrifices offered in righteousness,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">burnt and whole offerings;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">then bulls will be offered on Your altar.</span>

Chapter 52

For the leader. A <i>maskil</i> of David, 
when Doeg the Edomite came and informed Saul, telling him, “David came to Ahimelech’s house.”<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote">Cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="I Samuel 22:9" href="I_Samuel.22.9">1 Sam. 22.9ff</a>.</i> 
<span class="poetry indentAll">Why do you boast of your evil, brave fellow?</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">God’s faithfulness never ceases.<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>never ceases </b>Lit. “is all the day.”</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Your tongue devises mischief,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">like a sharpened razor that works treacherously.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You prefer evil to good,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the lie, to speaking truthfully. <i>   Selah.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You love all pernicious words,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">treacherous speech.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">So God will tear you down for good,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">will break you and pluck you from your tent,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and root you out of the land of the living. <i>   Selah.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">The righteous, seeing it, will be awestruck;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they will jibe at you,<sup class="footnote-marker">c</sup><i class="footnote"><b>you </b>Heb. “him.”</i> saying,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">“Here was a fellow who did not make God his refuge,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">but trusted in his great wealth,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">relied upon his mischief.”</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">But I am like a thriving olive tree in God’s house;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I trust in the faithfulness of God forever and ever.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I praise You forever, for You have acted;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I declare that Your name is good<sup class="footnote-marker">d</sup><i class="footnote"><b>I declare that Your name is good </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain; in contrast to others “I will wait for Your name for it is good.”</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">in the presence of Your faithful ones.</span>

Chapter 53

<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote">Cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 14:1" href="Psalms.14.1">Psalm 14</a>.</i> For the leader; on <i>mahalath</i>.<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b><i>mahalath</i> </b>Meaning of Heb. unknown.</i> A <i>maskil</i> of David.
<span class="poetry indentAll">The scoundrel thinks,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">“God does not care.”<sup class="footnote-marker">c</sup><i class="footnote"><b>God does not care </b>Lit. “There is no God”; cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 10:4" href="Psalms.10.4">10.4</a>.</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Mortals’<sup class="footnote-marker">d</sup><i class="footnote"><b>Mortals’ </b>Heb. “Their.”</i> wrongdoing is corrupt and loathsome;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">no one does good.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">God looks down from heaven on humankind</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">to find someone with understanding,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">someone mindful of God.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Everyone is dross,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">altogether foul;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">there is no one who does good,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">not even one.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Are they so witless, those evildoers,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who devour my people as they devour food,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and do not invoke God?</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">There they will be seized with fright</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">—never was there such a fright—</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for God has scattered the bones of your besiegers;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">you have put them to shame,<sup class="footnote-marker">e</sup><i class="footnote"><b>never was there … put them to shame </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for God has rejected them.</span>

Chapter 54

For the leader; with instrumental music. A <i>maskil</i> of David, 
when the Ziphites came and told Saul, “Know, David is in hiding among us.”<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote">Cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="I Samuel 23:19" href="I_Samuel.23.19">1 Sam. 23.19</a>.</i>

<span class="poetry indentAll">O God, hear my prayer;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">give ear to the words of my mouth.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For strangers have risen against me,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and those who are ruthless seek my life;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they are unmindful of God. <i>   Selah.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">See, God is my helper;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my Sovereign is my support.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">[God] will repay the evil of my watchful foes;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">by Your faithfulness, destroy them!</span>

<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for it has saved me from my foes,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and let me gaze triumphant upon my enemies.</span>

Chapter 55

For the leader; with instrumental music. A <i>maskil</i> of David.
<span class="poetry indentAll">Give ear, O God, to my prayer;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">do not ignore my plea;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">pay heed to me and answer me.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">I am tossed about, complaining and moaning</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">at the clamor of the enemy,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">because of the oppression of the wicked;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for they bring evil upon me</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and furiously harass me.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">My heart is convulsed within me;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">terrors of death assail me.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Fear and trembling invade me;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I am clothed with horror.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I said,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">“O that I had the wings of a dove!</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I would fly away and find rest;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">surely, I would flee far off;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I would lodge in the wilderness; <i>   selah</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I would soon find me a refuge</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">from the sweeping wind,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">from the tempest.”</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">O my Sovereign, confound their speech, confuse it!</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">For I see lawlessness and strife in the city;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">day and night they make their rounds on its walls;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">evil and mischief are inside it.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Malice is within it;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">fraud and deceit never leave its square.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">It is not an enemy who reviles me</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">—I could bear that;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">it is not my foe who boasts against me</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">—for then I could hide;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">but it is you, my equal,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my companion, my friend;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">sweet was our fellowship;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">we walked together in God’s house.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Let [God] incite death against them;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">may they go down alive into Sheol!</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">For where they dwell,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">there evil is.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">As for me, I call to God;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble"> 
G<small>OD</small>
 will deliver me.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Evening, morning, and noon,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I complain and moan,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and my voice is heard.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">[God] redeems me unharmed</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">from the battle against me;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">it is as though many are on my side.<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>it is as though many are on my side </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">God who has reigned from the first,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who will have no successor,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">hears and humbles those who show no reverence. <i>   Selah.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">My companion<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>My companion </b>Heb. “He,” i.e., the friend of v. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 55:14" href="Psalms.55.14">14</a>.</i> caused harm to allies</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and broke a pact—</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">with talk smoother than butter,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">yet with a mind set on war;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">with words that were softer than oil,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">yet in fact were drawn swords.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Cast your burden on G<small>OD</small> and you will be sustained;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the righteous will never be allowed to collapse.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For You, O God, will bring them down to the nethermost Pit—</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">those treacherous murderers;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they shall not live out half their days—</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">but I trust in You.</span>

Chapter 56

For the leader; on <i>yonath elem reḥokim</i>.<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b><i>yonath elem reḥokim</i> </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> Of David. A <i>michtam</i>; when the Philistines seized him in Gath.
