<span class="poetry indentAll">Have mercy on me, O God,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for people persecute me;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">all day long my adversary oppresses me.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">My watchful foes persecute me all day long;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">many are my adversaries, O Exalted One.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">When I am afraid, I trust in You,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">in God, whose word I praise,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">in God I trust;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I am not afraid;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">what can mortals<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>mortals </b>Lit. “flesh.”</i> do to me?</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">All day long they cause me grief in my affairs,<sup class="footnote-marker">c</sup><i class="footnote"><b>they cause me grief in my affairs </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they plan only evil against me.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They plot, they lie in ambush;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they watch my every move, hoping for my death.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Cast them out for their evil;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">subdue peoples in Your anger, O God.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll"><sup class="footnote-marker">d</sup><i class="footnote">Meaning of verse uncertain.</i> You keep count of my wanderings;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">put my tears into Your flask,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">into Your record.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Then my enemies will retreat when I call on You;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">this I know, that God is for me.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">In God, whose word I praise,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">in G<small>OD</small>, whose word I praise,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">in God I trust;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I am not afraid;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">what can mere humans do to me?</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I must pay my vows to You, O God;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I will render thank offerings to You.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For You have saved me from death,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my foot from stumbling,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">that I may walk before God in the light of life.</span>

Chapter 57

For the leader; <i>al tashḥeth</i>.<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b><i>al tashḥeth</i> </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> Of David. A <i>michtam</i>; when he fled from Saul into a cave.
<span class="poetry indentAll">Have mercy on me, O God, have mercy on me,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for I seek refuge in You,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I seek refuge in the shadow of Your wings,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">until danger passes.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I call to God Most High,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">to God who is good to me,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who will reach down from heaven and deliver me—</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">sending down steadfast love;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my persecutor reviles. <i>   Selah.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">As for me, I lie down among lions who devour humans—</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">whose teeth are spears and arrows,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">whose tongue is a sharp sword.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Exalt Yourself over the heavens, O God,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">let Your glory be over all the earth!</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They prepared a net for my feet to ensnare me;<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>to ensnare me </b>Cf. Mishnaic Heb. <i>kefifah</i>, a wicker basket used in fishing.</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they dug a pit for me,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">but they fell into it. <i>   Selah.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll"><sup class="footnote-marker">c</sup><i class="footnote">Cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 108:2-6" href="Psalms.108.2-6">108.2–6</a>.</i> My heart is firm, O God;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my heart is firm;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I will sing, I will chant a hymn.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Awake, O my soul!</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Awake, O harp and lyre!</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">I will wake the dawn.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I will praise You among the peoples, O my Sovereign;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I will sing a hymn to You among the nations—</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for Your faithfulness is as high as heaven;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Your steadfastness reaches to the sky.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Exalt Yourself over the heavens, O God,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">let Your glory be over all the earth!</span>

Chapter 58

For the leader; <i>al tashḥeth</i>. Of David. A <i>michtam</i>.
<span class="poetry indentAll">O mighty ones,<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>O mighty ones </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> do you really decree what is just?</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Do you judge humankind with equity?</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">In your minds you devise wrongdoing in the land;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">with your hands you deal out lawlessness.<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>with your hands you deal out lawlessness </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">The wicked are defiant from birth;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the liars go astray from the womb.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Their venom is like that of a snake,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">a deaf viper that stops its ears</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">so as not to hear the voice of charmers</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">or the expert mutterer of spells.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">O God, smash their teeth in their mouth;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">shatter the fangs of lions, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">let them melt, let them vanish like water—</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">aim Your arrows that they be cut down—</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">like a snail that melts away as it moves;<sup class="footnote-marker">c</sup><i class="footnote"><b>like a snail that melts away as it moves </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">like a woman’s stillbirth—may they never see the sun!</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Before the thorns grow into a bramble,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">whirl them away alive in fury.<sup class="footnote-marker">d</sup><i class="footnote"><b>the thorns grow … in fury </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">The righteous will rejoice when they see revenge;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they will bathe their feet in the blood of the wicked.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">People will say,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">“There is, then, a reward for the righteous;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">there is, indeed, divine justice on earth.”</span>

Chapter 59

For the leader; <i>al tashḥeth</i>. Of David. A <i>michtam</i>; when Saul sent men to watch his house in order to put him to death.<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>when Saul sent … death </b>Cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="I Samuel 19:11" href="I_Samuel.19.11">1 Sam. 19.11</a>.</i> 
<span class="poetry indentAll">Save me from my enemies, O my God;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">secure me against my assailants.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Save me from evildoers;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">deliver me from murderers.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For see, they lie in wait for me;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">fierce people plot against me</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for no offense of mine,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for no transgression, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for no guilt of mine</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">do they rush to array themselves against me.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Look, rouse Yourself in my behalf!</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, God of hosts,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">God of Israel,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">bestir Yourself to bring all nations to account;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">have no mercy on any treacherous villain. <i>   Selah.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They come each evening growling like dogs,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">roaming the city.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They rave with their mouths,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">sharp words<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>sharp words </b>Lit. “swords.”</i> are on their lips;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">[they think,] “Who hears?”</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">But You, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, laugh at them;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You mock all the nations.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">O my<sup class="footnote-marker">c</sup><i class="footnote"><b>my </b>With several mss.; cf. v. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 59:18" href="Psalms.59.18">18</a>; Heb. 3rd person.</i> strength, I wait for You;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for God is my haven.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">My faithful God will come to aid me;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">God will let me gloat over my watchful foes.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Do not kill them lest my people be unmindful;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">with Your power make wanderers of them;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">bring them low, O our shield, my Sovereign,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">because of their sinful mouths,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the words on their lips.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Let them be trapped by their pride,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and by the imprecations and lies they utter.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">In Your fury put an end to them;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">put an end to them that they be no more;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">that it may be known to the ends of the earth</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">that God does rule over Jacob. <i>   Selah.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They come each evening growling like dogs,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">roaming the city.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They wander in search of food;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and whine if they are not satisfied.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">But I will sing of Your strength,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">extol each morning Your faithfulness;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for You have been my haven,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">a refuge in time of trouble.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">O my strength, to You I sing hymns;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for God is my haven, my faithful God.</span>

Chapter 60

For the leader; on <i>shushan eduth</i>.<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b><i>shushan eduth</i> </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> A <i>michtam</i> of David (to be taught), 
when he fought with Aram-naharaim and Aram-zobah, and Joab returned and defeated Edom—[an army] of twelve thousand men—in the Valley of Salt.<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote">Cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="II Samuel 8" href="II_Samuel.8">2 Sam. 8</a>; <a class="refLink" data-ref="I Chronicles 18" href="I_Chronicles.18">1 Chron. 18</a>.</i> 
<span class="poetry indentAll">O God, You have rejected us,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You have made a breach in us;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You have been angry;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">restore us!</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You have made the land quake;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You have torn it open.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Mend its fissures,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for it is collapsing.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You have made Your people suffer hardship;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You have given us wine that makes us reel.<sup class="footnote-marker">c</sup><i class="footnote"><b>You have given us wine that makes us reel </b>Or “You have sated Your people with a bitter draft.”</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Give those who fear You because of Your truth</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">a banner for rallying.<sup class="footnote-marker">d</sup><i class="footnote"><b>Give those … rallying </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> <i>   Selah.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll"><sup class="footnote-marker">e</sup><i class="footnote">Cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 108:7-14" href="Psalms.108.7-14">Ps. 108.7–14</a>.</i> That those whom You love might be rescued,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">deliver with Your right hand and answer me.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">God promised in the sanctuary<sup class="footnote-marker">f</sup><i class="footnote"><b>in the sanctuary </b>Or “by God’s holiness.”</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">that I would exultingly divide up Shechem,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and measure the Valley of Sukkoth;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Gilead and Manasseh would be mine,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Ephraim my chief stronghold,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Judah my scepter;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Moab would be my washbasin;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">on Edom I would cast my shoe;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">acclaim me, O Philistia!</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Would that I were brought to the bastion!</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Would that I were led to Edom!</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">But You have rejected us, O God;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">God, You do not march with our armies.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Grant us Your aid against the foe,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for human help is worthless.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">We shall triumph with God,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who will trample our foes.</span>

Chapter 61

For the leader; with instrumental music. Of David.
<span class="poetry indentAll">Hear my cry, O God,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">heed my prayer.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">From the end of the earth I call to You;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">when my heart is faint,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You lead me to a rock that is high above me.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For You have been my refuge,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">a tower of strength against the enemy.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">O that I might dwell in Your tent forever,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">take refuge under Your protecting wings. <i>   Selah.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">O God, You have heard my vows;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">grant the request<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>request </b>Taking the noun <i>yrsht</i> as an alternate form of <i>ʼrsht</i>; cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 21:3" href="Psalms.21.3">Ps. 21.3</a>.</i> of those who fear Your name.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Add days to the days of the king;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">may his years extend through generations;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">may he dwell in God’s presence forever;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">appoint<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>appoint </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> steadfast love to guard him.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">So I will sing hymns to Your name forever,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">as I fulfill my vows day after day.</span>

Chapter 62

For the leader; on <i>Jeduthun</i>. A psalm of David.
<span class="poetry indentAll">Truly my soul waits quietly for God,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">from whom my deliverance comes.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Truly [God] is my rock and deliverance,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my haven; I shall never be shaken.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">How long will all of you attack<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>attack </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> someone,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">to crush<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>crush </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> them, as though they were</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">a leaning wall, a tottering fence?</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You lay plans to topple them from their status;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">you delight in falsehood;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">you bless with your mouths,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">while inwardly you curse.<sup class="footnote-marker">c</sup><i class="footnote"><b>You…your…you </b>Heb. “They…their…they.”</i> <i>   Selah.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Truly, wait quietly for God, O my soul,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">from whom comes my hope.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">[God] is my rock and deliverance,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my haven; I shall not be shaken.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I rely on God, my deliverance and glory,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my rock of strength;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">in God is my refuge.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Trust in [God] at all times, O people;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">pour out your hearts before the Holy One;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">God is our refuge. <i>   Selah.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Humans are mere breath;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">mortals, an illusion<sup class="footnote-marker">d</sup><i class="footnote"><b>Humans are mere breath; / mortals, an illusion </b>Or “The common people are mere breath; / even the notables, an illusion—”; or “Mortals are mere breath; / partisans, an illusion—.”</i>—</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">placed on a scale all together,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they weigh even less than a breath.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Do not trust in violence,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">or put false hopes in robbery;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">if force bears fruit pay it no mind.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">One thing God has spoken;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">two things have I heard:</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">that might belongs to God,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and faithfulness is Yours, O my Sovereign,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">to reward everyone according to their deeds.</span>

Chapter 63

A psalm of David, when he was in the Wilderness of Judah.
<span class="poetry indentAll">God, You are my God;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I search for You,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my soul thirsts for You,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my body yearns for You,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">as a parched and thirsty land that has no water.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I shall behold You in the sanctuary,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and see Your might and glory,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Truly Your faithfulness is better than life;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my lips declare Your praise.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I bless You all my life;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I lift up my hands, invoking Your name.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I am sated as with a rich feast,<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>rich feast </b>Lit. “suet and fat.”</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I sing praises with joyful lips</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">when I call You to mind upon my bed,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">when I think of You in the watches of the night—</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for You are my help,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and in the shadow of Your wings</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I shout for joy.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">My soul is attached to You;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Your right hand supports me.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">May those who seek to destroy my life</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">enter the depths of the earth.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">May they be gutted by the sword;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">may they be prey to jackals.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">But the king shall rejoice in God;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">all who swear by [God] shall exult,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">when the mouth of liars is stopped.</span>

Chapter 64

For the leader. A psalm of David.
<span class="poetry indentAll">Hear my voice, O God, when I plead;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">guard my life from the enemy’s terror.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Hide me from a band of evildoers,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">from a crowd of wrongdoers,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who whet their tongues like swords;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they aim their arrows—cruel words—</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">to shoot from hiding at someone blameless,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">shooting suddenly and without fear.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They arm themselves with an evil word;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">when they speak, it is to conceal traps;<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>They arm themselves … conceal traps </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they think, “Who will see them?”</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll"><sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote">Meaning of verse uncertain.</i> Let the wrongdoings they have concealed,<sup class="footnote-marker">c</sup><i class="footnote"><b>they have concealed </b>Reading <i>ṭamnu</i> with some mss. (cf. Minḥat Shai) and Rashi; most printed editions <i>tamnu</i>, traditionally rendered “they have accomplished.”</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">each one’s inner, secret thoughts,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">be wholly exposed.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">God shall shoot them with arrows;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they shall be struck down suddenly.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Their tongue shall be their downfall;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">all who see them shall recoil in horror;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">all people shall stand in awe;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they shall proclaim the work of God</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">whose deed they perceived.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">In G<small>OD</small> shall the righteous rejoice</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and take refuge;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">all the upright shall exult.</span>

Chapter 65

For the leader. A psalm of David. A song.
<span class="poetry indentAll">Praise befits You in Zion, O God;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">vows are paid to You;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">all humankind<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>humankind </b>Lit. “flesh.”</i> comes to You,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You who hear prayer.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">When all manner of sins overwhelm me,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">it is You who forgive our iniquities.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Happy is the one You choose and bring near</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">to dwell in Your courts;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">may we be sated with the blessings of Your house,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Your holy temple.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Answer us with victory through awesome deeds,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">O God, our deliverer,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">in whom all the ends of the earth</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and the distant seas</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">put their trust;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who by divine power fixed the mountains firmly,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who is girded with might,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who stills the raging seas,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the raging waves,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and tumultuous peoples.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Those who live at the ends of the earth are awed by Your signs;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You make the lands of sunrise and sunset shout for joy.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You take care of the earth and irrigate it;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You enrich it greatly,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">with the channel of God full of water;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You provide grain for all;<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>grain for all </b>Heb. “their grain.”</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for so do You prepare it.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Saturating its furrows,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">leveling its ridges,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You soften it with showers,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You bless its growth.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You crown the year with Your bounty;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">fatness is distilled in Your paths—</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the pasturelands distill it;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the hills are girded with joy.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">The meadows are clothed with flocks,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the valleys mantled with grain;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they raise a shout, they break into song.</span>

Chapter 66

For the leader. A song. A psalm.<br><span class="poetry indentAll">Raise a shout for God, all the earth;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">sing the glory of God’s name,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">make glorious God’s praise.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Say to God,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">“How awesome are Your deeds,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Your enemies cower before Your great strength;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">all the earth bows to You,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and sings hymns to You;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">all sing hymns to Your name.” <i>   Selah.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Come and see the works of God,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who is held in awe by mortals for acts divine,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and who turned the sea into dry land:</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Israel<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>Israel </b>Heb. “they”; cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Joshua 4:23" href="Joshua.4.23">Josh. 4.23</a>.</i> crossed the river on foot;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">we therefore rejoice in [God].</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">[God] rules forever with divine might,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">eyes scanning the nations—</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">not letting the rebellious assert themselves. <i>   Selah.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">O peoples, bless our God;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">celebrate with praises</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the One who has granted us life,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and has not let our feet slip.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You have tried us, O God,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">refining us, as one refines silver.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You have caught us in a net,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">caught us in trammels.<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>caught us in trammels </b>Lit. “put a trammel on our loins.”</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You have let people ride over us;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">we have endured fire and water,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and You have brought us through to prosperity.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I enter Your house with burnt offerings,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I pay my vows to You,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">[vows] that my lips pronounced,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">that my mouth uttered in my distress.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I offer up fatlings to You,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">with the odor of burning rams;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I sacrifice bulls and he-goats. <i>   Selah.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Come and hear, all you who fear God,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">as I tell what was done for me.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I called aloud to [God],</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">glorification on my tongue.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Had I an evil thought in my mind,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my Sovereign would not have listened.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">But God did listen—</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">paying heed to my prayer.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Blessed is God who has not turned away my prayer,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">or faithful care, from me.</span>

Chapter 67

For the leader; with instrumental music. A psalm. A song.
<span class="poetry indentAll">May God be gracious to us and bless us,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">showing us favor, <i>   selah</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">that Your way be known on earth,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Your deliverance among all nations.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Peoples will praise You, O God;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">all peoples will praise You.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Nations will exult and shout for joy,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for You rule the peoples with equity,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You guide the nations of the earth. <i>   Selah.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">The peoples will praise You, O God;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">all peoples will praise You.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">May the earth yield its produce;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">may God, our God, bless us.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">May God bless us,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and be revered to the ends of the earth.</span>

Chapter 68

<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote">The coherence of this psalm and the meaning of many of its passages are uncertain.</i> For the leader. Of David. A psalm. A song.
<span class="poetry indentAll">God will arise;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">all opponents shall be scattered,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and foes shall flee.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Disperse them as smoke is dispersed;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">as wax melts at fire,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">so the wicked shall perish before God.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">But the righteous shall rejoice;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they shall exult in the presence of God;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they shall be exceedingly joyful.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Sing to God, chant hymns to the divine name;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">extol the One who rides the clouds,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the One whose name is Yah.<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>Yah </b>A shortened form of the divine Name; see <a class="refLink" data-ref="Isaiah 12:2" href="Isaiah.12.2">Isa. 12.2</a>; <a class="refLink" data-ref="Isaiah 26:4" href="Isaiah.26.4">26.4</a>.</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Exult in God’s presence—</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the guardian of the fatherless, the champion of widows,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">God, dwelling in holiness.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">God restores the lonely to their homes,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">sets free the imprisoned, safe and sound,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">while the rebellious must live in a parched land.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">O God, when You went at the head of Your army,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">when You marched through the desert, <i>   selah</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the earth trembled, the sky rained because of God,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">yon Sinai, because of God—the God of Israel.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You released a bountiful rain, O God;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">when Your own land languished, You sustained it.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Your tribe dwells there;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">O God, in Your goodness You provide for the needy.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">My Sovereign gives a command;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the women who bring the news are a great host:</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">“The kings and their armies are in headlong flight;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the women at home are sharing in the spoils;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">even for those of you who lie among the sheepfolds</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">there are wings of a dove sheathed in silver,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">its pinions in fine gold.”</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">When Shaddai scattered the kings,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">it seemed like a snowstorm in Zalmon.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">O majestic mountain, Mount Bashan;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">O jagged mountain, Mount Bashan;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">why so hostile, O jagged mountains,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">toward the mountain God desired as a dwelling?</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll"> 
G<small>OD</small>
 shall abide there forever.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">God’s chariots are myriads upon myriads,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">thousands upon thousands;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my Sovereign is among them as in Sinai in holiness.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You went up to the heights, having taken captives,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">having received tribute of people,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">even of those who rebel</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">against the abiding there of Yah—who is God.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Blessed is my Sovereign,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">day by day supporting us—</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">God, our deliverance. <i>   Selah.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">God is for us a God of deliverance;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble"> 
G<small>OD</small>
 my Sovereign provides an escape from death.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">God will smash the heads of all opponents,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the hairy crown of the one who walks about in guilt.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">My Sovereign said, “I will retrieve from Bashan,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I will retrieve from the depths of the sea;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">that your feet may wade through blood,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">that the tongue of your dogs may have its portion of your enemies.”</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">People see Your processions, O God,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the processions of my God, my monarch,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">into the sanctuary.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">First come singers, then musicians,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">amidst maidens playing hand-drums.<sup class="footnote-marker">c</sup><i class="footnote"><b>maidens playing hand-drums </b>See note at <a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 15:20" href="Exodus.15.20">Exod. 15.20</a>.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">In assemblies bless God,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble"> 
E<small>TERNAL</small> One, O you who are from the fountain of Israel.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">There is little Benjamin who rules them,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the princes of Judah who command them,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the princes of Zebulun and Naphtali.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Your God has ordained strength for you,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the strength, O God,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">that You displayed for us</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">from Your temple above Jerusalem.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">The kings bring You tribute.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Blast the beast of the marsh,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the herd of bulls among the peoples, the calves,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">till they come cringing with pieces of silver.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Scatter the peoples who delight in wars!</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Tribute-bearers shall come from Egypt;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Cush shall hasten its gifts to God.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">O kingdoms of the earth,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">sing to God;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">chant hymns to my Sovereign, <i>   selah</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">to the One who rides the ancient highest heavens,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who thunders forth with a mighty voice.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Ascribe might to God,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">whose majesty is over Israel,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">whose might is in the skies.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You are awesome, O God, in Your holy places;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">it is the God of Israel who gives might and power to the people.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Blessed is God.</span>

Chapter 69

For the leader. On <i>shoshannim</i>.<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b><i>shoshannim</i> </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> Of David.
<span class="poetry indentAll">Deliver me, O God,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for the waters have reached my neck;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I am sinking into the slimy deep</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and find no foothold;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I have come into the watery depths;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the flood sweeps me away.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I am weary with calling;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my throat is dry;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my eyes fail</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">while I wait for God.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">More numerous than the hairs of my head</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">are those who hate me without reason;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">many are those who would destroy me,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my treacherous enemies.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Must I restore what I have not stolen?</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">God, You know my folly;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my guilty deeds are not hidden from You.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Let those who look to You,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">O my Sovereign, G<small>OD</small> of hosts,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">not be disappointed on my account;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">let those who seek You,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">O God of Israel,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">not be shamed because of me.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">It is for Your sake that I have been reviled,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">that shame covers my face;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I am a stranger to my kin,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">an alien to my own siblings.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">My zeal for Your house has been my undoing;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the reproaches of those who revile You have fallen upon me.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">When I wept and fasted,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I was reviled for it.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I made sackcloth my garment;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I became a byword among them.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Those who sit in the gate talk about me;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I am the taunt of drunkards.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">As for me, may my prayer come to You, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">at a favorable moment;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">O God, in Your abundant faithfulness,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">answer me with Your sure deliverance.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Rescue me from the mire;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">let me not sink;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">let me be rescued from my enemies,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and from the watery depths.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Let the floodwaters not sweep me away;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">let the deep not swallow me;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">let the mouth of the Pit not close over me.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Answer me, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">according to Your great steadfastness;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">in accordance with Your abundant mercy</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">turn to me;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">do not hide Your face from Your servant,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for I am in distress;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">answer me quickly.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Come near to me and redeem me;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">free me from my enemies.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You know my reproach,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my shame, my disgrace;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You are aware of all my foes.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Reproach breaks my heart,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I am in despair;<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>in despair </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I hope for consolation, but there is none,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for comforters, but find none.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They give me gall for food,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">vinegar to quench my thirst.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">May their table be a trap for them,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">a snare for their allies.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">May their eyes grow dim so that they cannot see;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">may their loins collapse continually.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Pour out Your wrath on them;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">may Your blazing anger overtake them;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">may their encampments be desolate;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">may their tents stand empty.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For they persecute those You have struck;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they talk about the pain of those You have felled.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Add that to their guilt;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">let them have no share of Your beneficence;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">may they be erased from the book of life,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and not be inscribed with the righteous.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">But I am lowly and in pain;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Your help, O God, keeps me safe.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I will extol God’s name with song,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">exultation, and praise.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">That will please G<small>OD</small> more than oxen,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">than bulls with horns and hoofs.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">The lowly will see and rejoice;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">you who are mindful of God, take heart!</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For G<small>OD</small> listens to the needy,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and does not spurn those held captive.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Heaven and earth shall sing praise,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the seas, and all that moves in them.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For God will deliver Zion</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and rebuild the cities of Judah;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they shall live there and inherit it;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the offspring of God’s servants shall possess it;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">those who cherish God’s name shall dwell there.</span>

Chapter 70

For the leader. Of David. <i>Lehazkir</i>.<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b><i>Lehazkir</i> </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> 
<span class="poetry indentAll"><sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote">Cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 40:14-18" href="Psalms.40.14-18">Ps. 40.14–18</a>.</i> Hasten, O God, to save me;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, to aid me!</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Let those who seek my life</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">be frustrated and disgraced;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">let those who wish me harm,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">fall back in shame.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Let those who say, “Aha! Aha!”</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">turn back because of their frustration.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">But let all who seek You be glad and rejoice in You;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">let those who are eager for Your deliverance always say,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">“Extolled be God!”</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">But I am poor and needy;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">O God, hasten to me!</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">You are my help and my rescuer;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, do not delay.</span>

Chapter 71

<span class="poetry indentAll">I seek refuge in You, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">may I never be disappointed.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">As You are beneficent, save me and rescue me;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">incline Your ear to me and deliver me.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Be a sheltering rock for me to which I may always repair;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">decree my deliverance,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for You are my rock and my fortress.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">My God, rescue me from the hand of the wicked,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">from the grasp of the unjust and the lawless.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For You are my hope,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">O my Sovereign G<small>OD</small>,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my trust from my youth.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">While yet unborn, I depended on You;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">in the womb of my mother, You were my support;<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>support </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I sing Your praises always.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I have become an example for many,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">since You are my mighty refuge.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">My mouth is full of praise to You,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">glorifying You all day long.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Do not cast me off in old age;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">when my strength fails, do not forsake me!</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For my enemies talk against me;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">those who wait for me are of one mind,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">saying, “God has forsaken him;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">chase him and catch him,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for no one will save him!”</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">O God, be not far from me;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my God, hasten to my aid!</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Let my accusers perish in frustration;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">let those who seek my ruin be clothed in reproach and disgrace!</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">As for me, I will hope always,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and add to the many praises of You.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">My mouth tells of Your beneficence,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">of Your deliverance all day long,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">though I know not how to tell it.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I come with praise of Your mighty acts, O my Sovereign G<small>OD</small>;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I celebrate Your beneficence, Yours alone.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You have let me experience it, God, from my youth;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">until now I have proclaimed Your wondrous deeds,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and even in hoary old age do not forsake me, God,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">until I proclaim Your strength to the next generation,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Your mighty acts, to all who are to come,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Your beneficence, high as the heavens, O God,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You who have done great things;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">O God, who is Your peer!</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You who have made me undergo many troubles and misfortunes</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">will revive me again,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and raise me up from the depths of the earth.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You will grant me much greatness,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You will turn and comfort me.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Then I will acclaim You to the music of the lyre</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for Your faithfulness, O my God;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I will sing a hymn to You with a harp,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">O Holy One of Israel.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">My lips shall be jubilant, as I sing a hymn to You,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my whole being, which You have redeemed.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">All day long my tongue shall recite Your beneficent acts,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">how those who sought my ruin were frustrated and disgraced.</span>

Chapter 72

Of Solomon.<br><span class="poetry indentAll">O God, endow the king with Your judgments,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the king’s son with Your righteousness;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">that he may judge Your people rightly,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Your lowly ones, justly.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Let the mountains produce well-being for the people,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the hills, the reward of justice.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Let him champion the lowly among the people,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">deliver the needy folk,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and crush those who wrong them.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Let them fear You as long as the sun shines,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">while the moon lasts, generations on end.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Let him be like rain that falls on a mown field,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">like a downpour of rain on the ground,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">that the righteous may flourish in his time,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and well-being abound, till the moon is no more.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Let him rule from sea to sea,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">from the river to the ends of the earth.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Let desert-dwellers kneel before him,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and his enemies lick the dust.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Let kings of Tarshish and the islands pay tribute,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">kings of Sheba and Seba offer gifts.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Let all kings bow to him,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and all nations serve him.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For he saves the needy who cry out,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the lowly who have no helper.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">He cares about the poor and the needy;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">He brings the needy deliverance.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">He redeems them from fraud and lawlessness;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the shedding of their blood weighs heavily upon him.<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>the shedding of their blood weighs heavily upon him </b>Or “their life is precious in his sight.”</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">So let him live, and receive gold of Sheba;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">let prayers for him be said always,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">blessings on him invoked at all times.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Let abundant grain be in the land, to the tops of the mountains;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">let his crops thrive like the forest of Lebanon;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and let the people sprout up in towns like country grass.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">May his name be eternal;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">while the sun lasts, may his name endure;<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>Let abundant grain … endure </b>Meaning of some Heb. phrases in these verses uncertain.</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">let peoples invoke his blessedness upon themselves;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">let all nations count him happy.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Blessed is the E<small>TERNAL</small> God, God of Israel,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who alone does wondrous things;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Blessed is God’s glorious name forever;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">such glory fills the whole world.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Amen and Amen.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">End of the prayers of David son of Jesse.</span>

Chapter 73

A psalm of Asaph.<br><span class="poetry indentAll">God is truly good to Israel,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">to those whose heart is pure.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">As for me, my feet had almost strayed,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my steps were nearly led off course,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for I envied the wanton;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I saw the wicked at ease.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Death has no pangs for them;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">their body is healthy.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They have no part in human travail;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they are not afflicted like the rest of humankind.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">So pride adorns their necks,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">lawlessness enwraps them as a mantle.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Fat shuts out their eyes;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">their fancies are extravagant.<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>Fat … extravagant </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They scoff and plan evil;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">from their eminence they plan wrongdoing.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They set their mouths against heaven,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and their tongues range over the earth.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll"><sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote">Meaning of verse uncertain.</i> So they pound this people again and again,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">until they are drained of their very last tear.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Then they say, “How could God know?</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Is there knowledge with the Most High?”</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Such are the wicked;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">ever tranquil, they amass wealth.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">It was for nothing that I kept my heart pure</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and washed my hands in innocence,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">seeing that I have been constantly afflicted,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">that each morning brings new punishments.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Had I decided to say these things,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I should have been false to the circle of Your disciples.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">So I applied myself to understand this,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">but it seemed a hopeless task</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">till I entered God’s sanctuary</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and reflected on their fate.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You surround them with flattery;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You make them fall through blandishments.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">How suddenly are they ruined,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">wholly swept away by terrors.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">When You are aroused You despise their image,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">as one does a dream after waking, O my Sovereign.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">My mind was stripped of its reason,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my feelings were numbed.<sup class="footnote-marker">c</sup><i class="footnote"><b>my feelings were numbed </b>Lit. “I was pierced through in my kidneys.”</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I was a dolt, without knowledge;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I was brutish toward You.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Yet I was always with You,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You held my right hand;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You guided me by Your counsel</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and led me toward honor.<sup class="footnote-marker">d</sup><i class="footnote"><b>and led me toward honor </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain; in contrast to others “And afterward receive me with glory.”</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Whom else have I in heaven?</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">And having You, I want no one on earth.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">My body and mind fail;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">but God is the stay<sup class="footnote-marker">e</sup><i class="footnote"><b>stay </b>Lit. “rock.”</i> of my mind, my portion forever.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Those who keep far from You perish;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You annihilate all who are untrue to You.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">As for me, nearness to God is good;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I have made the Sovereign G<small>OD</small> my refuge,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">that I may recount all Your works.</span>

Chapter 74

A <i>maskil</i> of Asaph.<br><span class="poetry indentAll">Why, O God, do You forever reject us,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">do You fume in anger at the flock that You tend?</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Remember the community You made Yours long ago,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Your very own tribe that You redeemed,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Mount Zion, where You dwell.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Bestir Yourself<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>Bestir Yourself </b>Lit. “Lift up Your feet.”</i> because of the perpetual tumult,<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>perpetual tumult </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">all the outrages of the enemy in the sanctuary.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Your foes roar inside Your meeting-place;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they take their signs for true signs.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">It is like those who wield axes</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">against a gnarled tree;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">with hatchet and pike</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they hacked away at its carved work.<sup class="footnote-marker">c</sup><i class="footnote"><b>It is like … carved work </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They made Your sanctuary go up in flames;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they brought low in dishonor the dwelling-place of Your presence.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They resolved, “Let us destroy them altogether!”</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">They burned all God’s tabernacles in the land.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">No signs appear for us;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">there is no longer any prophet;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">no one among us knows for how long.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Till when, O God, will the foe blaspheme,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">will the enemy forever revile Your name?</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Why do You hold back Your hand, Your right hand?</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Draw it out of Your bosom!<sup class="footnote-marker">d</sup><i class="footnote"><b>Draw it out of Your bosom </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">O God, my Sovereign from of old,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who brings deliverance throughout the land;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">it was You who drove back the sea with Your might,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who smashed the heads of the monsters in the waters;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">it was You who crushed the heads of Leviathan,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who left it as food for the denizens of the desert;<sup class="footnote-marker">e</sup><i class="footnote"><b>the denizens of the desert </b>Or “seafaring peoples”; meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">it was You who released springs and torrents,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who made mighty rivers run dry;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the day is Yours, the night also;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">it was You who set in place the orb of the sun;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You fixed all the boundaries of the earth;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">summer and winter—You made them.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Be mindful of how the enemy blasphemes G<small>OD</small>,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">how base people revile Your name.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Do not deliver Your dove to the wild beast;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">do not ignore forever the band of Your lowly ones.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Look to the covenant!</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">For the dark places of the land are full of the haunts of lawlessness.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Let not the downtrodden turn away disappointed;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">let the poor and needy praise Your name.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Rise, O God, champion Your cause;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">be mindful that You are blasphemed by scoundrels all day long.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Do not ignore the shouts of Your foes,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the din of Your adversaries that ascends all the time.</span>

Chapter 75

For the leader; <i>al tashḥeth</i>.A psalm of Asaph, a song.
<span class="poetry indentAll">We praise You, O God;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">we praise You;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Your presence is near;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">people tell of Your wondrous deeds.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">“At the time I choose,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I will give judgment equitably.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Earth and all its inhabitants dissolve;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">it is I who keep its pillars firm. <i>   Selah.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">To the wanton I say, ‘Do not be wanton!’</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">to the wicked, ‘Do not lift up your horns!’”</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Do not lift your horns up high</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">in vainglorious bluster.<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>in vainglorious bluster </b>Lit. “with arrogant neck you speak.”</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For exaltation comes not from the east</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">or from the west or the wilderness;<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>wilderness </b>Reading <i>midbār</i> (with <i>qamaṣ</i>, not <i>pataḥ</i>), as in many mss.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for God it is who gives judgment—</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">bringing down one and lifting up another.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">There is a cup in G<small>OD</small>’s hand</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">with foaming wine fully mixed;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">from this [God] pours;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">all the wicked of the earth drink,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">draining it to the very dregs.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">As for me, I will declare forever,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I will sing a hymn to the God of Jacob.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">“All the horns of the wicked I will cut;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">but the horns of the righteous shall be lifted up.”</span>

Chapter 76

For the leader; with instrumental music.A psalm of Asaph, a song.
<span class="poetry indentAll">God is known in Judah,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">God’s name is great in Israel;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Salem became an abode;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Zion, the divine den.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">There [God] broke the fiery arrows of the bow,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the shield and the sword of war. <i>   Selah.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You were resplendent,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">glorious, on the mountains of prey.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">The stout-hearted were despoiled;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they were in a stupor;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the bravest of soldiers could not lift a hand.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">At Your blast, O God of Jacob,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">horse and chariot lay stunned.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">O You! You are awesome!</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Who can withstand You</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">when You are enraged?</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">In heaven You pronounced sentence;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the earth was numbed with fright</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">as God rose to execute judgment,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">to deliver all the lowly of the earth. <i>   Selah.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll"><sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote">Meaning of verse uncertain.</i> Even the fiercest among humans shall acknowledge You,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">when You gird on the last bit of fury.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Make vows and pay them to the E<small>TERNAL</small> your God;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">those all around shall bring tribute to the Awesome One—<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>all around … Awesome One </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who curbs the spirit of princes,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">inspires awe in the kings of the earth.</span>

Chapter 77

For the leader; on <i>Jeduthun</i>.Of Asaph. A psalm.
<span class="poetry indentAll">I cry aloud to God;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I cry to God that I may be heard.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">In my time of distress I turn to my Sovereign,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">with my hand [uplifted];</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">[my eyes] flow all night without respite;<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>with my hand … without respite </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I will not be comforted.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I call God to mind, I moan,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I complain, my spirit fails. <i>   Selah.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You have held my eyelids open;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I am overwrought, I cannot speak.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">My thoughts turn to days of old,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">to years long past.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I recall at night their jibes at me;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I commune with myself;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my spirit inquires,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">“Will my Sovereign reject forever</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and never again show favor?</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Has such faithfulness disappeared forever?</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Will those promises be unfulfilled for all time?</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Has God forgotten how to pity?</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Has God’s compassion been stifled in anger?” <i>   Selah.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">And I said, “It is my fault</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">that the right hand of the Most High has changed.”<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>It is my fault / … changed </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I recall the deeds of Yah;<sup class="footnote-marker">c</sup><i class="footnote"><b>Yah </b>See note at <a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 68:5" href="Psalms.68.5">68.5</a>.</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">yes, I recall Your wonders of old;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I recount all Your works;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I speak of Your acts.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">O God, Your ways are holiness;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">what god is as great as God?</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You are the God who works wonders;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You have manifested Your strength among the peoples.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">By Your arm You redeemed Your people,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the children of Jacob and Joseph. <i>   Selah.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">The waters saw You, O God,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the waters saw You and were convulsed;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the very deep quaked as well.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Clouds streamed water;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the heavens rumbled;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Your arrows flew about;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Your thunder rumbled like wheels;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">lightning lit up the world;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the earth quaked and trembled.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Your way was through the sea,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Your path, through the mighty waters;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Your tracks could not be seen.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You led Your people like a flock</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">in the care of Moses and Aaron.</span>

Chapter 78

A <i>maskil</i> of Asaph.<br><span class="poetry indentAll">Give ear, my people, to my teaching,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">turn your ear to what I say.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I will expound a theme,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">hold forth on the lessons of the past—</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">things we have heard and known,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">that our ancestors have told us.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">We will not withhold them from their children,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">telling the coming generation</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the praises of G<small>OD</small> and of divine might,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and the wonders performed.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">[God] established a decree in Jacob,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">ordained a teaching in Israel,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">charging our ancestors</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">to make them known to their children,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">that a future generation might know—</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">children yet to be born—</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and in turn tell their children</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">that they might put their confidence in God,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and not forget God’s great deeds,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">but observe the commandments,</span>
