<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and not be like their ancestors,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">a wayward and defiant generation,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">a generation whose heart was inconstant,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">whose spirit was not true to God.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Like the Ephraimite archers</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who played false in the day of battle,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they did not keep God’s covenant,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they refused to follow divine instruction;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they forgot what was done for them</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and the wonders they were shown.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">[God] performed marvels in the sight of their ancestors,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">in the land of Egypt, the plain of Zoan.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">[God] split the sea and took them through it—</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">making the waters stand like a wall.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">[God] led them with a cloud by day,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and throughout the night by the light of fire.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">[God] split rocks in the wilderness</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and gave them drink as if from the great deep.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">[God] brought forth streams from a rock</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and made them flow down like a river.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">But they went on sinning,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">defying the Most High in the parched land.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">To test God was in their mind</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">when they demanded food for themselves.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They spoke against God, saying,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">“Can God spread a feast in the wilderness?</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">True, [God]<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>[God] </b>I.e., Moses, acting as God’s agent; cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 17:5-6" href="Exodus.17.5-6">Exod. 17.5–6</a>.</i> struck the rock and waters flowed,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">streams gushed forth;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">but can [God] provide bread</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and supply meat for this people?”</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">
G<small>OD</small>
 heard and then raged;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">fire broke out against Jacob,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">anger flared up at Israel,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">because they did not put their trust in God,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">did not rely on divine deliverance.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">So [God] commanded the skies above,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">opened the doors of heaven</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and rained manna upon them for food,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">giving them heavenly grain.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Each person ate a hero’s meal;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they were sent provision in plenty.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">[God] set the east wind moving in heaven,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and drove the south wind mightily.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">[God] rained meat on them like dust,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">winged birds like the sands of the sea,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">making them come down inside God’s camp,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">around the divine dwelling-place.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They ate till they were sated;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they were given what they craved.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They had not yet wearied of what they craved,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the food was still in their mouths</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">when God’s anger flared up at them.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">[God] slew their sturdiest,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">struck down the youth of Israel.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Nonetheless, they went on sinning</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and had no faith in God’s wonders.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Their days were made to end in futility,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">their years in sudden death.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">When stricken,<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>stricken </b>Lit. “killed.”</i> they returned,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and sought God once again.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They remembered that God was their rock,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">God Most High, their Redeemer.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Yet they deceived [God] with their speech,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and lied with their words.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Their hearts were inconstant;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they were untrue to the covenant.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">But [God], being merciful, forgave iniquity</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and would not destroy—</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">restraining wrath time and again</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and not giving full vent to such fury—</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">remembering that they were but flesh,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">a passing breath that does not return.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">How often did they act defiantly in the wilderness,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">then cause grief in the wasteland!</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Again and again they tested God,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">vexed<sup class="footnote-marker">c</sup><i class="footnote"><b>vexed </b>Or “set a limit to.”</i> the Holy One of Israel.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They did not remember God’s strength,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">or the day they were redeemed from the foe;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">how [God] displayed signs in Egypt,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and wonders in the plain of Zoan.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">[God first] turned their rivers into blood—</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">making their waters undrinkable;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">then inflicted upon them swarms of insects to devour them,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">frogs to destroy them;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">then gave their crops over to grubs,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">their produce to locusts;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">then killed their vines with hail,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">their sycamores with frost;<sup class="footnote-marker">d</sup><i class="footnote"><b>with frost </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">then gave their beasts over to hail,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">their cattle to lightning bolts;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">and inflicted a burning anger upon them—</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">wrath, indignation, trouble,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">a band of deadly messengers.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">[God] cleared a path for that anger,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and did not stop short of slaying them,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">but gave them over to pestilence.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">[God] struck every [male] first-born in Egypt,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the first fruits of their vigor in the tents of Ham.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">God’s own people were set moving like sheep,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">driven like a flock in the wilderness.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">[God] led them in safety; they were unafraid;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">as for their enemies, the sea covered them.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">[God] brought them to the holy realm,<sup class="footnote-marker">e</sup><i class="footnote"><b>realm </b>Or “hill” with Septuagint and Saadia.</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the mountain God’s right hand had acquired.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">[God] expelled nations before them,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">settled the tribes of Israel in their tents,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">allotting them their portion by the line.<sup class="footnote-marker">f</sup><i class="footnote"><b>settled the tribes of Israel in their tents, / allotting them their portion by the line </b>Clauses transposed for clarity.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Yet they defiantly tested God Most High,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and did not observe divine decrees.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They fell away, disloyal like their ancestors;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they played false like a treacherous bow.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They provoked anger with their high places;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they kindled wrath with their idols.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">God heard it and was enraged—</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">utterly rejecting Israel.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">[God] forsook the tabernacle of Shiloh,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the tent that had been set among mortals.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">God’s might<sup class="footnote-marker">g</sup><i class="footnote"><b>God’s might </b>I.e., the Ark; cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 132:8" href="Psalms.132.8">Ps. 132.8</a>.</i> was allowed to go into captivity,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">that glory into the hands of the foe.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">This people was given over to the sword;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">God’s very own the object of rage.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Fire consumed their young men,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and their maidens remained unwed.<sup class="footnote-marker">h</sup><i class="footnote"><b>remained unwed </b>Lit. “had no nuptial song.”</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Their priests fell by the sword,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and their widows could not weep.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">The Sovereign awoke as from sleep—</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">like a warrior shaking off<sup class="footnote-marker">i</sup><i class="footnote"><b>shaking off </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> wine—</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and beat back all foes,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">dealing them lasting disgrace.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">[God] rejected the clan of Joseph</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and did not choose the tribe of Ephraim.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">[God] did choose the tribe of Judah—</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Mount Zion, which was beloved—</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">building the Sanctuary like the heavens,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">like the earth that [God] established forever.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">David, God’s servant, was chosen,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and taken from the sheepfolds.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">He was brought from minding the nursing ewes</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">to tend the people of Jacob, Israel, God’s very own.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">He tended them with blameless heart;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">with skillful hands he led them.</span>

Chapter 79

A psalm of Asaph.<br><span class="poetry indentAll">O God, heathens have entered Your domain,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">defiled Your holy temple,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and turned Jerusalem into ruins.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They have left Your servants’ corpses</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">as food for the fowl of heaven,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and the flesh of Your faithful for the wild beasts.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Their blood was shed like water around Jerusalem,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">with none to bury them.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">We have become the butt of our neighbors,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the scorn and derision of those around us.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">How long, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, will You be angry forever,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">will Your indignation blaze like fire?</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Pour out Your fury on the nations that do not know You,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">upon the kingdoms that do not invoke Your name,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for they have devoured Jacob</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and desolated his home.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Do not hold our former iniquities against us;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">let Your compassion come swiftly toward us,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for we have sunk very low.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Help us, O God, our deliverer,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for the sake of the glory of Your name.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Save us and forgive our sin,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for the sake of Your name.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Let the nations not say, “Where is their God?”</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Before our eyes let it be known among the nations</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">that You avenge the spilled blood of Your servants.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Let the groans of the prisoners reach You;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">reprieve those condemned to death,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">as befits Your great strength.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Pay back our neighbors sevenfold</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for the abuse they have flung at You, O Sovereign.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Then we, Your people,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the flock You shepherd,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">shall glorify You forever;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for all time we shall tell Your praises.</span>

Chapter 80

For the leader; on <i>shoshannim</i>, <i>eduth</i>. Of Asaph. A psalm.
<span class="poetry indentAll">Give ear, O shepherd of Israel</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who leads Joseph like a flock!</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Appear, You who are enthroned on the cherubim,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">at the head of Ephraim, Benjamin, and Manasseh!</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Rouse Your might and come to our help!</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Restore us, O God;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">show Your favor that we may be delivered.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, God of hosts,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">how long will You be wrathful</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">toward the prayers of Your people?</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You have fed them tears as their daily bread,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">made them drink great measures of tears.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You set us at strife with our neighbors;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">our enemies mock us at will.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">O God of hosts, restore us;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">show Your favor that we may be delivered.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You plucked up a vine from Egypt;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You expelled nations and planted it.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You cleared a place for it;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">it took deep root and filled the land.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">The mountains were covered by its shade,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">mighty cedars by its boughs.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Its branches reached the sea,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">its shoots, the river.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Why did You breach its wall</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">so that every passerby plucks its fruit,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">wild boars gnaw at it,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and creatures of the field feed on it?</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">O God of hosts, turn again,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">look down from heaven and see;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">take note of that vine,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the stock planted by Your right hand,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the stem<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>stem </b>Lit. “son.”</i> you have taken as Your own.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For it is burned by fire and cut down,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">perishing before Your angry blast.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Grant Your help<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>help </b>Lit. “hand.”</i> to the one at Your right hand,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the mortal You have taken as Your own.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">We will not turn away from You;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">preserve our life that we may invoke Your name.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, God of hosts, restore us;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">show Your favor that we may be delivered.</span>

Chapter 81

For the leader; on the <i>gittith</i>. Of Asaph.
<span class="poetry indentAll">Sing joyously to God, our strength;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">raise a shout for the God of Jacob.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Take up the song,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">sound the hand-drum,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the melodious lyre and harp.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Blow the horn on the new moon,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">on the full moon for our feast day.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For it is a law for Israel,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">a ruling of the God of Jacob—</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">imposed as a decree upon Joseph</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">when he went forth from<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>he went forth from </b>Or “[God] went forth against.”</i> the land of Egypt;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I heard a language that I knew not.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">“I relieved his shoulder of the burden,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">his hands were freed from the basket.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">In distress you called and I rescued you;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I answered you from the secret place of thunder<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>secret place of thunder </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I tested you at the Waters of Meribah. <i>   Selah.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Hear, My people, and I will admonish you;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Israel, if you would but listen to Me!</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You shall have no foreign god,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">you shall not bow to an alien god.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I the E<small>TERNAL</small> am your God</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who brought you out of the land of Egypt;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">open your mouth wide and I will fill it.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">But My people would not listen to Me,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Israel would not obey Me.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">So I let them go after their willful heart</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">that they might follow their own devices.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">If only My people would listen to Me,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">if Israel would follow My paths,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">then would I subdue their enemies at once,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">strike their foes again and again.”</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Those who hate G<small>OD</small> shall cower;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">their doom shall be eternal.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">[God] fed Israel<sup class="footnote-marker">c</sup><i class="footnote"><b>Israel </b>Heb. “him.”</i> the finest wheat;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">“I sated you with honey from the rock.”</span>

Chapter 82

A psalm of Asaph.<br><span class="poetry indentAll">God stands in the divine assembly,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">pronouncing judgment among the divine beings.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">How long will you judge perversely,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">showing favor to the wicked? <i>   Selah.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Judge the wretched and the orphan,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">vindicate the lowly and the poor,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">rescue the wretched and the needy;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">save them from the hand of the wicked.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They neither know nor understand,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they go about in darkness;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">all the foundations of the earth totter.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I had taken you for divine beings,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">attendants<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>attendants </b>Lit. “sons.”</i> of the Most High, all of you;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">but you shall die as mortals do,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">fall like any prince.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Arise, O God, judge the earth,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for all the nations are Your possession.</span>

Chapter 83

A song, a psalm of Asaph.
<span class="poetry indentAll">O God, do not be silent;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">do not hold aloof;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">do not be quiet, O God!</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For Your enemies rage,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Your foes assert themselves.<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>assert themselves </b>Lit. “lift up the head.”</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They plot craftily against Your people,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">take counsel against Your treasured ones.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They say, “Let us wipe them out as a nation;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Israel’s name will be mentioned no more.”</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Unanimous in their counsel</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they have made an alliance against You—</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the clans of Edom and the Ishmaelites,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Moab and the Hagrites,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Gebal, Ammon, and Amalek,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Philistia with the inhabitants of Tyre;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Assyria too joins forces with them;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they give support to the descendants of Lot.<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>the descendants of Lot </b>I.e., the Moabites and the Ammonites; cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Genesis 19:36-38" href="Genesis.19.36-38">Gen. 19.36–38</a>.</i> <i>   Selah.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Deal with them as You did with Midian,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">with Sisera, with Jabin,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">at the brook Kishon—</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who were destroyed at En-dor,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who became dung for the field.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Treat their nobles like Oreb and Zeeb,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">all their princes like Zebah and Zalmunna,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who said, “Let us take the meadows of God as our possession.”</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">O my God, make them like thistledown,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">like stubble driven by the wind.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">As a fire burns a forest,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">as flames scorch the hills,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">pursue them with Your tempest,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">terrify them with Your storm.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Cover<sup class="footnote-marker">c</sup><i class="footnote"><b>Cover </b>Lit. “Fill.”</i> their faces with shame</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">so that they seek Your name, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">May they be frustrated and terrified,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">disgraced and doomed forever.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">May they know</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">that Your name, Yours alone, is G<small>OD</small>,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">supreme over all the earth.</span>

Chapter 84

For the leader; on the <i>gittith</i>. Of the Korahites. A psalm.
<span class="poetry indentAll">How lovely is Your dwelling-place,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">O G<small>OD</small> of Hosts.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I long, I yearn for the courts of the E<small>TERNAL</small> One;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my body and soul shout for joy to the living God.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Even the sparrow has found a home,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and the swallow a nest for herself</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">in which to set her young,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">near Your altar, O G<small>OD</small> of Hosts,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my monarch and my God.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Happy are those who dwell in Your house;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they forever praise You. <i>   Selah.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Happy are those who find refuge in You,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">whose mind is on the [pilgrim] highways.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They pass through the Valley of Baca,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">regarding it as a place of springs,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">as if the early rain had covered it with blessing.<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>regarding it … blessing </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They go from rampart to rampart,<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>rampart to rampart </b>In contrast to others “strength to strength.”</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">appearing before God in Zion.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">O E<small>TERNAL</small> God of hosts,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">hear my prayer;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">give ear, O God of Jacob. <i>   Selah.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">O God, behold our shield,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">look upon the face of Your anointed.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Better one day in Your courts than a thousand [anywhere else];</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I would rather stand at the threshold of God’s house</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">than dwell in the tents of the wicked.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For the E<small>TERNAL</small> God is sun<sup class="footnote-marker">c</sup><i class="footnote"><b>sun </b>Or “bulwark,” with Targum; cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Isaiah 54:12" href="Isaiah.54.12">Isa. 54.12</a>.</i> and shield;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble"> 
G<small>OD</small>
 bestows grace and glory,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and does not withhold bounty from those who live without blame.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">O G<small>OD</small> of Hosts,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">happy is the one who trusts in You.</span>

Chapter 85

For the leader. Of the Korahites. A psalm.
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, You will favor<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>will favor </b>Or “have favored.”</i> Your land,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">restore<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>restore </b>Or “have restored.”</i> Jacob’s fortune;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You will forgive<sup class="footnote-marker">c</sup><i class="footnote"><b>will forgive </b>Or “have forgiven.”</i> Your people’s iniquity,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">pardon<sup class="footnote-marker">d</sup><i class="footnote"><b>pardon </b>Or “have pardoned.”</i> all their sins; <i>   selah</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You will withdraw<sup class="footnote-marker">e</sup><i class="footnote"><b>will withdraw </b>Or “have withdrawn.”</i> all Your anger,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">turn<sup class="footnote-marker">f</sup><i class="footnote"><b>turn </b>Or “have turned.”</i> away from Your rage.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Turn again, O God, our helper,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">revoke Your displeasure with us.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Will You be angry with us forever,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">prolong Your wrath for all generations?</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Surely You will revive us again,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">so that Your people may rejoice in You.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Show us, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, Your faithfulness;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">grant us Your deliverance.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Let me hear what God, the E<small>TERNAL</small>, will speak,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">as a promise of well-being to the faithful ones—this people;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">may they not turn to folly.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Help is very near those who show reverence,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">to make God’s glory dwell in our land.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Faithfulness and truth meet;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">justice and well-being kiss.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Truth springs up from the earth;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">justice looks down from heaven.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">
G<small>OD</small>
 also bestows bounty;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">our land yields its produce.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Justice walks in front</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">as [God] sets out on the way.</span>

Chapter 86

A prayer of David.<br><span class="poetry indentAll">Incline Your ear, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">answer me,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for I am poor and needy.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Preserve my life, for I am steadfast;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">O You, my God,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">deliver Your servant who trusts in You.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Have mercy on me, O my Sovereign,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for I call to You all day long;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">bring joy to Your servant’s life,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for on You, my Sovereign, I set my hope.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For You, my Sovereign, are good and forgiving,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">abounding in steadfast love to all who call on You.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Give ear, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, to my prayer;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">heed my plea for mercy.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">In my time of trouble I call You,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for You will answer me.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">There is none like You among the gods, O my Sovereign,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and there are no deeds like Yours.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">All the nations You have made</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">will come to bow down before You, O my Sovereign,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and they will pay honor to Your name.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For You are great and perform wonders;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You alone are God.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Teach me Your way, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I will walk in Your truth;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">let my heart be undivided in reverence for Your name.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I will praise You, O my Sovereign, my God, with all my heart</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and pay honor to Your name forever.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For Your steadfast love toward me is great;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You have saved me from the depths of Sheol.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">O God, arrogant people have risen against me;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">a ruthless band seeks my life;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they are not mindful of You.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">But You, O my Sovereign, are a God</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">compassionate and merciful,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">slow to anger, abounding in steadfast love and faithfulness.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Turn to me and have mercy on me;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">grant Your strength to Your servant</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and deliver the son of Your maidservant.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Show me a sign of Your favor,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">that my enemies may see and be frustrated</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">because You, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, have given me aid and comfort.</span>

Chapter 87

<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote">The meaning of many passages in this psalm is uncertain.</i> Of the Korahites. A psalm. A song.<br><span class="poetry indentAll">The temple’s<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>The temple’s </b>Heb. “Its.”</i> foundation on the holy mountains—</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the gates of Zion—</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">
G<small>OD</small>
 loves</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">more than all the dwellings of Jacob.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Glorious things are spoken of you,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">O city of God. <i>   Selah.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I mention Rahab<sup class="footnote-marker">c</sup><i class="footnote"><b>Rahab </b>A primeval monster; here, a poetic term for Egypt; cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Isaiah 30:7" href="Isaiah.30.7">Isa. 30.7</a>.</i> and Babylon among those who acknowledge Me;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Philistia, and Tyre, and Cush—each was born there.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Indeed, it shall be said of Zion,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">“They<sup class="footnote-marker">d</sup><i class="footnote"><b>They </b>I.e., the nations of v. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 87:4" href="Psalms.87.4">4</a>, or their members.</i> were all born there.”</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">It is the Most High who will preserve it.<sup class="footnote-marker">e</sup><i class="footnote"><b>It is the Most High who will preserve it </b>Or “[God] will preserve it supreme.”</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">
G<small>OD</small>
 will inscribe in the register of peoples</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">that each was born there. <i>   Selah.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Singers and dancers alike [will say]:</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">“All my roots<sup class="footnote-marker">f</sup><i class="footnote"><b>roots </b>Lit. “sources.”</i> are in You.”</span>

Chapter 88

A song. A psalm of the Korahites. For the leader; <i>maḥalath leannoth</i>.<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b><i>maḥalath leannoth</i> </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> A <i>maskil</i> of Heman the Ezrahite.
<span class="poetry indentAll">O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, God of my deliverance,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">when I cry out in the night<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>when I cry out in the night </b>Or “by day I cry out [and] by night.”</i> before You,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">let my prayer reach You;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">incline Your ear to my cry.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For I am sated with misfortune;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I am at the brink of Sheol.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I am numbered with those who go down to the Pit;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I am like someone helpless<sup class="footnote-marker">c</sup><i class="footnote"><b>like someone helpless </b>Or “like a virile man who is helpless.”</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">abandoned<sup class="footnote-marker">d</sup><i class="footnote"><b>abandoned </b>Lit. “released.”</i> among the dead,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">like bodies lying in the grave</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">of whom You are mindful no more,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and who are cut off from Your care.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You have put me at the bottom of the Pit,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">in the darkest places, in the depths.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Your fury lies heavy upon me;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You afflict me with all Your breakers. <i>   Selah.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You make my companions shun me;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You make me abhorrent to them;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I am shut in and do not go out.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">My eyes pine away from affliction;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I call to You, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, each day;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I stretch out my hands to You.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Do You work wonders for the dead?</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Do the shades rise to praise You? <i>   Selah.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Is Your faithful care recounted in the grave,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Your constancy in the place of perdition?</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Are Your wonders made known in the netherworld,<sup class="footnote-marker">e</sup><i class="footnote"><b>netherworld </b>Lit. “darkness.”</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Your beneficent deeds in the land of oblivion?</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">As for me, I cry out to You, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">each morning my prayer greets You.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Why, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, do You reject me,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">do You hide Your face from me?</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">From my youth I have been afflicted</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and near death;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I suffer Your terrors wherever I turn.<sup class="footnote-marker">f</sup><i class="footnote"><b>wherever I turn </b>Following Saadia; meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Your fury overwhelms me;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Your terrors destroy me.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They swirl about me like water all day long;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they encircle me on every side.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You have put friend and neighbor far from me</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and my companions out of my sight.<sup class="footnote-marker">g</sup><i class="footnote"><b>out of my sight </b>Lit. “into darkness.”</i> </span>

Chapter 89

A <i>maskil</i> of Ethan the Ezrahite.
<span class="poetry indentAll">I will sing of G<small>OD</small>’s steadfast love forever;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">to all generations I will proclaim Your faithfulness with my mouth.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I declare, “Your steadfast love is confirmed forever;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">there in the heavens You establish Your faithfulness.”</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">“I have made a covenant with My chosen one;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I have sworn to My servant David:</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I will establish your offspring forever,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I will confirm your throne for all generations.” <i>   Selah.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Your wonders, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, are praised by the heavens,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Your faithfulness, too, in the assembly of holy beings.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For who in the skies can equal G<small>OD</small>,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">can compare with G<small>OD</small> among the divine beings,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">a God greatly dreaded in the council of holy beings,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">held in awe by those all around?</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, God of hosts,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who is mighty like You, O Yah?<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>Yah </b>See note at <a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 68:5" href="Psalms.68.5">68.5</a>.</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Your faithfulness surrounds You;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You rule the swelling of the sea;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">when its waves surge, You still them.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You crushed Rahab; he was like a corpse;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">with Your powerful arm You scattered Your enemies.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">The heaven is Yours,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the earth too;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the world and all it holds—</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You established them.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">North and south—</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You created them;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Tabor and Hermon sing forth Your name.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Yours is an arm endowed with might;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Your hand is strong;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Your right hand, exalted.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Righteousness and justice are the base of Your throne;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">steadfast love and faithfulness stand before You.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Happy is the people who know the joyful shout;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, they walk in the light of Your presence.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They rejoice in Your name all day long;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they are exalted through Your righteousness.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For You are their strength in which they glory;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">our horn is exalted through Your favor.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Truly our shield is of G<small>OD</small>,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">our monarch, of the Holy One of Israel.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Then<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>Then </b>Referring to vv. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 89:4-5" href="Psalms.89.4-5">4–5</a>; cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="II Samuel 7:1-17" href="II_Samuel.7.1-17">2 Sam. 7.1–17</a>.</i> You spoke to Your faithful ones in a vision</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and said, “I have conferred power upon a warrior;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I have exalted one chosen out of the people.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I have found David, My servant;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">anointed him with My sacred oil.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">My hand shall be constantly with him,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and My arm shall strengthen him.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">No enemy shall oppress him,<sup class="footnote-marker">c</sup><i class="footnote"><b>oppress him </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">no one vile afflict him.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I will crush his adversaries before him;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I will strike down those who hate him.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">My faithfulness and steadfast love shall be with him;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">his horn shall be exalted through My name.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I will set his hand upon the sea,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">his right hand upon the rivers.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">He shall say to Me,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">‘You are my father,<sup class="footnote-marker">d</sup><i class="footnote"><b>father </b>I.e., with the authority to declare which offspring (= nation’s king) is the favored one.</i> my God, the rock of my deliverance.’</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I will appoint him first-born,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">highest of the kings of the earth.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I will maintain My steadfast love for him always;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">My covenant with him shall endure.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I will establish his line forever,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">his throne, as long as the heavens last.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">If his sons forsake My Teaching</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and do not live by My rules;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">if they violate My laws,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and do not observe My commands,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I will punish their transgression with the rod,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">their iniquity with plagues.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">But I will not take away My steadfast love from him;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I will not betray My faithfulness.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I will not violate My covenant,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">or change what I have uttered.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I have sworn by My holiness, once and for all;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I will not be false to David.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">His line shall continue forever,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">his throne, as the sun before Me,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">as the moon, established forever,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">an enduring witness in the sky.” <i>   Selah.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Yet You have rejected, spurned,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and become enraged at Your anointed.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You have repudiated the covenant with Your servant;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You have dragged his dignity in the dust.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You have breached all his defenses,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">shattered his strongholds.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">All who pass by plunder him;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">he has become the butt of his neighbors.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You have exalted the right hand of his adversaries,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and made all his enemies rejoice.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You have turned back the blade of his sword,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and have not sustained him in battle.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You have brought his splendor<sup class="footnote-marker">e</sup><i class="footnote"><b>his splendor </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> to an end</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and have hurled his throne to the ground.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You have cut short the days of his youth;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You have covered him with shame. <i>   Selah.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">How long, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One; will You forever hide Your face,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">will Your fury blaze like fire?</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">O remember how short my life is;<sup class="footnote-marker">f</sup><i class="footnote"><b>how short my life is </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">why should You have created every person in vain?</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Who<sup class="footnote-marker">g</sup><i class="footnote"><b>Who </b>Or “What virile man.”</i> can live and not see death,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">can escape the clutches of Sheol? <i>   Selah.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">O my Sovereign, where is Your steadfast love of old</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">that You swore to David in Your faithfulness?</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Remember, O my Sovereign, the abuse flung at Your servants</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">that I have borne in my bosom [from] many peoples,<sup class="footnote-marker">h</sup><i class="footnote"><b>that I have borne in my bosom [from] many peoples </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">how Your enemies, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, have flung abuse,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">abuse at Your anointed at every step.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Blessed is G<small>OD</small> forever;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Amen and Amen.</span>

Chapter 90

A prayer of Moses, the agent of God.<br><span class="poetry indentAll">O my Sovereign, You have been our refuge in every generation.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Before the mountains came into being,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">before You brought forth the earth and the world,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">from eternity to eternity You are God.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You return humans to dust;<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>dust </b>Or “contrition.”</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You decreed, “Return, you mortals!”</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For in Your sight a thousand years</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">are like yesterday that has passed,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">like a watch of the night.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You engulf mortals<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>mortals </b>Heb. “them.”</i> in sleep;<sup class="footnote-marker">c</sup><i class="footnote"><b>For in Your sight … sleep </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">at daybreak they are like grass that renews itself;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">at daybreak it flourishes anew;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">by dusk it withers and dries up.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">So we are consumed by Your anger,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">terror-struck by Your fury.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You have set our iniquities before You,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">our hidden sins in the light of Your face.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">All our days pass away in Your wrath;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">we spend our years like a sigh.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">The span of our life is seventy years,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">or, given the strength, eighty years;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">but the best of them<sup class="footnote-marker">d</sup><i class="footnote"><b>best of them </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> are trouble and sorrow.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">They pass by speedily, and we are in darkness.<sup class="footnote-marker">e</sup><i class="footnote"><b>are in darkness </b>Or “fly away.”</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Who can know Your furious anger?</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Your wrath matches the fear of You.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Teach us to count our days rightly,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">that we may obtain a wise heart.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Turn, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One!</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">How long?</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Show mercy to Your servants.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Satisfy us at daybreak with Your steadfast love</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">that we may sing for joy all our days.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Give us joy for as long as You have afflicted us,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for the years we have suffered misfortune.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Let Your deeds be seen by Your servants,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Your glory by their children.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">May the favor of my Sovereign, our God, be upon us;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">let the work of our hands prosper,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">O prosper the work of our hands!</span>

Chapter 91

<span class="poetry indentAll">O you who dwell in the shelter of the Most High</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and abide in the protection of Shaddai—</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I say of G<small>OD</small>, my refuge and stronghold,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my God in whom I trust,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">that you will be saved from the fowler’s trap,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">from the destructive plague.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">With pinions you will be covered;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">you will find refuge under God’s wings—</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">whose fidelity is an encircling shield.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You need not fear the terror by night,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">or the arrow that flies by day,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the plague that stalks in the darkness,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">or the scourge that ravages at noon.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">A thousand may fall at your left side,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">ten thousand at your right,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">but it shall not reach you.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You will see it with your eyes,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">you will witness the punishment of the wicked.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Because you took G<small>OD</small>—my refuge,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the Most High—as your haven,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">no harm will befall you,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">no disease touch your tent.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For God’s angels will be ordered</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">to guard you wherever you go.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They will carry you in their hands</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">lest you hurt your foot on a stone.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You will tread on cubs and vipers;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">you will trample lions and asps.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">“Because such people are devoted to Me, I will deliver them;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I will keep them safe, for they know My name.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">When they call on Me, I will answer them;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I will be with them in distress;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I will rescue them and make them honored;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I will let them live to a ripe old age,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and show them My salvation.”</span>

Chapter 92

A psalm. A song; for the sabbath day.
<span class="poetry indentAll">It is good to praise G<small>OD</small>,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">to sing hymns to Your name, O Most High,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">To proclaim Your steadfast love at daybreak,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Your faithfulness each night</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">With a ten-stringed harp,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">with voice and lyre together.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You have gladdened me by Your deeds, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I shout for joy at Your handiwork.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">How great are Your works, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">how very subtle<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>subtle </b>Or “profound.”</i> Your designs!</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">A brute cannot know,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">a fool cannot understand this:</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">though the wicked sprout like grass,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">though all evildoers blossom,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">it is only that they may be destroyed forever.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">But You are exalted, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, for all time.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Surely, Your enemies, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">surely, Your enemies perish;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">all evildoers are scattered.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You raise my horn high like that of a wild ox;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I am soaked in freshening oil.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I shall see the defeat of my watchful foes,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">hear of the downfall of the wicked who beset me.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">The righteous bloom like a date-palm;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they thrive like a cedar in Lebanon;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">planted in the house of G<small>OD</small>,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they flourish in the courts of our God.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">In old age they still produce fruit;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they are full of sap and freshness—</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">attesting that G<small>OD</small> is upright,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my rock, in whom there is no wrong.</span>

Chapter 93

<span class="poetry indentAll">
G<small>OD</small>
 is sovereign,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and robed in grandeur;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble"> 
G<small>OD</small>
 is robed,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and girded with strength.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">The world stands firm;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">it cannot be shaken.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Your throne stands firm from of old;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">from eternity You have existed.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">The ocean sounds, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the ocean sounds its thunder,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the ocean sounds its pounding.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Above the thunder of the mighty waters,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">more majestic than the breakers of the sea</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">is G<small>OD</small>, majestic on high.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Your decrees are indeed enduring;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">holiness befits Your house,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, for all times.</span>

Chapter 94

<span class="poetry indentAll">God of retribution, E<small>TERNAL</small> One,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">God of retribution, appear!</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Rise up, judge of the earth,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">give the arrogant their deserts!</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">How long shall the wicked, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">how long shall the wicked exult,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">shall they utter insolent speech,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">shall all evildoers vaunt themselves?</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They crush Your people, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they afflict Your very own;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they kill the widow and the stranger;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they murder the fatherless,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">thinking, “Yah<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>Yah </b>See note at <a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 68:5" href="Psalms.68.5">68.5</a>.</i> does not see it,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the God of Jacob does not pay heed.”</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Take heed, you most brutish people;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">fools, when will you get wisdom?</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Shall the One who implants the ear not hear,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the One who forms the eye not see?</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Shall the One who disciplines nations not punish,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the One who instructs humankind in knowledge?</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">
G<small>OD</small>
 knows human designs to be futile.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Happy are those<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>are those </b>Or “is the virile man.”</i> whom You discipline, O Yah,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">whom You instruct in Your teaching,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">whom You give tranquility in times of misfortune,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">until a pit be dug for the wicked.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For G<small>OD</small> will not forsake this people;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">God’s very own will not be abandoned.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Judgment shall again accord with justice</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and all the upright shall rally to it.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Who will take my part against evildoers?</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Who will stand up for me against wrongdoers?</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Were not G<small>OD</small> my help,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I should soon dwell in silence.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">When I think my foot has given way,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Your faithfulness, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, supports me.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">When I am filled with cares,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Your assurance soothes my soul.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Shall the seat of injustice be Your partner,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">that frames mischief by statute?</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They band together to do away with the righteous;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they condemn the innocent to death.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">But G<small>OD</small> is my haven;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my God is my sheltering rock.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Their evil will be made to recoil upon them,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">through their own wickedness they will be annihilated;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble"> the E<small>TERNAL</small> our God will annihilate them.</span>

Chapter 95

<span class="poetry indentAll">Come, let us sing joyously to G<small>OD</small>,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">raise a shout for our rock and deliverer;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">let us come into the divine presence with praise;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">let us shout out in song!</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For the E<small>TERNAL</small> is a great God,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the great ruler of all divine beings.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">In God’s hand are the depths of the earth;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the peaks of the mountains are God’s.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">The sea is God’s—the One who made it;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and the land, fashioned by God’s hands.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Come, let us bow down and kneel,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">bend the knee before the E<small>TERNAL</small> our maker,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for this One is our God,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and we are the people being cared for—the tended flock.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">O, if you would but heed God’s charge this day:</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Do not be stubborn as at Meribah,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">as on the day of Massah, in the wilderness,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">when your ancestors put Me to the test,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">tried Me, though they had seen My deeds.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Forty years I was provoked by that generation;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I thought, “They are a senseless people;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they would not know My ways.”</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Concerning them I swore in anger,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">“They shall never come to My resting-place!”</span>

Chapter 96

<span class="poetry indentAll"><sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote">Cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="I Chronicles 16:23-33" href="I_Chronicles.16.23-33">1 Chron. 16.23–33</a>.</i> Sing to G<small>OD</small> a new song,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">sing to G<small>OD</small>, all the earth.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Sing to G<small>OD</small>, bless this name,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">proclaim God’s victory day after day.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Tell of this glory among the nations,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">God’s wondrous deeds, among all peoples.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For G<small>OD</small> is great and much acclaimed,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and is held in awe by all divine beings.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">All the gods of the peoples are mere idols,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">but the E<small>TERNAL</small> made the heavens.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Glory and majesty are present;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">strength and splendor are in the holy temple.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Ascribe to G<small>OD</small>, O families of the peoples,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">ascribe to G<small>OD</small> glory and strength.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Ascribe to G<small>OD</small> the glory of this name,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">bring tribute and enter the temple’s<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>the temple’s </b>Heb. “its.”</i> courts.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Bow down to G<small>OD</small>, majestic in holiness;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">tremble in the divine presence, all the earth!</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Declare among the nations, “G<small>OD</small> is sovereign!”</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">The world stands firm; it cannot be shaken;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the peoples will be judged with equity.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Let the heavens rejoice and the earth exult;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">let the sea and all within it thunder,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the fields and everything in them exult;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">then shall all the trees of the forest shout for joy</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">at the presence of G<small>OD</small>, who is coming,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">coming to rule the earth—</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">to rule the world justly,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and its peoples in faithfulness.</span>

Chapter 97

<span class="poetry indentAll">
G<small>OD</small>
 is sovereign!</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Let the earth exult,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the many islands rejoice!</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Surrounded by dense clouds—</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">righteousness and justice are the base of the heavenly throne.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Fire is the vanguard,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">burning up foes on every side.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">God’s lightnings light up the world;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the earth is convulsed at the sight;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">mountains melt like wax at G<small>OD</small>’s presence,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">at the presence of the Sovereign of all the earth.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">The heavens proclaim God’s righteousness</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and all peoples see God’s glory.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">All who worship images,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who vaunt their idols,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">are dismayed;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">all divine beings bow down in homage.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Zion, hearing it, rejoices,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the towns<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>towns </b>Or “women.”</i> of Judah exult,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">because of Your judgments, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For You, E<small>TERNAL</small> One, are supreme over all the earth;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You are exalted high above all divine beings.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">O you who love G<small>OD</small>, hate evil!</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">For the lives of the loyal are guarded;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they are saved from the hand of the wicked.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Light is sown for the righteous,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">radiance<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>radiance </b>In contrast to others “joy.”</i> for the upright.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">O you righteous, rejoice in G<small>OD</small> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and acclaim God’s holy name!</span>

Chapter 98

A psalm.<br><span class="poetry indentAll">Sing to G<small>OD</small> a new song,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who has worked wonders—</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who with right hand, and holy arm,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">has won victory.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">
G<small>OD</small>
 has manifested victory,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and displayed triumph in the sight of the nations—</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">mindful of God’s steadfast love and faithfulness toward the house of Israel.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">All the ends of the earth beheld the victory of our God.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Raise a shout to G<small>OD</small>, all the earth,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">break into joyous songs of praise!</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Sing praise to G<small>OD</small> with the lyre,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">with the lyre and melodious song.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">With trumpets and the blast of the horn</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">raise a shout before G<small>OD</small>, the King.<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>King </b>I.e., the One who leads the celestial army to victory.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Let the sea and all within it thunder,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the world and its inhabitants;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">let the rivers clap their hands,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the mountains sing joyously together</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">at the presence of G<small>OD</small>—</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who is coming to rule the earth:</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">[God] will rule the world justly,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and its peoples with equity.</span>

<span class="poetry indentAll">

 is great in Zion,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and exalted above all peoples.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They praise Your name as great and awesome;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">[God] is holy!</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Mighty ruler<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>Mighty ruler </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> who loves justice,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">it was You who established equity,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You who worked righteous judgment in Jacob.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Exalt the E<small>TERNAL</small> our God</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and bow down to the divine footstool;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">[God] is holy!</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Moses and Aaron among God’s priests,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Samuel, among those who call on the divine name—</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">when they called to G<small>OD</small>,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they were answered.</span>

Chapter 100

A psalm for praise.<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>for praise </b>Traditionally “for the thanksgiving offering.”</i> <br><span class="poetry indentAll">Raise a shout for G<small>OD</small>, all the earth;</span>
