Chapter 101

Of David. A psalm.<br><span class="poetry indentAll">I will sing of faithfulness and justice;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I will chant a hymn to You, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I will study the way of the blameless;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">when shall I attain it?</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">I will live without blame within my house.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I will not set before my eyes anything base;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I hate crooked dealing;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I will have none of it.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Perverse thoughts will be far from me;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I will know nothing of evil.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">One who slanders a friend in secret I will destroy;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I cannot endure anyone haughty and proud.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">My eyes are on the trustworthy ones of the land,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">to have them at my side.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">One who follows the way of the blameless</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">shall be in my service.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">One who deals deceitfully</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">shall not live in my house;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">one who speaks untruth</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">shall not stand before my eyes.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Each morning I will destroy</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">all the wicked of the land,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">to rid G<small>OD</small>’s city</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">of all evildoers.</span>

Chapter 102

A prayer of one who is lowly and faint, pouring forth a plea before G<small>OD</small>.
<span class="poetry indentAll">O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, hear my prayer;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">let my cry come before You.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Do not hide Your face from me</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">in my time of trouble;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">turn Your ear to me;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">when I cry, answer me speedily.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For my days have vanished like smoke</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and my bones are charred like a hearth.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">My body is stricken and withered like grass;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">too wasted<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>too wasted </b>In contrast to others “I forget.”</i> to eat my food;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">on account of my vehement groaning</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my bones show through my skin.<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>show through my skin </b>Lit. “cling to my flesh.”</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I am like a great owl in the wilderness,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">an owl among the ruins.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I lie awake; I am like</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">a lone bird upon a roof.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">All day long my enemies revile me;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my deriders use my name to curse.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For I have eaten ashes like bread</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and mixed my drink with tears,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">because of Your wrath and Your fury;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for You have cast me far away.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">My days are like a lengthening shadow;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I wither like grass.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">But You, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, are enthroned forever;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Your fame endures throughout the ages.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You will surely arise and take pity on Zion,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for it is time to be gracious to her;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the appointed time has come.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Your servants take delight in its stones,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and cherish its dust.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">The nations will fear the name of G<small>OD</small>,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">all the kings of the earth, Your glory.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For G<small>OD</small> has built Zion,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">appearing in divine glory—</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">turning to the prayer of the destitute<sup class="footnote-marker">c</sup><i class="footnote"><b>of the destitute </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and not spurning their prayer.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">May this be written down for a coming generation,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">that people yet to be created may praise Yah.<sup class="footnote-marker">d</sup><i class="footnote"><b>Yah </b>See note at <a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 68:5" href="Psalms.68.5">68.5</a>.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Looking down from the holy heights,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble"> 
G<small>OD</small>
 beholds the earth from heaven</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">to hear the groans of the prisoner,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">to release those condemned to death;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">that G<small>OD</small>’s fame may be recounted in Zion,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">with praises offered in Jerusalem,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">when the nations gather together,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the kingdoms, to serve G<small>OD</small>.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">My strength was drained in mid-course,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my days shortened.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I say, “O my God, do not take me away</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">in the midst of my days,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You whose years go on for generations on end.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Of old You established the earth;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the heavens are the work of Your hands.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They shall perish, but You shall endure;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they shall all wear out like a garment;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You change them like clothing and they pass away.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">But You are the same, and Your years never end.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">May the children of Your servants dwell securely</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and their offspring endure in Your presence.”</span>

Chapter 103

Of David.<br><span class="poetry indentAll">Bless G<small>OD</small>, O my soul,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">all my being, that holy name.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Bless the E<small>TERNAL</small> One, O my soul,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and do not forget all God’s bounties.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">All your sins are forgiven,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">all your diseases healed.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Your life is redeemed from the Pit,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">you are surrounded with steadfast love and mercy.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You are satisfied with good things in the prime of life,<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>the prime of life </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">so that your youth is renewed like the eagle’s.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">
G<small>OD</small>
 executes righteous acts</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and judgments for all who are wronged—</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">making known to Moses the divine ways,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and to the children of Israel, holy deeds.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">
G<small>OD</small>
 is compassionate and gracious,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">slow to anger, abounding in steadfast love.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">[God] will not contend forever,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">or nurse anger for all time.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">[God] has not dealt with us according to our sins,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">nor requited us according to our iniquities.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For as the heavens are high above the earth,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">so great is divine steadfast love toward those who show reverence.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">As east is far from west,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">so far have our sins been removed from us.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">As a father has compassion for his children,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">so G<small>OD</small> has compassion for those who show reverence.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For [God] knows how we are formed,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and is mindful that we are dust.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Mortals, their days are like those of grass;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they bloom like a flower of the field;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">a wind passes by and it is no more,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">its own place no longer knows it.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">But G<small>OD</small>’s steadfast love is for all eternity</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">toward those who show reverence,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and God’s beneficence is for the children’s children</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">of those who keep the covenant</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and remember to observe the divine precepts.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">
G<small>OD</small>
 has established the heavenly throne,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">with a sovereign rule over all.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Bless the E<small>TERNAL</small> One, O angels,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">mighty creatures who do God’s bidding,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">ever obedient to that bidding;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">bless the E<small>TERNAL</small> One, all you<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>you </b>Heb. “His.”</i> hosts,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">you<sup class="footnote-marker">c</sup><i class="footnote"><b>you </b>See preceding note.</i> servants who do God’s will;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">bless the E<small>TERNAL</small> One, all God’s works,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">through the length and breadth of God’s realm;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">bless the E<small>TERNAL</small> One, O my soul.</span>

Chapter 104

<span class="poetry indentAll">Bless the E<small>TERNAL</small> One, O my soul;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, my God, You are very great;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You are clothed in glory and majesty,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">wrapped in a robe of light;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You spread the heavens like a tent cloth.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>You </b>Heb. 3rd person; so also in vv. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 104:4" href="Psalms.104.4">4</a> and <a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 104:5" href="Psalms.104.5">5</a>.</i> set the rafters of the heavenly lofts in the waters—</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">making the clouds a chariot,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">moving on the wings of the wind.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You make messengers of the winds,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">servants of fiery flames.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You established the earth on its foundations,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">so that it shall never totter.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You made the deep cover it as a garment;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the waters stood above the mountains.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They fled at Your blast,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">rushed away at the sound of Your thunder—</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">mountains rising, valleys sinking—</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">to the place You established for them.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You set bounds they must not pass</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">so that they never again cover the earth.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You make springs gush forth in torrents;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they make their way between the hills,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">giving drink to all the wild beasts;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the wild asses slake their thirst.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">The birds of the sky dwell beside them</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and sing among the foliage.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You water the mountains from Your<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>Your </b>Heb. 3rd person.</i> lofts;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the earth is sated from the fruit of Your work.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You make the grass grow for the cattle,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and herbage for humans’ labor</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">that they may get food out of the earth—</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">wine that cheers human hearts,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">oil that makes the face shine,<sup class="footnote-marker">c</sup><i class="footnote"><b>oil that makes the face shine </b>Lit. “to make the face shine from oil.”</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and bread that sustains human life.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">The trees of the E<small>TERNAL</small> drink their fill,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the cedars of Lebanon, God’s own planting,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">where birds make their nests;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the stork has her home in the junipers.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">The high mountains are for wild goats;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the crags are a refuge for rock-badgers.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">[God] made the moon to mark the seasons;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the sun knows when to set.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You bring on darkness and it is night,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">when all the beasts of the forests stir.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">The lions roar for prey,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">seeking their food from God.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">When the sun rises, they come home</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and couch in their dens.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">People then go out to their work,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">to their labor until the evening.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">How many are the things You have made, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You have made them all with wisdom;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the earth is full of Your creations.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">There is the sea, vast and wide,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">with its creatures beyond number,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">living things, small and great.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">There go the ships,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and Leviathan that You formed to sport with.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">All of them look to You</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">to give them their food when it is due.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Give it to them, they gather it up;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">open Your hand, they are well satisfied;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">hide Your face, they are terrified;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">take away their breath, they perish</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and turn again into dust;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">send back Your breath, they are created,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and You renew the face of the earth.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">May G<small>OD</small>’s glory endure forever;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">may G<small>OD</small> rejoice in these works!</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">—The One who looks at the earth and it trembles,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">touches the mountains and they smoke.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I will sing to the E<small>TERNAL</small> as long as I live;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">all my life I will chant hymns to my God.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">May my prayer be found pleasing;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I will rejoice in G<small>OD</small>.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">May sinners disappear from the earth,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and the wicked be no more.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Bless Yah,<sup class="footnote-marker">d</sup><i class="footnote"><b>Yah </b>See note at <a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 68:5" href="Psalms.68.5">68.5</a>.</i> O my soul.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Hallelujah.</span>

Chapter 105

<span class="poetry indentAll">Praise G<small>OD</small>;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">call on this name;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">proclaim God’s deeds among the peoples.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Sing out praises;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">speak of all those wondrous acts.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Exult in the holy name;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">let all who seek G<small>OD</small> rejoice.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Turn to G<small>OD</small>, to divine might;<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>divine might </b>I.e., the Ark; cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 78:61" href="Psalms.78.61">Ps. 78.61</a>; <a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 132:8" href="Psalms.132.8">132.8</a>.</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">seek God’s presence constantly.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Remember the wonders that have been done,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the portents, and judgments pronounced,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">O offspring of Abraham, God’s servant,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">O descendants of Jacob, the chosen ones.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">The E<small>TERNAL</small> is our God,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">whose judgments are throughout the earth.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">[God] is ever mindful of the covenant,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the promise given for a thousand generations,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">that was made with Abraham,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">sworn to Isaac,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and confirmed in a decree for Jacob,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for Israel, as an eternal covenant,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">saying, “To you I will give the land of Canaan</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">as your allotted heritage.”</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They were then few in number,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">a mere handful, sojourning there,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">wandering from nation to nation,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">from one kingdom to another.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">None were allowed to oppress them;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">kings were reproved on their account,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">“Do not touch My anointed ones;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">do not harm My prophets.”</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">A famine was called down on the land,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">destroying every staff of bread.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">[God] sent ahead of them an agent—</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Joseph, sold into slavery.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">His feet were subjected to fetters;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">an iron collar was put on his neck.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Until his prediction came true</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble"> 
G<small>OD</small>’s decree purged him.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">The king sent to have him freed;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the ruler of nations released him.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">He made him the lord of his household,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">empowered him over all his possessions,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">to discipline his princes at will,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">to teach his elders wisdom.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Then Israel came to Egypt;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Jacob sojourned in the land of Ham.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">[God] made that people very fruitful,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">more numerous than their foes,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">then changed the heart<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>changed the heart </b>Or “Their heart changed.”</i> [of the Egyptians] to hate this people,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">to plot against God’s servants.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Moses—God’s servant—was sent,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and Aaron, who had been chosen.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They performed God’s signs among them,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and wonders, against the land of Ham.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">[God] sent darkness; it was very dark;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">did they not defy God’s word?<sup class="footnote-marker">c</sup><i class="footnote"><b>did they not defy God’s word </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Their waters were turned into blood</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and their fish were killed.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Their land teemed with frogs,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">even the rooms of their king.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Swarms of insects came at God’s command,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">lice, throughout their country.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They were given hail for rain,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and flaming fire in their land.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Their vines and fig trees were struck,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the trees of their country broken down.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Locusts came at God’s command,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">grasshoppers without number.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They devoured every green thing in the land;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they consumed the produce of the soil.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">[God] struck down every [male] first-born in the land,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the first fruit of their vigor.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Israel<sup class="footnote-marker">d</sup><i class="footnote"><b>Israel </b>Heb. “them.”</i> was led out with silver and gold;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">none among their tribes faltered.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Egypt rejoiced when they left,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for dread of Israel<sup class="footnote-marker">e</sup><i class="footnote"><b>Israel </b>Heb. “them.”</i> had fallen upon them.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">[God] spread a cloud for a cover,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and fire to light up the night.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They asked, and were brought quail,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and were satisfied with food from heaven.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">[God] opened a rock so that water gushed forth;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">it flowed as a stream in the parched land.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Mindful of the sacred promise</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">to Abraham—God’s servant,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">The people were led out in gladness,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">God’s chosen ones with joyous song.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They were given the lands of nations;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they inherited the wealth of peoples,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">that they might keep God’s laws</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and observe God’s teachings.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Hallelujah.</span>

Chapter 106

<span class="poetry indentAll">Hallelujah.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Praise G<small>OD</small>, who is good—</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">whose steadfast love is eternal.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Who can tell G<small>OD</small>’s mighty acts,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">proclaim all due praises?</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Happy are those who act justly,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who do right at all times.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Be mindful of me, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, when You favor Your people;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">take note of me when You deliver them,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">that I may enjoy the prosperity of Your chosen ones,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">share the joy of Your nation,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">glory in Your very own people.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">We have sinned like our ancestors;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">we have gone astray, done evil.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Our ancestors in Egypt did not perceive Your wonders;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they did not remember Your abundant love,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">but rebelled at the sea, at the Sea of Reeds.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Yet they were saved, as befits God’s name,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">to make known God’s might.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">A blast was sent against the Sea of Reeds;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">it became dry;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they were led through the deep as through a wilderness.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They were delivered from the foe,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">redeemed from the enemy.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Water covered their adversaries;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">not one of them was left.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Then they believed God’s promise,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and sang God’s praises.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">But they soon forgot those deeds;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they would not wait to learn the divine plan.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They were seized with craving in the wilderness,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and put God to the test in the wasteland.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They were given what they asked for,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">then made to waste away.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">There was envy of Moses in the camp,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and of Aaron, G<small>OD</small>’s holy one.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">The earth opened up and swallowed Dathan,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">closed over the party of Abiram.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">A fire blazed among their party,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">a flame that consumed the wicked.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They made a calf at Horeb</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and bowed down to a molten image.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They exchanged their glory</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for the image of a bull that feeds on grass.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They forgot God who saved them,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who performed great deeds in Egypt,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">wondrous deeds in the land of Ham,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">awesome deeds at the Sea of Reeds.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They would have been destroyed</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">had not Moses, God’s chosen one,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">stood in the breach</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">to avert God’s destructive wrath.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They rejected the desirable land,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and put no faith in the divine promise.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They grumbled in their tents</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and disobeyed G<small>OD</small>.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">So a divine hand was raised in oath</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">to make them fall in the wilderness,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">to disperse<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>disperse </b>Cf. Targum, Kimhi.</i> their offspring among the nations</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and scatter them through the lands.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They attached themselves to Baal Peor,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">ate sacrifices offered to the dead.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They provoked anger by their deeds,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and a plague broke out among them.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Phinehas stepped forth and intervened,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and the plague ceased.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">It was reckoned to his merit</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for all generations, to eternity.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They provoked wrath at the waters of Meribah</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and Moses suffered on their account,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">because they rebelled against [God]</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and he spoke rashly.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They did not destroy the nations</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">as G<small>OD</small> had commanded them,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">but mingled with the nations</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and learned their ways.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They worshiped their idols,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">which became a snare for them.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Their own sons and daughters</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they sacrificed to demons.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They shed innocent blood,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the blood of their sons and daughters,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">whom they sacrificed to the idols of Canaan;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">so the land was polluted with bloodguilt.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Thus they became defiled by their acts,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">debauched through their deeds.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">
G<small>OD</small>
 was angry with this people</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and abhorred them as an inheritance.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They were handed over to the nations;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">their foes ruled them.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Their enemies oppressed them</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and they were subject to their power.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They were saved time and again,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">but they were deliberately rebellious,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and so they were brought low by their iniquity.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Upon seeing that they were in distress,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and hearing their cry,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">[God] was mindful of the covenant</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and in great faithfulness relented.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Their captors were made to be kindly disposed toward them.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Deliver us, our E<small>TERNAL</small> God,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and gather us from among the nations,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">to acclaim Your holy name,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">to glory in Your praise.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Blessed is the E<small>TERNAL</small>, God of Israel,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">From eternity to eternity.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Let all the people say, “Amen.”</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Hallelujah.</span>

Chapter 107

<span class="poetry indentAll">“Praise G<small>OD</small>, who is good—</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">whose steadfast love is eternal!”</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Thus let G<small>OD</small>’s redeemed say,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">those redeemed from adversity,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who have been gathered in from the lands,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">from east and west,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">from the north and from the sea.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Some lost their way in the wilderness,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">in the wasteland;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they found no settled place.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Hungry and thirsty,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">their spirit failed.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">In their adversity they cried to G<small>OD</small>,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and they were rescued from their troubles.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They were shown a direct way</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">to reach a settled place.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Let them give praise for G<small>OD</small>’s steadfast love</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and wondrous deeds for humankind—</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for satisfying the thirsty,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and filling the hungry with all good things.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Some lived in deepest darkness,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">bound in cruel irons,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">because they defied the word of God,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">spurned the counsel of the Most High.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Their hearts were humbled through suffering;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they stumbled with no one to help.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">In their adversity they cried to G<small>OD</small>,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and were rescued from their troubles.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They were brought out of deepest darkness,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">their bonds broken asunder.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Let them give praise for G<small>OD</small>’s steadfast love</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and wondrous deeds for humankind—</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">shattering gates of bronze,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">breaking their iron bars.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">There were fools who suffered for their sinful way,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and for their iniquities.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">All food was loathsome to them;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they reached the gates of death.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">In their adversity they cried to G<small>OD</small> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and they were saved from their troubles.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">[God] gave an order and healed them—</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">delivering them from the pits.<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>the pits </b>Of death.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Let them give praise for G<small>OD</small>’s steadfast love</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and wondrous deeds for humankind.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Let them offer thanksgiving sacrifices,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and tell those deeds in joyful song.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Others go down to the sea in ships,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">ply their trade in the mighty waters;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they have seen G<small>OD</small>’s works</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and such wonders in the deep.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">God’s word raised a storm wind</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">that made the waves surge.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Mounting up to the heaven,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">plunging down to the depths,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">disgorging in their misery,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they reeled and staggered like a drunk,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">all their skill to no avail.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">In their adversity they cried to G<small>OD</small>,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and were saved from their troubles.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">The storm was reduced to a whisper;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the waves were stilled.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They rejoiced when all was quiet,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and were brought to the port they desired.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Let them give praise for G<small>OD</small>’s steadfast love,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and wondrous deeds for humankind.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Let them exalt in the congregation of the people,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">acclaim in the assembly of the elders.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">The rivers are turned into a wilderness,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">springs of water into thirsty land,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">fruitful land into a salt marsh,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">because of the wickedness of its inhabitants.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">The wilderness is turned into pools,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">parched land into springs of water.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">There the hungry are settled;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they build a place to settle in.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They sow fields and plant vineyards</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">that yield a fruitful harvest.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They are blessed and they increase greatly—</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">their cattle do not decrease,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">after they had been few and crushed</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">by oppression, misery, and sorrow.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">[God] pours contempt on nobles</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and makes them lose their way in trackless deserts;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">but the needy are secured from suffering,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">their families increased like flocks.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">The upright see it and rejoice;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the mouth of all wrongdoers is stopped.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">One who is wise will take note of these things</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and consider G<small>OD</small>’s steadfast love.</span>

Chapter 108

A song. A psalm of David.
<span class="poetry indentAll"><sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote">Cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 57:8-12" href="Psalms.57.8-12">Ps. 57.8–12</a>.</i> My heart is firm, O God;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I will sing and chant a hymn with all my soul.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Awake, O harp and lyre!</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I will wake the dawn.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I will praise You among the peoples, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">sing a hymn to You among the nations;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for Your faithfulness is higher than the heavens;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Your steadfastness reaches to the sky.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Exalt Yourself over the heavens, O God;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">let Your glory be over all the earth!</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll"><sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote">Cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 60:7-14" href="Psalms.60.7-14">Ps. 60.7–14</a>.</i> That those whom You love may be rescued,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">deliver with Your right hand and answer me.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">God promised in the sanctuary<sup class="footnote-marker">c</sup><i class="footnote"><b>in the sanctuary </b>Or “by God’s holiness.”</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">that I would exultingly divide up Shechem,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and measure the Valley of Sukkoth;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Gilead and Manasseh would be mine,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Ephraim my chief stronghold,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Judah my scepter;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Moab would be my washbasin;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">on Edom I would cast my shoe;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I would raise a shout over Philistia.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Would that I were brought to the bastion!</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Would that I were led to Edom!</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">But You have rejected us, O God;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">God, You do not march with our armies.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Grant us Your aid against the foe,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for human help is worthless.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">We shall triumph with God,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who will trample our foes.</span>

Chapter 109

For the leader. Of David. A psalm.<br><span class="poetry indentAll">O God of my praise,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">do not keep aloof,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for the wicked and the deceitful</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">open their mouth against me;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they speak to me with lying tongue.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They encircle me with words of hate;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they attack me without cause.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They answer my love with accusation</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and I must stand judgment<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>and I must stand judgment </b>Or “but I am all prayer”; meaning of Heb. uncertain, but see v. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 109:7" href="Psalms.109.7">7</a>.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They repay me with evil for good,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">with hatred for my love.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Appoint someone wicked over him;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">may an accuser stand at his right side;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">may he be tried and convicted;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">may he be judged and found guilty.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">May his days be few;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">may another take over his position.<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>his position </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">May his children be orphans,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">his wife a widow.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">May his children wander from their hovels,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">begging in search of [bread].</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">May his creditor seize all his possessions;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">may strangers plunder his wealth.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">May no one show him mercy;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">may none pity his orphans;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">may his posterity be cut off;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">may their names be blotted out in the next generation.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">May God be ever mindful of his father’s iniquity,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and may the sin of his mother not be blotted out.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">May G<small>OD</small> be aware of them always</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and cause their names to be cut off from the earth,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">because he was not minded to act kindly,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and hounded to death the poor and needy man,<sup class="footnote-marker">c</sup><i class="footnote"><b>the poor and needy man </b>The psalmist himself; cf. vv. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 109:22" href="Psalms.109.22">22</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 109:31" href="Psalms.109.31">31</a>.</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">one crushed in spirit.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">He loved to curse—may a curse come upon him!</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">He would not bless—may blessing be far from him!</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">May he be clothed in a curse like a garment,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">may it enter his body like water,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">his bones like oil.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Let it be like the cloak he wraps around him,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">like the belt he always wears.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">May G<small>OD</small> thus repay my accusers,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">all those who speak evil against me.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Now You, O G<small>OD</small>, my Sovereign,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">act in my behalf as befits Your name.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Good and faithful as You are, save me.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For I am poor and needy,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and my heart is pierced within me.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I fade away like a lengthening shadow;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I am shaken off like locusts.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">My knees give way from fasting;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my flesh is lean, has lost its fat.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I am the object of their scorn;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">when they see me, they shake their head.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Help me, O my E<small>TERNAL</small> God;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">save me in accord with Your faithfulness—</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">that all may know that it is Your hand,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">that You, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, have done it.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Let them curse, but You bless;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">let them rise up, but come to grief,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">while Your servant rejoices.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">My accusers shall be clothed in shame,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">wrapped in their disgrace as in a robe.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">My mouth shall sing much praise to G<small>OD</small>;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I will acclaim in the midst of a throng,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">because [God] stands at the right hand of the needy,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">to save them from those who would condemn them.</span>

Chapter 110

Of David. A psalm.<br><span class="poetry indentAll"> 
G<small>OD</small>
 said to my lord,<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>my lord </b>I.e., the king, who leads his army on campaigns.</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">“Sit at My right hand</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">while I make your enemies your footstool.”</span>

<span class="poetry indentAll">[God] works judgment upon the nations,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">heaping up bodies,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">crushing heads far and wide.</span>

Chapter 114

<span class="poetry indentAll">When Israel went forth from Egypt,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the house of Jacob from a people of strange speech,</span>

Chapter 116

<span class="poetry indentAll">I love the E<small>TERNAL</small> One </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for hearing my voice, my pleas;<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>I love the <small>ETERNAL ONE</small> / for hearing my voice, my pleas </b>Heb. transposed for clarity; in contrast to others “I would love that the L<small>ORD</small> hear,” etc.</i> </span>

Chapter 118

<span class="poetry indentAll">Praise G<small>OD</small>, who is good—</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">whose steadfast love is eternal.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Let Israel declare,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">“God’s steadfast love is eternal.”</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Let the house of Aaron declare,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">“God’s steadfast love is eternal.”</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Let those who fear G<small>OD</small> declare,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">“God’s steadfast love is eternal.”</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">In distress I called on Yah;<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>Yah </b>See note at <a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 68:5" href="Psalms.68.5">68.5</a>.</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Yah answered me and brought me relief.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">
G<small>OD</small>
 is on my side,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I have no fear;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">what can mortals do to me?</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">With G<small>OD</small> on my side as my helper,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I will see the downfall of my foes.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">It is better to take refuge in G<small>OD</small> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">than to trust in mortals;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">it is better to take refuge in G<small>OD</small> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">than to trust in the great.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">All nations have beset me;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">by G<small>OD</small>’s name I will surely cut them down.<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>cut them down </b>Meaning of <i>ʼamilam</i> in this and the following two verses uncertain.</i> </span>

<span class="poetry indentAll">You<sup class="footnote-marker">c</sup><i class="footnote"><b>You </b>I.e., the enemy.</i> pressed me hard,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I nearly fell;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">but G<small>OD</small> helped me.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Yah is my strength and might,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and has become my deliverance.</span>

G<small>OD</small>’s right hand is triumphant!”</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I shall not die but live</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and proclaim the works of Yah.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Yah punished me severely,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">but did not hand me over to death.</span>

<span class="poetry indentAll">I praise You, for You have answered me,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and have become my deliverance.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">The stone that the builders rejected</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">has become the chief cornerstone.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">This is G<small>OD</small>’s doing;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">it is marvelous in our sight.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">This is the day that G<small>OD</small> has made—</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">let us exult and rejoice on it.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, deliver us!</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, let us prosper!</span>

<span class="poetry indentAll">The E<small>TERNAL</small> is God,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who has given us light;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">bind the festal offering to the horns of the altar with cords.<sup class="footnote-marker">g</sup><i class="footnote"><b>bind … with cords </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span>

Chapter 119

<span class="poetry indentAll"><b>א</b> Happy are those whose way is blameless,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who follow G<small>OD</small>’s teaching.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Happy are those who observe God’s decrees,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who turn to the divine wholeheartedly.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They have done no wrong,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">but have followed God’s ways.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You have commanded that Your precepts</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">be kept diligently.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Would that my ways were firm</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">in keeping Your laws;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">then I would not be ashamed</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">when I regard all Your commandments.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I will praise You with a sincere heart</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">as I learn Your just rules.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I will keep Your laws;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">do not utterly forsake me.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll"> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll"><b>ב</b> How can youths keep their way pure?—</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">by holding to Your word.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I have turned to You with all my heart;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">do not let me stray from Your commandments.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">In my heart I treasure Your promise;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">therefore I do not sin against You.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Blessed are You, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">train me in Your laws.</span>

<span class="poetry indentAll">I am only a sojourner in the land;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">do not hide Your commandments from me.</span>

<span class="poetry indentAll">Your word is exceedingly pure,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and Your servant loves it.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Though I am belittled and despised,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I have not neglected Your precepts.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Your righteousness is eternal;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Your teaching is true.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Though anguish and distress come upon me,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Your commandments are my delight.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Your righteous decrees are eternal;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">give me understanding, that I might live.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll"> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll"><b>ק</b> I call with all my heart;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">answer me, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">that I may observe Your laws.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I call upon You; save me,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">that I may keep Your decrees.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I rise before dawn and cry for help;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I hope for Your word.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">My eyes greet each watch of the night,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">as I meditate on Your promise.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Hear my voice as befits Your steadfast love;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, preserve me, as is Your rule.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Those who pursue intrigue draw near;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they are far from Your teaching.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, are near,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and all Your commandments are true.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I know from Your decrees of old</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">that You have established them forever.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll"> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll"><b>ר</b> See my affliction and rescue me,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for I have not neglected Your teaching.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Champion my cause and redeem me;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">preserve me according to Your promise.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Deliverance is far from the wicked,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for they have not turned to Your laws.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Your mercies are great, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">as is Your rule, preserve me.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Many are my persecutors and foes;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I have not swerved from Your decrees.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I have seen traitors and loathed<sup class="footnote-marker">f</sup><i class="footnote"><b>loathed </b>Or “have contended with.”</i> them,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">because they did not keep Your word in mind.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">See that I have loved Your precepts;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, preserve me, as befits Your steadfast love.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Truth is the essence of Your word;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Your just rules are eternal.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll"> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll"><b>ש</b> Princes have persecuted me without reason;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my heart thrills at Your word.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I rejoice over Your promise</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">as one who obtains great spoil.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I hate and abhor falsehood;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I love Your teaching.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I praise You seven times each day</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for Your just rules.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Those who love Your teaching enjoy well-being;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they encounter no adversity.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I hope for Your deliverance, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I observe Your commandments.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I obey Your decrees</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and love them greatly.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I obey Your precepts and decrees;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">all my ways are before You.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll"> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll"><b>ת</b> May my plea reach You, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">grant me understanding according to Your word.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">May my petition come before You;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">save me in accordance with Your promise.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">My lips shall pour forth praise,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for You teach me Your laws.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">My tongue shall declare Your promise,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for all Your commandments are just.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Lend Your hand to help me,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for I have chosen Your precepts.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I have longed for Your deliverance, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Your teaching is my delight.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Let me live, that I may praise You;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">may Your rules be my help;</span>
