Chapter 134

A song of ascents.<br><span class="poetry indentAll">Now bless G<small>OD</small>,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">all you servants of G<small>OD</small> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who stand nightly</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">in G<small>OD</small>’s house.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Lift your hands toward the sanctuary</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and bless G<small>OD</small>.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">May G<small>OD</small>,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">maker of heaven and earth,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">bless you from Zion.</span>

Chapter 135

<span class="poetry indentAll">Hallelujah.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Praise the name of G<small>OD</small>;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">give praise, you servants of G<small>OD</small> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who stand in the house of G<small>OD</small>,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">in the courts of the house of our God.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Praise Yah,<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>Yah </b>See note at <a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 68:5" href="Psalms.68.5">68.5</a>.</i> for G<small>OD</small> is good;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">sing hymns to this name, for it is pleasant.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For Yah has chosen to keep Jacob close,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">[treating] Israel as a treasured possession.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For I know that G<small>OD</small> is great,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">that our Sovereign is greater than all gods.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Whatever G<small>OD</small> desires is done</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">in heaven and earth,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">in the seas and all the depths.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">This is who makes clouds rise from the end of the earth;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who makes lightning for the rain;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who releases the wind from divine vaults.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">[God] struck down the first-born of Egypt,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">human and animal alike—</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">sending signs and portents against<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>against </b>In contrast to others “against you.”</i> Egypt,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">against Pharaoh and all his servants,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">striking down many nations</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and slaying numerous kings—</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Sihon, king of the Amorites,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Og, king of Bashan,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and all the royalty of Canaan—</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and giving their lands as a heritage,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">as a heritage to Israel—God’s people.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, Your name endures forever,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Your fame, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, through all generations;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for G<small>OD</small> will champion this people,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and obtain satisfaction for their service.<sup class="footnote-marker">c</sup><i class="footnote"><b>their service </b>Lit. “His servants.”</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll"><sup class="footnote-marker">d</sup><i class="footnote">Cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 115:4-11" href="Psalms.115.4-11">Ps. 115.4–11</a>.</i> The idols of the nations are silver and gold,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the work of human hands.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They have mouths, but cannot speak;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they have eyes, but cannot see;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they have ears, but cannot hear,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">nor is there breath in their mouths.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Those who fashion them,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">all who trust in them,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">shall become like them.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">O house of Israel, bless G<small>OD</small>;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">O house of Aaron, bless G<small>OD</small>;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">O house of Levi, bless G<small>OD</small>;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">you who fear G<small>OD</small>, bless G<small>OD</small>.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Blessed is G<small>OD</small> from Zion,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the One who dwells in Jerusalem.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Hallelujah.</span>

Chapter 136

<span class="poetry indentAll">Praise G<small>OD</small>, who is good,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">—whose steadfast love is eternal.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Praise the God of gods,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">—whose steadfast love is eternal.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Praise the Sovereign of sovereigns,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">—whose steadfast love is eternal;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Who alone works great marvels,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">—whose steadfast love is eternal;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Who made the heavens with wisdom,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">—whose steadfast love is eternal;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Who spread the earth over the water,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">—whose steadfast love is eternal;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Who made the great lights,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">—whose steadfast love is eternal;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">the sun to dominate the day,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">—whose steadfast love is eternal;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">the moon and the stars to dominate the night,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">—whose steadfast love is eternal;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Who struck Egypt through their first-born,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">—whose steadfast love is eternal;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">and brought Israel out of their midst,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">—whose steadfast love is eternal;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">with a strong hand and outstretched arm,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">—whose steadfast love is eternal;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Who split apart the Sea of Reeds,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">—whose steadfast love is eternal;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">and made Israel pass through it,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">—whose steadfast love is eternal;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Who hurled Pharaoh and his army into the Sea of Reeds,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">—whose steadfast love is eternal;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Who led this people through the wilderness,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">—whose steadfast love is eternal;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Who struck down great kings,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">—whose steadfast love is eternal;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">and slew mighty kings,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">—whose steadfast love is eternal;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Sihon, king of the Amorites,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">—whose steadfast love is eternal;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Og, king of Bashan,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">—whose steadfast love is eternal;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">and gave their land as a heritage,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">—whose steadfast love is eternal;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">a heritage to Israel—God’s servant,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">—whose steadfast love is eternal;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Who took note of us in our degradation,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">—whose steadfast love is eternal;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">and rescued us from our enemies,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">—whose steadfast love is eternal;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Who gives food to all flesh,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">—whose steadfast love is eternal.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Praise the God of heaven,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">—whose steadfast love is eternal.</span>

Chapter 137

<span class="poetry indentAll">By the rivers of Babylon,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">there we sat,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">sat and wept,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">as we thought of Zion.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">There on the poplars</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">we hung up our lyres,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for our captors asked us there for songs,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">our tormentors,<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>tormentors </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> for amusement:</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">“Sing us one of the songs of Zion.”</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">How can we sing a song of G<small>OD</small> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">on alien soil?</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">If I forget you, O Jerusalem,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">let my right hand wither;<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>wither </b>In contrast to others “forget its cunning.”</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">let my tongue stick to my palate</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">if I cease to think of you,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">if I do not keep Jerusalem in memory</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">even at my happiest hour.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Remember, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, against the Edomites</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the day of Jerusalem’s fall;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">how they cried, “Strip her, strip her</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">to her very foundations!”</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Fair Babylon, you predator,<sup class="footnote-marker">c</sup><i class="footnote"><b>predator </b>With Targum; in contrast to others “who are to be destroyed.”</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">a blessing on the one who repays you in kind</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">what you have inflicted on us;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">a blessing on the one who seizes your babies</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and dashes them against the rocks!</span>

Chapter 138

Of David.<br><span class="poetry indentAll">I praise You with all my heart,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">sing a hymn to You before the divine beings;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I bow toward Your holy temple</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and praise Your name for Your steadfast love and faithfulness,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">because You have exalted Your name, Your word, above all.<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>Your name, Your word, above all </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">When I called, You answered me,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You inspired me with courage.<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>You inspired me with courage </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">All the kings of the earth shall praise You, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for they have heard the words You spoke.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They shall sing of G<small>OD</small>’s ways,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">“Great is G<small>OD</small>’s majesty!”</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">From way up high G<small>OD</small> sees the lowly;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">aloft, yet perceiving from afar.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Though I walk among enemies,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You preserve me in the face of my foes;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You extend Your hand;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">with Your right hand You deliver me.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">
G<small>OD</small>
 will settle accounts for me.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, Your steadfast love is eternal;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">do not forsake the work of Your hands.</span>

Chapter 139

For the leader. Of David. A psalm.<br><span class="poetry indentAll">O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, You have examined me and know me.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">When I sit down or stand up You know it;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You discern my thoughts from afar.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You observe<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>You observe </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> my walking and reclining,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and are familiar with all my ways.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">There is not a word on my tongue</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">but that You, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, know it well.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">You hedge me before and behind;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You lay Your hand upon me.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">It is beyond my knowledge;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">it is a mystery; I cannot fathom it.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Where can I escape from Your spirit?</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Where can I flee from Your presence?</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">If I ascend to heaven, You are there;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">if I descend to Sheol, You are there too.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">If I take wing with the dawn</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">to come to rest on the western horizon,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">even there Your hand will be guiding me,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Your right hand will be holding me fast.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">If I say, “Surely darkness will conceal me,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">night will provide me with cover,”<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>will conceal me, / night will provide me with cover </b>Cf. Rashi, Ibn Ezra; meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">darkness is not dark for You;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">night is as light as day;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">darkness and light are the same.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">It was You who created my conscience;<sup class="footnote-marker">c</sup><i class="footnote"><b>conscience </b>Lit. “kidneys.”</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You fashioned me in my mother’s womb.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I praise You,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for I am awesomely, wondrously made;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Your work is wonderful;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I know it very well.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">My frame was not concealed from You</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">when I was shaped in a hidden place,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">knit together in the recesses of the earth.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Your eyes saw my unformed limbs;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they were all recorded in Your book;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">in due time they were formed,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">to the very last one of them.<sup class="footnote-marker">d</sup><i class="footnote"><b>to the very last one of them </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">How weighty Your thoughts seem to me, O God,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">how great their number!</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I count them—they exceed the grains of sand;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I end—but am still with You.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">O God, if You would only slay the wicked—</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">you murderers, away from me!—</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who invoke You for intrigue,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Your enemies who swear by You falsely.<sup class="footnote-marker">e</sup><i class="footnote"><b>who invoke You … falsely </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, You know I hate those who hate You,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and loathe Your adversaries.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I feel a perfect hatred toward them;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I count them my enemies.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Examine me, O God, and know my mind;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">probe me and know my thoughts.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">See if I have vexatious ways,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and guide me in ways everlasting.</span>

Chapter 140

For the leader. A psalm of David.
<span class="poetry indentAll">Rescue me, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, from evildoers;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">save me from lawless opponents,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">whose minds are full of evil schemes,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who plot war every day.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They sharpen their tongues like serpents;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">spiders’ poison is on their lips. <i>   Selah.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, keep me out of the clutches of the wicked;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">save me from lawless opponents</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who scheme to make me fall.<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>make me fall </b>Lit. “push my feet.”</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Arrogant ones laid traps with ropes for me;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they spread out a net along the way;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they set snares for me. <i>   Selah.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I said to G<small>OD</small>: You are my God;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">give ear, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, to my pleas for mercy.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">O G<small>OD</small>, my Sovereign, the strength of my deliverance,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">You protected my head on the day of battle.<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>battle </b>Lit. “arms.”</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, do not grant the desires of the wicked;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">do not let their plan succeed,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">else they be exalted. <i>   Selah.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">May the heads of those who beset me</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">be covered with the mischief of their lips.<sup class="footnote-marker">c</sup><i class="footnote"><b>else they … lips </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">May coals of fire drop down upon them,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and they be cast into pits, never to rise again.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Let slanderers have no place in the land;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">let the evil of the lawless drive them into corrals.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I know that G<small>OD</small> will champion</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the cause of the poor, the right of the needy.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">The righteous shall surely praise Your name;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the upright shall dwell in Your presence.</span>

Chapter 141

A psalm of David.<br><span class="poetry indentAll">I call You, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, hasten to me;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">give ear to my cry when I call You.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Take my prayer as an offering of incense,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my upraised hands as an evening sacrifice.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, set a guard over my mouth,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">a watch at the door of my lips;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">let my mind not turn to an evil thing,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">to practice deeds of wickedness</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">with those evildoers;<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>those evildoers </b>Or “grandees who do evil”; force of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">let me not feast on their dainties.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll"><sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote">Meaning of verses uncertain.</i> Let someone righteous strike me in loyalty</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and reprove me;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">let my head not refuse such choice oil.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">My prayers are still against their<sup class="footnote-marker">c</sup><i class="footnote"><b>their </b>I.e., the evildoers of v. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 141:4" href="Psalms.141.4">4</a>.</i> evil deeds.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">May their judges slip on the rock,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">but let my words be heard, for they are sweet.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">As when the earth is cleft and broken up</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">our bones are scattered at the mouth of Sheol.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">My eyes are fixed upon You, O G<small>OD</small> my Sovereign;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I seek refuge in You, do not put me in jeopardy.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Keep me from the trap laid for me,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and from the snares of evildoers.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Let the wicked fall into their nets</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">while I alone come through.</span>

Chapter 142

A <i>maskil</i> of David, while he was in the cave.<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote">Cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="I Samuel 24:3-4" href="I_Samuel.24.3-4">1 Sam. 24.3–4</a>.</i> A prayer.
<span class="poetry indentAll">I cry aloud to G<small>OD</small>;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I appeal to G<small>OD</small> loudly for mercy.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I pour out my complaint directly;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I recount my tale of trouble</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">when my spirit fails within me.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">You know my course;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they have laid a trap in the path I walk.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Look at my right and see—</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I have no friend;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">there is nowhere I can flee,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">no one cares about me.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">So I cry to You, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I say, “You are my refuge,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">all I have in the land of the living.”</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Listen to my cry, for I have been brought very low;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">save me from my pursuers,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for they are too strong for me.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Free me from prison,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">that I may praise Your name.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">The righteous shall glory in me<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>shall glory in me </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for Your gracious dealings with me.</span>

Chapter 143

A psalm of David.<br><span class="poetry indentAll">O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, hear my prayer;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">give ear to my plea, as You are faithful;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">answer me, as You are beneficent.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Do not enter into judgment with Your servant,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for before You no creature is in the right.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">My foe hounded me;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">he crushed me to the ground;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">he made me dwell in darkness</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">like those long dead.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">My spirit failed within me;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my mind was numbed with horror.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Then I thought of the days of old;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">I rehearsed all Your deeds,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">recounted the work of Your hands.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I stretched out my hands to You,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">longing for You like thirsty earth. <i>   Selah.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Answer me quickly, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my spirit can endure no more.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Do not hide Your face from me,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">or I shall become like those who descend into the Pit.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Let me learn of Your faithfulness by daybreak,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for in You I trust;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">let me know the road I must take,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for on You I have set my hope.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Save me from my foes, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">to You I look for cover.<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>to You I look for cover </b>Meaning of Heb. uncertain.</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Teach me to do Your will,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for You are my God.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Let Your gracious spirit lead me</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">on level ground.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For the sake of Your name, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, preserve me;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">as You are beneficent, free me from distress.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">As You are faithful, put an end to my foes;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">destroy all my mortal enemies,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for I am Your servant.</span>

Chapter 144

Of David.<br><span class="poetry indentAll">Blessed is G<small>OD</small>, my rock,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who trains my hands for battle,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my fingers for warfare;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my faithful one, my fortress,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my haven and my deliverer,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">my shield, in whom I take shelter,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who makes peoples<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>peoples </b>So Targum, Saadia; in contrast to others “my people.”</i> subject to me.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, what are mortals that You should care about them,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">human beings, that You should think of them?</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">They are like a breath;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">their days are like a passing shadow.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">O E<small>TERNAL</small> One, bend Your sky and come down;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">touch the mountains and they will smoke.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Make lightning flash and scatter them;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">shoot Your arrows and rout them.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Reach Your hand down from on high;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">rescue me, save me from the mighty waters,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">from the hands of foreigners,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">whose mouths speak lies,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and whose oaths<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>oaths </b>With Rashi; lit. “right hand.”</i> are false.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">O God, I will sing You a new song,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">sing a hymn to You with a ten-stringed harp—</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">to the One who gives victory to kings,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who rescues David—God’s servant—from the deadly sword.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Rescue me, save me from the hands of foreigners,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">whose mouths speak lies,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and whose oaths<sup class="footnote-marker">c</sup><i class="footnote"><b>oaths </b>See note at v. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 144:8" href="Psalms.144.8">8</a>.</i> are false.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll"><sup class="footnote-marker">d</sup><i class="footnote">The meaning of several phrases in these verses is uncertain.</i> For our sons are like saplings,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">well-tended in their youth;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">our daughters are like cornerstones</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">trimmed to give shape to a palace.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Our storehouses are full,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">supplying produce of all kinds;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">our flocks number thousands,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">even myriads, in our fields;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">our cattle are well cared for.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">There is no breaching and no sortie,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and no wailing in our streets.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Happy the people who have it so;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">happy the people whose God is the E<small>TERNAL</small>.</span>

Chapter 145

A song of praise. Of David.<br><span class="poetry indentAll"> <b>א</b> I will extol You, my God and sovereign,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and bless Your name forever and ever.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll"> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll"><b>ב</b> Every day will I bless You</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and praise Your name forever and ever.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll"> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll"><b>ג</b> Great is G<small>OD</small> and much acclaimed;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">such greatness cannot be fathomed.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll"> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll"><b>ד</b> One generation shall laud Your works to another</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and declare Your mighty acts.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll"> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll"><b>ה</b> The glorious majesty of Your splendor</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and Your wondrous acts<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>splendor / and Your wondrous acts </b>A Qumran Psalms scroll reads: “splendor they will speak of / and Your wonders.”</i> will I recite.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll"> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll"><b>ו</b> All shall talk of the might of Your awesome deeds,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and I will recount Your greatness.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll"> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll"><b>ז</b> They shall celebrate Your abundant goodness,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and sing joyously of Your beneficence.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll"> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll"><b>ח</b> G<small>OD</small> is gracious and compassionate,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">slow to anger and abounding in kindness.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll"> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll"><b>ט</b> G<small>OD</small> is good to all,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and divine mercy is upon all God’s works.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll"> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll"><b>י</b> All Your works shall praise You, O E<small>TERNAL</small> One,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and Your faithful ones shall bless You.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll"> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll"><b>כ</b> They shall talk of the majesty of Your sovereignty,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and speak of Your might,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble"><b>ל</b> to make known to all humankind Your<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>Your </b>Heb. 3rd person.</i> mighty acts</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and Your<sup class="footnote-marker">c</sup><i class="footnote"><b>Your </b>See previous note.</i> sovereignty’s majestic glory.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll"> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll"><b>מ</b> Your rule is an eternal rule;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Your dominion is for all generations.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll"> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll"><b>ס</b> G<small>OD</small> supports all who stumble,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and makes all who are bent stand straight.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll"> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll"><b>ע</b> The eyes of all look to You expectantly,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and You give them their food when it is due.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll"> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll"><b>פ</b> You give it openhandedly,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">feeding every creature to its heart’s content.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll"> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll"><b>צ</b> G<small>OD</small> is beneficent in all ways</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and faithful in all works.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll"> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll"><b>ק</b> G<small>OD</small> is near to all who call,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">to all who call with sincerity.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll"> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll"><b>ר</b> Fulfilling the wishes of those who show reverence,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">[God] hears their cry and delivers them.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll"> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll"><b>ש</b> G<small>OD</small> watches over all who show their love,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">but all the wicked are destroyed.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll"> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAll"><b>ת</b> My mouth shall utter the praise of G<small>OD</small>,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">whose holy name all creatures<sup class="footnote-marker">d</sup><i class="footnote"><b>creatures </b>Lit. “flesh.”</i> shall bless forever and ever.</span>

Chapter 146

<span class="poetry indentAll">Hallelujah.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Praise G<small>OD</small>, O my soul!</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">I will praise G<small>OD</small> all my life,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">sing hymns to my God while I exist.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Put not your trust in the great,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">in mortals who cannot save.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Their breath departs;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">they return to the dust;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">on that day their plans come to nothing.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Happy are those whose help is the God of Jacob,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">whose hope is in the E<small>TERNAL</small> their God,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">maker of heaven and earth,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">the sea and all that is in them;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who keeps faith forever;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who secures justice for those who are wronged,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">gives food to the hungry.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll"> 
G<small>OD</small>
 sets prisoners free;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">
G<small>OD</small>
 restores sight to the blind;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble"> 
G<small>OD</small>
 makes those who are bent stand straight;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble"> 
G<small>OD</small>
 loves the righteous;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">
G<small>OD</small>
 watches over the stranger</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and gives courage to the orphan and widow,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">but makes the path of the wicked tortuous.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">
G<small>OD</small>
 shall reign forever,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">your God, O Zion, for all generations.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Hallelujah.</span>

Chapter 147

<span class="poetry indentAll">Hallelujah.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">It is good to chant hymns to our God;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">it is pleasant to sing glorious praise.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">
G<small>OD</small>
 rebuilds Jerusalem,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">gathering in the exiles of Israel—</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">healing their broken hearts,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and binding up their wounds.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">[God] reckoned the number of the stars</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and gave each its name.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Great and full of power is our Sovereign—</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">whose wisdom is beyond reckoning.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">
G<small>OD</small>
 gives courage to the lowly,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and brings the wicked down to the dust.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Sing to G<small>OD</small> a song of praise,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">chant a hymn with a lyre to our God,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who covers the heavens with clouds,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">provides rain for the earth,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">makes mountains put forth grass;</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who gives the beasts their food,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">to the raven’s brood what they cry for.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">[God] does not prize the strength of horses,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">nor value the warrior’s fleetness;<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>fleetness </b>Or “prowess”; lit. “thighs.”</i> </span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">but G<small>OD</small> values those who show reverence,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">those who depend on God’s faithful care.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">O Jerusalem, glorify G<small>OD</small>;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">praise your God, O Zion!</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For the bars of your gates have been made strong,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and your children have been blessed within you.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Your realm has been endowed with well-being,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and you have been satisfied with choice wheat.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">[God] sends forth words to the earth</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">with swift commands.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">[God] lays down snow like fleece,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">scatters frost like ashes.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">[God] tosses down hail like crumbs—</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who can endure such icy cold?</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">[God] issues a command—it melts them;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">breathes, and the waters flow.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Divine commands were issued to Jacob,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">God’s statutes and rules to Israel.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">This was not done for any other nation;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">of such rules they know nothing.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Hallelujah.</span>

Chapter 148

<span class="poetry indentAll">Hallelujah.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Praise G<small>OD</small> from the heavens;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">give praise on high.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Give praise, all you angels,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">give praise, all divine hosts.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Give praise, sun and moon,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">give praise, all bright stars.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Give praise, highest heavens,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and you waters that are above the heavens.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Let them praise the name of G<small>OD</small>—</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">who commanded that they be created,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">and who made them endure forever,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">establishing an order that shall never change.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Praise G<small>OD</small>, O you who are on earth,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">all sea monsters and ocean depths,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">fire and hail, snow and smoke,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">storm wind that executes God’s command,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">all mountains and hills,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">all fruit trees and cedars,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">all wild and tamed animals,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">creeping things and winged birds,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">all kings and peoples of the earth,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">all princes of the earth and its judges,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">youths and maidens alike,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">old and young together.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Let them praise G<small>OD</small>’s name—</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for sublime is this name alone—</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">of the One whose splendor covers heaven and earth.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">[God] has exalted the horn of this people</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">for the glory of all faithful ones,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Israel, the people brought close.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Hallelujah.</span>

Chapter 149

<span class="poetry indentAll">Hallelujah.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Sing to G<small>OD</small> a new song,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">sing praises in the congregation of the faithful.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Let Israel rejoice in its maker;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">let the children of Zion exult in their monarch.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Let them praise God’s name in dance;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">with hand-drum and lyre let them chant such praises.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">For G<small>OD</small> delights in this people,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and adorns the lowly with victory.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Let the faithful exult in glory;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">let them shout for joy upon their couches,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">with paeans to God in their throats</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">and two-edged swords in their hands,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">to impose retribution upon the nations,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">punishment upon the peoples,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">binding their kings with shackles,</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">their nobles with chains of iron,</span>
<span class="poetry indentAllDouble">executing the doom decreed against them.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">This is the glory of all the faithful.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Hallelujah.</span>

Chapter 150

<span class="poetry indentAll">Hallelujah.</span><br><span class="poetry indentAll">Give praise in the divine sanctuary;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">give praise in the sky, the divine stronghold.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Give praise for mighty acts;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">give praise for<sup class="footnote-marker">a</sup><i class="footnote"><b>for </b>Or “as befits.”</i> exceeding greatness.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Give praise with blasts of the horn;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">give praise with harp and lyre.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Give praise with hand-drum and dance;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">give praise with lute and pipe.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Give praise with resounding cymbals;</span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">give praise with loud-clashing cymbals.</span>
<span class="poetry indentAll">Let all that breathes praise Yah.<sup class="footnote-marker">b</sup><i class="footnote"><b>Yah </b>See note at <a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 68:5" href="Psalms.68.5">68.5</a>.</i> </span><br><span class="poetry indentAllDouble">Hallelujah.</span>
